“坚守我的立场。他们会同意的，因为这样没有伤害任何人的既得利益。埃旺热利斯塔夫人急着想把女儿嫁出去，她的把戏我清楚得很——得提防着她！” “Hold firm to my conditions.They will consent, for no one’s apparent interest is injured.Madame Evangelista is very anxious to marry her daughter; I see that in her little game—Beware of her!”
保尔回到会客厅，看到他的未来岳母正低声与索洛内交谈着。纳塔莉被这些密谈排除在外，正把弄着屏风。她觉得有些尴尬，寻思着：“真奇怪！我的事，他们却丝毫不跟我讲。” Paul returned to the salon, where he found his future mother-inlaw conversing in a low tone with Solonet.Natalie, kept outside of these mysterious conferences, was playing with a screen.Embarrassed by her position, she was thinking to herself: “How odd it is that they tell me nothing of my own affairs.”
年轻的公证人已经大概看懂了这个新契约的长远影响，它就是以双方的自尊为基础而建立的。他的主顾已经迎头掉进了这个陷阱。此刻，马蒂亚斯只是一个公证人，而年轻的索洛内却把年轻人的虚荣带进了公事当中。个人的自满和虚荣会使一个人忘记自己的利益，这是经常发生的事情。在这种情况下，索洛内总管让寡妇认为内斯特是无法击败阿喀琉斯的。他建议寡妇接受这些条件，促使婚姻谈判成功。他并不怎么关心婚约会造成什么影响。对他来所，只要埃旺热利斯塔夫人解除了债务，生活得到了保证，并且把纳塔莉嫁出去了，那就是胜利。 The younger notary had seized, in the main, the future effect of the new proposal, based, as it was, on the self-love of both parties, into which his client had fallen headlong.Now, while Mathias was more than a mere notary, Solonet was still a young man, and brought into his business the vanity of youth.It often happens that personal conceit makes a man forgetful of the interests of his client.In this case, Maitre Solonet, who would not suffer the widow to think that Nestor had vanquished Achilles, advised her to conclude the marriage on the terms proposed.Little he cared for the future working of the marriage contract; to him, the conditions of victory were: Madame Evangelista released from her obligations as guardian, her future secured, and Natalie married.
“波多尔城的人都会知道你给了你女儿一百一十万法郎，你还可以有留下两万五的年金，”索洛内对他的主顾耳语道。“我都没想到，能得到这么个大好结局。” “Bordeaux shall know that you have ceded eleven hundred thousand francs to your daughter, and that you still have twenty-five thousand francs a year left,” whispered Solonet to his client.“For my part, I did not expect to obtain such a fine result.”
“可是，”她说，“你跟我说说，为什么设立这种不动产的限嗣继承就能瞬间解决这场暴风骤雨呢？” “But,” she said, “explain to me why the creation of this entail should have calmed the storm at once.”
“那是因为对你和你女儿不信任。不动产的限嗣继承是不能改变的，无论是丈夫还是妻子都不能动用这笔财产。” “It relieves their distrust of you and your daughter.An entail is unchangeable; neither husband nor wife can touch that capital.”
“这种安排岂不是一种侮辱嘛！” “Then this arrangement is positively insulting!”
“不，我们把这称作谨慎。老家伙已经上钩了。如果你拒绝不动产的限嗣继承，他会说：‘你们的目的就是花光我主顾的钱。如果设立了不动产的限嗣继承，主顾的钱财将免遭挥霍，就像“嫁妆体制”一样安全。’” “No; we call it simply precaution.The old fellow has caught you in a net.If you refuse to consent to the entail, he can reply: ‘Then your object is to squander the fortune of my client, who, by the creation of this entail, is protected from all such injury as securely as if the marriage took place under the “regime dotal.”’”
索洛内心中也有所不安，寻思道：“这些规条的后果要到未来才会显示出来，那时埃旺热利斯塔夫人早就归西了。”想到这些，他也就没什么担忧了。 Solonet quieted his own scruples by reflecting: “After all, these stipulations will take effect only in the future, by which time Madame Evangelista will be dead and buried.”
埃旺热利斯塔夫人听完解释也就十分满意了，她对索洛内可是有百分百的信心。她对法律本来就一无所知，考虑到女儿就要嫁出去了，这件事已经赢了，便高兴得不得了。正如马蒂亚斯精明的预想一样，索洛内和埃旺热利斯塔夫人都没有完全看穿这个提案，他这个提案的理由是无懈可击的。 Madame Evangelista contented herself, for the present, with these explanations, having full confidence in Solonet.She was wholly ignorant of law; considering her daughter as good as married, she thought she had gained her end, and was filled with the joy of success.Thus, as Mathias had shrewdly calculated, neither Solonet nor Madame Evangelista understood as yet, to its full extent, this scheme which he had based on reasons that were undeniable.
“好的，马蒂亚斯先生，”寡妇说道，“所有事情都谈妥了，是吧？” “Well, Monsieur Mathias,” said the widow, “all is for the best, is it not?”
“夫人，如果你和伯爵先生都同意这种安排，你们应该互相作出承诺。“我认为，你们应该知道吧？”他看着两人继续说道，“婚姻的基础是，限嗣继承的财产包括朗斯特拉克的地产、苗圃街的房产和未来妻子带来的八十万法郎，这八十万用以投资不动产。请容我再重复一次，夫人，这必须是庄严慎重的承诺，也是绝对不可缺少的承诺。不动产的限嗣继承的设立需要办一些手续，要到司法部登记，还要皇室的法令，我们还得马上去购买新的土地，这样以便把新购置的土地也算入其中，皇室法令颁发后，这些财产就不可更改了。许多家庭还会要求立约作保，但是这次，我认为口头同意就足够了。你们赞成吗？” “Madame, if you and Monsieur le comte consent to this arrangement you ought to exchange pledges.It is fully understood, I suppose,” he continued, looking from one to the other, “that the marriage will only take place on condition of creating an entail upon the estate of Lanstrac and the house in the rue de la Pepiniere, together with eight hundred thousand francs in money brought by the future wife, the said sum to be invested in landed property?Pardon me the repetition, madame; but a positive and solemn engagement becomes absolutely necessary.The creation of an entail requires formalities, application to the chancellor, a royal ordinance, and we ought at once to conclude the purchase of the new estate in order that the property be included in the royal ordinance by virtue of which it becomes inalienable.In many families this would be reduced to writing, but on this occasion I think a simple consent would suffice.Do you consent?”
“赞成，”埃旺热利斯塔夫人答道。 “Yes,” replied Madame Evangelista.
“赞成。”保尔应道。 “Yes,” said Paul.
“我呢？”纳塔莉笑着问道。 “And I?” asked Natalie, laughing.
“你还小，小姐，”索洛内回答道，“不要抱怨了。” “You are a minor, mademoiselle,” replied Solonet; “don’t complain of that.”
大家同意由马蒂亚斯总管草拟契约，索洛内起草监护人账目和财产让与文书。按照法律条文规定，在婚礼举行前几天签署这两个契约。说了一些客套话后，两位公证人准备离开了。 It was then agreed that Maitre Mathias should draw up the contract, Maitre Solonet the guardianship account and release, and that both documents should be signed, as the law requires some days before the celebration of the marriage.After a few polite salutations the notaries withdrew.
“在下雨，马蒂亚斯，我送你回家吧？”索洛内说道。“我的马车就在这里。” “It rains, Mathias; shall I take you home?” said Solonet.“My cabriolet is here.”
“我的马车也在这里。”保尔说，示意想送老人回家。 “My carriage is here too,” said Paul, manifesting an intention to accompany the old man.
“我可不想占用你快乐的时间，”马蒂亚斯答道，“我还是接受我朋友索洛内的好意。” “I won’t rob you of a moment’s pleasure,” said Mathias.“I accept my friend Solonet’s offer.”
“哦，”坐在行进的马车上，阿客琉斯对内斯特说，“您今晚真是有大家风范。事实就是，这些年轻人如果没有你的帮助，非得倾家荡产不可。” “Well,” said Achilles to Nestor, as the cabriolet rolled away, “you have been truly patriarchal tonight.The fact is, those young people would certainly have ruined themselves.”
“我对他们的未来真是忧心忡忡。”马蒂亚斯应道，对自己这个提案的真实动机却只字不提。 “I felt anxious about their future,” replied Mathias, keeping silent as to the real motives of his proposition.
此刻，两位公证人就像一对演员，刚在台上剑拔弩张、针锋相对，转过头来在台下又勾肩搭背起来。 At this moment the two notaries were like a pair of actors arm in arm behind the stage on which they have played a scene of hatred and provocation.
“不过，”索洛内突然又想起了自己的分内事，问道，“你说的买地的事应该是由我来操办，是吧？用的钱就是来自嫁妆的。” “But,” said Solonet, thinking of his rights as notary, “isn’t it my place to buy that land you mentioned?The money is part of our dowry.”
“那你如何把埃旺热利斯塔小姐名下的财产纳入德马内维尔伯爵设立的不动产的限嗣继承财产里面呢？”马蒂亚斯问道。 “How can you put property bought in the name of Mademoiselle Evangelista into the creation of an entail by the Comte de Manerville?” replied Mathias.
“这个问题我们得咨询司法部了。”索洛内说道。 “We shall have to ask the chancellor about that,” said Solonet.
“但我可是那块地买主和卖主共有的公证人。”马蒂亚斯说。“而且，德马内维尔先生可以用自己的名义购买。待到支付款项时，我们可以提及使用陪嫁的钱财。” “But I am the notary of the seller as well as of the buyer of that land,” said Mathias.“Besides, Monsieur de Manerville can buy in his own name.At the time of payment we can make mention of the fact that the dowry funds are put into it.”
“你什么事情都能解决，老前辈，”索洛内笑着调侃道，“今晚你是全胜了，我们不是你的对手。” “You’ve an answer for everything, old man,” said Solonet, laughing.“You were really surpassing tonight; you beat us squarely.”
“对一个老家伙来说，对你们的葡萄弹并没有思想准备，我能做成这样，已经很不错了，是吧？” “For an old fellow who didn’t expect your batteries of grape-shot, I did pretty well, didn’t I?”
“哈！哈！哈！”索洛内笑了起来。 “Ha! ha! ha!” laughed Solonet.
在这场可恶的斗争中，一个家庭的物质财富差点儿被摧毁，但是对于这两位公证人来说，只不过是职业上的一场较量而已。 The odious struggle in which the material welfare of a family had been so perilously near destruction was to the two notaries nothing more than a matter of professional polemics.
“这一行我干了四十年了，总还是有点儿用的。”马蒂亚斯说道，“你看，索洛内，”他接着说，“我是个好人，签署卖地契约时，你也可以参与。” “I haven’t been forty years in harness for nothing,” remarked Mathias.“Look here, Solonet,” he added, “I’m a good fellow; you shall help in drawing the deeds for the sale of those lands.”
“谢谢，亲爱的马蒂亚斯。作为报答，我一有机会就会为您服务。 “Thanks, my dear Mathias.I’ll serve you in return on the very first occasion.”
当两位公证人只是感觉有些口干舌燥，正心平气和地往家走的时候，留在屋里的保尔和埃旺热利斯塔夫人则神经紧张，筋肉和大脑仍然在不停地颤抖。这是他们的利益和感情受到激烈的震荡之后的一种感觉。对埃旺热利斯塔夫人来说，这场暴风雨的最后几声响雷来自天边的一抹红云，她沉思着，不惜代价地想看清红云的后面究竟隐藏着什么。 While the two notaries were peacefully returning homeward, with no other sensations than a little throaty warmth, Paul and Madame Evangelista were left a prey to the nervous trepidation, the quivering of the flesh and brain which excitable natures pass through after a scene in which their interests and their feelings have been violently shaken.In Madame Evangelista these last mutterings of the storm were overshadowed by a terrible reflection, a lurid gleam which she wanted, at any cost, to dispel.
她自言自语道：我辛辛苦苦花了六个月准备的事，难道就这样被马蒂亚斯总管毁于一旦？”“他把保尔拉到旁边一个房间，是否是想让保尔起疑，好使他不受我的影响？” “Has Maitre Mathias destroyed in a few minutes the work I have been doing for six months?” she asked herself.“Was he withdrawing Paul from my influence by filling his mind with suspicion during their secret conference in the next room?”
她站在壁炉前，把肘支在壁炉的大理石边缘上，陷入了沉思中。大门在两位公证人的马车驶出后一关闭，她就迫不及待地转过身来，打算从未来女婿身上来消除心中的疑惑。 She was standing absorbed in these thoughts before the fireplace, her elbow resting on the marble mantel-shelf.When the porte-cochere closed behind the carriage of the two notaries, she turned to her future son-inlaw, impatient to solve her doubts.
“今天真是我经历过的最可怕的一天。”保尔看到这些困难都迎刃而解了，高兴地说道，“我没见过比老马蒂亚斯先生更直率的人了。愿上帝听到他的祈祷，让我成为法兰西贵族院议员！亲爱的纳塔莉，我这个愿望，更多的是为了你，而不是为我自己。你就是我的雄心壮志；我活着也只是为了你。” “This has been the most terrible day of my life,” cried Paul, overjoyed to see all difficulties vanish.“I know no one so downright in speech as that old Mathias.May God hear him, and make me peer of France!Dear Natalie, I desire this for your sake more than for my own.You are my ambition; I live only in you.”
埃旺热利斯塔夫人听到这番肺腑之言，尤其是看到保尔那双清澈无邪的碧蓝眼睛，表明他绝无二心。她感到很满意。她后悔刚刚不该用尖酸的语言去刺激他。她还沉浸在成功的喜悦中，决定用未来的生活来安抚他。她神态自若，眼神中展现出温柔的友情，这越发使她显得迷人。她微笑着答道： Hearing this speech uttered in the accents of the heart, and noting, more especially, the limpid azure of Paul’s eyes, whose glance betrayed no thought of double meaning, Madame Evangelista’s satisfaction was complete.She regretted the sharp language with which she had spurred him, and in the joy of success she resolved to reassure him as to the future.Calming her countenance, and giving to her eyes that expression of tender friendship which made her so attractive, she smiled and answered:—
“我要说的跟你差不多。亲爱的保尔，也许作为一个西班牙后裔，我更像一个父亲而不是一个母亲。你是个大好人，像上帝一样和蔼——不要对我那几句未经思考就脱口而出的话而生气。握个手吧。” “I can say as much to you.Perhaps, dear Paul, my Spanish nature has led me farther than my heart desired.Be what you are,—kind as God himself,—and do not be angry with me for a few hasty words.Shake hands.”
保尔有点羞愧。他觉得该受责备的人应该是自己，于是他亲吻了一下埃旺热利斯塔夫人的脸颊。 Paul was abashed; he fancied himself to blame, and he kissed Madame Evangelista.
“亲爱的保尔，”她激动地说道，“事情能这么轻而易举地解决，他们两个精明人为什么要拖我们进来呢？” “Dear Paul,” she said with much emotion, “why could not those two sharks have settled this matter without dragging us into it, since it was so easy to settle?”
“我真想不到，您是如此宽宏大量！”保尔答道。 “In that case I should not have known how grand and generous you can be,” replied Paul.
“她的确是这样的人，”纳塔莉握住保尔的手，高声说道。 “Indeed she is, Paul,” cried Natalie, pressing his hand.
“我们还有一些小问题尚待解决，我亲爱的孩子。”埃旺热利斯塔夫人说，“许多人都对所谓的虚荣很重视，我女儿和我却不是很在意。纳塔莉不需要我的首饰，不过我还是很乐意给她的。” “We have still a few little matters to settle, my dear son,” said Madame Evangelista.“My daughter and I are above the foolish vanities to which so many persons cling.Natalie does not need my diamonds, but I am glad to give them to her.”
“啊！我亲爱的母亲，您认为我会接受您的金银首饰吗？” “Ah! my dear mother, do you suppose that I will accept them?”
“是的，孩子，契约中明文规定了的。” “Yes, my child; they are one of the conditions of the contract.”
“我不会要的。我不结婚了，”纳塔莉急切地大声答道。“那些首饰是当初父亲高高兴兴地亲手送给你的。你自己留着吧。保尔先生怎么能——？ “I will not allow it; I will not marry at all,” cried Natalie, vehemently.“Keep those jewels which my father took such pride in collecting for you.How could Monsieur Paul exact—”
“别说了，亲爱的，”母亲说道，眼眶中满溢着泪水。“我不善于理财，迫使我付出比这还要大得多的代价。” “Hush, my dear,” said her mother, whose eyes now filled with tears.“My ignorance of business compels me to a greater sacrifice than that.”
“什么代价？” “What sacrifice?”
“我欠你的债务，我得把房子卖了才还得清。” “I must sell my house in order to pay the money that I owe to you.”
“您怎么可能欠我的钱？”她说，“我的生命都是您给的！如果我的婚姻会给您带来哪怕最小的损失，我也不结婚了。” “What money can you possibly owe to me?” she said; “to me, who owe you life!If my marriage costs you the slightest sacrifice, I will not marry.”
“孩子！” “Child!”
“亲爱的纳塔莉，你得明白，不是我，也不是你母亲，更不是你自己要母亲作出这些牺牲，而是我们的孩子。” “Dear Natalie, try to understand that neither I, nor your mother, nor you yourself, require these sacrifices, but our children.”
“要是我不结婚了呢？” “Suppose I do not marry at all?”
“你是不是不爱我了？”保尔温柔地问道。 “Do you not love me?” said Paul, tenderly.
“来，来，我的傻孩子；你以为婚约是纸搭的房子，一吹就能倒的吗？”不懂事的姑娘，你不知道我们费了多大的劲才为你大儿子找到不动产的限嗣继承权。这件事我们好不容易才谈妥，不要又让我们重新开始麻烦了。 “Come, come, my silly child; do you imagine that a contract is like a house of cards which you can blow down at will?Dear little ignoramus, you don’t know what trouble we have had to found an entail for the benefit of your eldest son.Don’t cast us back into the discussions from which we have just escaped.”
“那你为什么非要弄得我母亲一无所有呢？”纳塔莉看着保尔，质问道。 “Why do you wish to ruin my mother?” said Natalie, looking at Paul.
“你们为什么如此富裕呢？”他笑着答道。 “Why are you so rich?” he replied, smiling.
“孩子们，不要吵架了，你们还没结婚呢。”埃旺热利斯塔夫人说。“保尔，”她继续说道，“你不用给我们彩礼、珠宝和衣物之类的。纳塔莉这些东西都很多。可以把本来用来购买这些结婚礼物的钱存下来。结婚的时候花上十万法郎买结婚礼物，不明智也很世俗，不如每年花五千，反而能省掉一个年轻女子的许多烦恼，还能用上一辈子。而且这购置彩礼的钱要拿去装饰你巴黎的房子。春季的时候，我们会回到朗斯特拉克，等到冬天时，索洛内将结清我的债务。” “Don’t quarrel, my children, you are not yet married,” said Madame Evangelista.“Paul,” she continued, “you are not to give either corbeille, or jewels, or trousseau.Natalie has everything in profusion.Lay by the money you would otherwise put into wedding presents.I know nothing more stupidly bourgeois and commonplace than to spend a hundred thousand francs on a corbeille, when five thousand a year given to a young woman saves her much anxiety and lasts her lifetime.Besides, the money for a corbeille is needed to decorate your house in Paris.We will return to Lanstrac in the spring; for Solonet is to settle my debts during the winter.”
“那样就再好不过了。”保尔愉悦之极，高声应道。 “All is for the best,” cried Paul, at the summit of happiness.
“那我将看到巴黎了！”纳塔莉叫起来，那腔调连德马赛这样的人听到了都会吓一跳。 “So I shall see Paris!” cried Natalie, in a tone that would justly have alarmed de Marsay.
“如果就这样定了，”保尔说，“我就跟德马赛写信了，叫他在意大利歌剧院给我订个包厢。” “If we decide upon this plan,” said Paul, “I’ll write to de Marsay and get him to take a box for me at the Bouffons and also at the Italian opera.”
“你真是太好了，我都不敢这样要求你。”纳塔莉说。“如果丈夫能猜得出妻子内心的想法，那婚姻将是一件非常令人高兴的事。” “You are very kind; I should never have dared to ask for it,” said Natalie.“Marriage is a very agreeable institution if it gives husbands a talent for divining the wishes of their wives.”
“没什么。”保尔答道，“不过不早了，我得告辞了。” “It is nothing else,” replied Paul.“But see how late it is; I ought to go.”
“今晚怎么走这么早？”埃旺热利斯塔夫人说道，她试着显得体贴周到，男人对这些是非常敏感的。 “Why leave so soon tonight?” said Madame Evangelista, employing those coaxing ways to which men are so sensitive.
虽然所有的事都很顺利，也是在礼仪法律之内解决的，可是这一切还是给女婿和岳母的心里都埋下了不信任和不和的种子。一旦碰到愤怒的火苗或感情的冲击，都会发芽成长起来。在大部分家庭中，婚约中女方“嫁妆”和男方聘礼的确定都会埋下最初的敌意，都是由于自尊、某种情感创伤、后悔作出牺牲和渴望减少牺牲等造成的。当困难出现时，总会有一个胜方和一个败方。在双方父母看来，这纯粹是一桩于己有利的生意。因此，在这样的谈判中，充满了算计、狡猾和欺骗。一般来说，只有丈夫深谙其道，而像纳塔莉这样的妻子对这些会使她变富裕或穷困的条约却一窍不通。 Though all this passed on the best of terms, and according to the laws of the most exquisite politeness, the effect of the discussion of these contending interests had, nevertheless, cast between son and mother-inlaw a seed of distrust and enmity which was liable to sprout under the first heat of anger, or the warmth of a feeling too harshly bruised.In most families the settlement of “dots” and the deeds of gift required by a marriage contract give rise to primitive emotions of hostility, caused by self-love, by the lesion of certain sentiments, by regret for the sacrifices made, and by the desire to diminish them.When difficulties arise there is always a victorious side and a vanquished one.The parents of the future pair try to conclude the matter, which is purely commercial in their eyes, to their own advantage; and this leads to the trickery, shrewdness, and deception of such negotiations.Generally the husband alone is initiated into the secret of these discussions, and the wife is kept, like Natalie, in ignorance of the stipulations which make her rich or poor.
保尔离开的时候，他想道，多亏了他家公证人聪明能干，才使他的财产几乎完好无损。只要埃旺热利斯塔夫人和她女儿不分开住，她们每年将有十万法郎的收入用以支配开销。他那幸福舒适的生活完全可以实现。 As he left the house, Paul reflected that, thanks to the cleverness of his notary, his fortune was almost entirely secured from injury.If Madame Evangelista did not live apart from her daughter their united household would have an income of more than a hundred thousand francs to spend.All his expectations of a happy and comfortable life would be realized.
“我的岳母看上去是个不错的女人。”他寻思着，仍然沉浸在他岳母巧言令色的影响之下。之前那番争论所造成的乌云显然已经在埃旺热利斯塔夫人的努力之下被驱散了。“马蒂亚斯搞错了。这些公证人都是奇怪的家伙，他们总把人往坏的地方想。怪就要怪那个坏小子索洛内，他总是打着自己的小算盘。” “My mother-inlaw seems to me an excellent woman,” he thought, still under the influence of the cajoling manner by which she had endeavored to disperse the clouds raised by the discussion.“Mathias is mistaken.These notaries are strange fellows; they envenom everything.The harm started from that little cock-sparrow Solonet, who wanted to play a clever game.”
当保尔睡在床上正思考着自己这一天来所得到的利益时，埃旺热利斯塔夫人同样地也正在庆祝着自己的胜利。 While Paul went to bed recapitulating the advantages he had won during the evening, Madame Evangelista was congratulating herself equally on her victory.
“喂，亲爱的妈妈，您对此满意吗？”纳塔莉跟着埃旺热利斯塔夫人走进卧室时问道。 “Well, darling mother, are you satisfied?” said Natalie, following Madame Evangelista into her bedroom.
“是的，亲爱的，”母亲答道，“一切都还如意，我感觉压在肩头的那块大石头搬开了。保尔是个易于相处的人。一个可爱的家伙！是的，一定的，我们得使他的生活更上一层楼。你将使他生活幸福，而我要负责让他在政治上取得成功。西班牙大使是我的老朋友，我要和他重续友情——也要和其他的旧相识联系上。噢！你会看到的！我们即将成为巴黎的中心，周围的一切都将是快乐和幸福。亲爱的，你来享受幸福，而我这一生中最后的意义就是——帮他实现雄心壮志！看我卖了这房子，你也不要惊慌。难道你认为我们还会回到波尔多来吗？不。朗斯特拉克？是的。不过，冬天我们都会在巴黎过，那儿才是我们利益之所在。纳塔莉，告诉我，我要你做的，是不是非常难以做到？” “Yes, love,” replied the mother, “everything went well, according to my wishes; I feel a weight lifted from my shoulders which was crushing me.Paul is a most easy-going man.Dear fellow!yes, certainly, we must make his life prosperous.You will make him happy, and I will be responsible for his political success.The Spanish ambassador used to be a friend of mine, and I’ll renew the relation—as I will with the rest of my old acquaintance.Oh! you’ll see! we shall soon be in the very heart of Parisian life; all will be enjoyment for us.You shall have the pleasures, my dearest, and I the last occupation of existence,—the game of ambition!Don’t be alarmed when you see me selling this house.Do you suppose we shall ever come back to live in Bordeaux? no. Lanstrac? yes.But we shall spend all our winters in Paris, where our real interests lie.Well, Natalie, tell me, was it very difficult to do what I asked of you?”
“我的好妈妈！我时常会感觉有点儿惭愧。” “My little mamma! every now and then I felt ashamed.”
“索洛内建议我把房子卖掉，好从中获取年金，”埃旺热利斯塔夫人说道，“不过我不能这么做，我不愿从你那里拿走一个分钱。” “Solonet advises me to put the proceeds of this house into an annuity,” said Madame Evangelista, “but I shall do otherwise; I won’t take a penny of my fortune from you.”
“当时我看见你们都十分生气，”纳塔莉说，“这场暴风骤雨是怎么平息的呢？” “I saw you were all very angry,” said Natalie.“How did the tempest calm down?”
“我把我的钻石送给他了，”埃旺热利斯塔夫人答道，“索洛内是正确的。这件事情上，他表现得多么能干。把我的首饰盒拿出来算了，纳塔莉。我还从没算过我的那些钻石到底值多少。我当时说价值十万法郎，都是胡说的。德吉亚斯夫人总认为，单单就你父亲在结婚那天送我的项链和耳环就不只那个数了。我那可怜的丈夫真是奢侈！再加上我家传下来的钻石，就是腓力二世送给阿尔伯公爵的那颗，后来我阿姨又传给我了。我记得当时市值就达八万法郎——是一颗我们西班牙的金币。“ “By an offer of my diamonds,” replied Madame Evangelista.“Solonet was right.How ably he conducted the whole affair.Get out my jewel-case, Natalie.I have never seriously considered what my diamonds are worth.When I said a hundred thousand francs I talked nonsense.Madame de Gyas always declared that the necklace and earrings your father gave me on our marriage day were worth at least that sum.My poor husband was so lavish!Then my family diamond, the one Philip the Second gave to the Duke of Alba, and which my aunt bequeathed to me, the ‘Discreto,’ was, I think, appraised in former times at four thousand quadruples,—one of our Spanish gold coins.”
纳塔莉把母亲的珍珠项链、钻石首饰、黄金手镯和珍稀宝石都摆出来了，用一种难以言表的表情欣赏着这些珠宝——正如犹太评论家们所说——堕落的天使从地球内部找来天国火焰之花，以此引诱了人类的女儿们。 Natalie laid out upon her mother’s toilet-table the pearl necklace, the sets of jewels, the gold bracelets and precious stones of all description, with that inexpressible sensation enjoyed by certain women at the sight of such treasures, by which—so commentators on the Talmud say—the fallen angels seduce the daughters of men, having sought these flowers of celestial fire in the bowels of the earth.
“当然，”埃旺热利斯塔夫人说道，“虽说我只知道接受和佩戴这些珠宝，但我也知道它们值不少钱。而且，如果我们成为一家人后，我可以把我的那些纯银餐具卖掉，按重量计算，能得到三万法郎。我记得当初我把餐具从利马带来，过海关的时候，海关人员称重后定的这个价。索洛内是正确的，我明天将派人去请埃利·玛古斯来。这个犹太人将为我们的珠宝估个价。也许我不用把所有财产都投到年金中去。” “Certainly,” said Madame Evangelista, “though I know nothing about jewels except how to accept and wear them, I think there must be a great deal of money in these.Then, if we make but one household, I can sell my plate, the weight of which, as mere silver, would bring thirty thousand francs.I remember when we brought it from Lima, the custom-house officers weighed and appraised it.Solonet is right, I’ll send tomorrow to Elie Magus.The Jew shall estimate the value of these things.Perhaps I can avoid sinking any of my fortune in an annuity.”
“多么漂亮的一条珍珠项链啊！”纳塔莉叹道。 “What a beautiful pearl necklace!” said Natalie.
“如果他爱你，他应该把这根项链留着送给你，”她母亲答道，“我想他或许会把我所有的珠宝都加工成适合你佩戴的，然后让你保存。婚约中拟定，珠宝是你的财产之一。就说到这里吧，晚安，亲爱的。今天都很累，我们都早点休息吧。” “He ought to give it to you, if he loves you,” replied her mother; “and I think he might have all my other jewels reset and let you keep them.The diamonds are a part of your property in the contract.And now, good-night, my darling.After the fatigues of this day we both need rest.”
这位习惯奢华的克里奥尔贵妇无力分析这样的婚约会带来什么样的后果。她看到女儿即将嫁给一个容易掌控的男人，而这个男人也将承认她们母女俩女主人的地位，两家的财产合二为一，她们的生活方式也不会变化。想到这些，她心满意足地睡觉去了。跟女儿的账也算结清了，虽然婚约中承认了所有的财产都是女儿的，埃旺热利斯塔夫人仍然能舒适地生活。 The woman of luxury, the Creole, the great lady, incapable of analyzing the results of a contract which was not yet in force, went to sleep in the joy of seeing her daughter married to a man who was easy to manage, who would let them both be mistresses of his home, and whose fortune, united to theirs, would require no change in their way of living.Thus having settled her account with her daughter, whose patrimony was acknowledged in the contract, Madame Evangelista could feel at her ease.
“之前我还担心得不得了，真是愚蠢之极。”她寻思着，“不过我原本还真希望这婚事谈不成。” “How foolish of me to worry as I did,” she thought.“But I wish the marriage were well over.”
因此，埃旺热利斯塔夫人、保尔、纳塔莉和两位公证人都对第一天的结果感到满意。双方阵营都为对方唱起了赞歌——真是一种危险的状况。总有一天，失败者会搞明白自己所犯的错误。对于埃旺热利斯塔夫人来说，她的女婿就是失败方。 So Madame Evangelista, Paul, Natalie, and the two notaries were equally satisfied with the first day’s result.The Te Deum was sung in both camps,—a dangerous situation; for there comes a moment when the vanquished side is aware of its mistake.To Madame Evangelista’s mind, her son-inlaw was the vanquished side.
第四章 婚约——第二日 CHAPTER IV THE MARRIAGE CONTRACT—SECOND DAY
第二天，埃旺热利斯塔夫人把埃利·玛古斯请到自己家中，他碰巧正好也在波尔多。外面传言保尔伯爵即将与纳塔莉小姐联姻，玛古斯本以为是要给新娘购买珠宝首饰。因此，当这个犹太人听说情况正好相反，是要自己来给这个岳母的首饰估价时，不由得大吃一惊。犹太人凭直觉，以及提出的一些拐弯抹角的问题，终于搞清楚了这些珠宝的价格是包括在婚约里面的。珠宝暂时是不卖的，但他得像个到珠宝店买珠宝的人一样，对这些珠宝估个价。只有珠宝商才分辨得出哪些是亚洲钻石，哪些是巴西钻石。戈尔康达和萨普耳的宝石颜色纯白，闪闪发光，其他宝石都不具备这样的特点——巴西宝石的水色偏黄，因此价格相对偏低一点。埃旺热利斯塔夫人的项链和耳环完全由亚洲钻石组成，埃利·玛古斯为其估价为二十五万法郎。而那颗祖传钻石，他认为是私人藏品中最好的一颗，业界内很有知名度，估价为十万法郎。这个估价也证明了她丈夫是多么的奢侈。埃旺热利斯塔夫人听到这个报价后，便询问老犹太人是否这笔钱能马上得到。 The next day Elie Magus (who happened at that time to be in Bordeaux) obeyed Madame Evangelista’s summons, believing, from general rumor as to the marriage of Comte Paul with Mademoiselle Natalie, that it concerned a purchase of jewels for the bride.The Jew was, therefore, astonished when he learned that, on the contrary, he was sent for to estimate the value of the mother-inlaw’s property.The instinct of his race, as well as certain insidious questions, made him aware that the value of the diamonds was included in the marriage-contract.The stones were not to be sold, and yet he was to estimate them as if some private person were buying them from a dealer.Jewellers alone know how to distinguish between the diamonds of Asia and those of Brazil.The stones of Golconda and Visapur are known by a whiteness and glittering brilliancy which others have not,—the water of the Brazilian diamonds having a yellow tinge which reduces their selling value.Madame Evangelista’s necklace and earrings, being composed entirely of Asiatic diamonds, were valued by Elie Magus at two hundred and fifty thousand francs.As for the “Discreto,” he pronounced it one of the finest diamonds in the possession of private persons; it was known to the trade and valued at one hundred thousand francs.On hearing this estimate, which proved to her the lavishness of her husband, Madame Evangelista asked the old Jew whether she should be able to obtain that money immediately.
“夫人，”犹太人答道，“如果你真希望卖掉的话，那颗祖传宝石我出七万五，项链和耳环出十六万。” “Madame,” replied the Jew, “if you wish to sell I can give you only seventy-five thousand for the brilliant, and one hundred and sixty thousand for the necklace and earrings.”
“为什么减这么多呢？” “Why such reduction?”
“夫人，”玛古斯回答，“钻石越好，我们越要保存着不卖。宝石身价太高，因此很少有人愿意出资购买。商人不愿意损失他的现金利息，这部分额外支出加上这种商品的价格有涨有跌，也就解释了为什么买价和卖价之间的差异。持有这些钻石的二十年间，你已经损失了三十万法郎的利息。假设你一年佩戴十次，也就是说你每参加一次晚会就用掉三千法郎。那笔钱能买多少漂亮的衣服啊。所以那些持有钻石首饰的人都笨透了。但对于我们来说，幸运的是，女人们从不愿意这样计算。” “Madame,” replied Magus, “the finer the diamond, the longer we keep it unsold.The rarity of such investments is one reason for the high value set upon precious stones.As the merchant cannot lose the interest of his money, this additional sum, joined to the rise and fall to which such merchandise is subject, explains the difference between the price of purchase and the price of sale.By owning these diamonds you have lost the interest on three hundred thousand francs for twenty years.If you wear your jewels ten times a year, it costs you three thousand francs each evening to put them on.How many beautiful gowns you could buy with that sum.Those who own diamonds are, therefore, very foolish; but, luckily for us, women are never willing to understand the calculation.”
“谢谢你给我解释清楚了，那我就要利用它们盈利了。” “I thank you for explaining it to me, and I shall profit by it.”
“你希望卖掉吗？”玛古斯迫切地问道。 “Do you wish to sell?” asked Magus, eagerly.
“剩下的珠宝都值多少钱？” “What are the other jewels worth?”
犹太人仔细地观察着这些黄金饰品，就着灯光鉴赏珍珠，并且端详了红宝石、发饰、别针、手镯和项链，咕哝道： The Jew examined the gold of the settings, held the pearls to the light, scrutinized the rubies, the diadems, clasps, bracelets, and chains, and said, in a mumbling tone:—
“这里面有很多葡萄牙钻石是产于巴西的。照我看，总共价值不超过十万。不过，”他继续说道，“商人卖给顾客，至少能卖到十五万法郎。” “A good many Portuguese diamonds from Brazil are among them.They are not worth more than a hundred thousand to me.But,” he added, “a dealer would sell them to a customer for one hundred and fifty thousand, at least.”
“我会留着。”埃旺热利斯塔夫人说。 “I shall keep them,” said Madame Evangelista.
“你错了，”埃利·玛古斯答道，“用卖掉首饰的资金去投资，五年之后你赚到的钱又能买到同样好的钻石，还保留了卖钻石的钱。” “You are wrong,” replied Elie Magus.“With the income from the sum they represent you could buy just as fine diamonds in five years, and have the capital to boot.”
这一次特别的谈话后来被传了出去，更进一步证实了有关婚约争论的谣言。家中的仆人偷听到了几次屋内的大声喧哗，便揣测争论的激烈程度，比事实还要夸张许多。他们与其他家仆聊天，那些传言又从低到高传到主人的耳朵里了。整个社交圈，乃至整个城镇的人都很关注这两个富裕的名门望族之间的联姻，无论是大人物还是市井之徒都热心于此事。还没超过一个星期，到处都是闻所未闻的谣言。 This singular conference became known, and corroborated certain rumors excited by the discussion of the contract.The servants of the house, overhearing high voices, supposed the difficulties greater than they really were.Their gossip with other valets spread the information, which from the lower regions rose to the ears of the masters.The attention of society, and of the town in general, became so fixed on the marriage of two persons equally rich and well-born, that every one, great and small, busied themselves about the matter, and in less than a week the strangest rumors were bruited about.
“埃旺热利斯塔夫人准备卖掉房子，她肯定是破产咯。她想把金银首饰卖给埃利·玛古斯呢。她和德马内维尔伯爵先生还没真正达成任何共识。这件婚事到底能不能谈成？” “Madame Evangelista sells her house; she must be ruined.She offered her diamonds to Elie Magus.Nothing is really settled between herself and the Comte de Manerville.Is it probable that the marriage will ever take place?”
对这个问题，有些人说能，有些人说不能。当有人就此事问到两位公证人时，公证人公开否认了这些谣言，并宣布唯一的难题只是在不动产的限嗣继承上，根据官方规矩还有一些时间上的拖延。但是当公众舆论已经朝着一个既定方向前进的时候，要使它调转过来是非常困难的。尽管保尔每天都会到埃旺热利斯塔夫人家，公证人也否认了传言，但是那些风言风语仍然继续着。年轻的姑娘们、她们的母亲和阿姨们，都对自己或者家人梦寐以求的婚事而焦虑着，因此不能容忍埃旺热利斯塔家的西班牙女人们太得意，就像作家们互相妒忌对方的成功一样。埃旺热利斯塔家这二十年来生活奢侈豪华，伤害到了一些人的自尊心，现在他们要报复。省府一位有头有脸的人物说，即使双方谈不拢，两位公证人也会这么辟谣的。不动产的限嗣继承的设立需要耗时很久，使得波尔多的上层人士疑心更重。 To this question some answered yes, and others said no.The two notaries, when questioned, denied these calumnies, and declared that the difficulties arose only from the official delay in constituting the entail.But when public opinion has taken a trend in one direction it is very difficult to turn it back.Though Paul went every day to Madame Evangelista’s house, and though the notaries denied these assertions continually, the whispered calumny went on.Young girls, and their mothers and aunts, vexed at a marriage they had dreamed of for themselves or for their families, could not forgive the Spanish ladies for their happiness, as authors cannot forgive each other for their success.A few persons revenged themselves for the twenty-years luxury and grandeur of the family of Evangelista, which had lain heavily on their self-love.A leading personage at the prefecture declared that the notaries could have chosen no other language and followed no other conduct in the case of a rupture.The time actually required for the establishment of the entail confirmed the suspicions of the Bordeaux provincials.
“整个冬天都是类似的话，然后春天到了，他们会去湖边度假，不到一年我们就会知道，这婚事是没影的事。” “They will keep the ball going through the winter; then, in the spring, they will go to some watering-place, and we shall learn before the year is out that the marriage is off.”
“当然，为了两家的面子，他们会解释说，”一些人说，“困难不是一方造成的，而是司法部门不同意。大家都明白是限嗣继承这问题把婚事搞砸的。” “And, of course, we shall be given to understand,” said others, “for the sake of the honor of the two families, that the difficulties did not come from either side, but the chancellor refused to consent; you may be sure it will be some quibble about that entail which will cause the rupture.”
“埃旺热利斯塔夫人的开销，”有些人说，“即便是瓦伦西亚的金矿都不够用。到了该女儿嫁妆的时候，她可是一个子儿都没有了。” “Madame Evangelista,” some said, “lived in a style that the mines of Valencia couldn’t meet.When the time came to melt the bell, and pay the daughter’s patrimony, nothing would be found to pay it with.”
现在是估算这位漂亮的寡妇生活开销到底有多大的绝好时机，或者说是时候证明她已经倾家荡产了。谣言四起，甚至有人为此下起了赌注。按照世俗惯例，这些流言蜚语不能被当事方所听到。保尔和埃旺热利斯塔夫人没有推心置腹的朋友，也没有不共戴天的敌人，所以没人会告诉他们外面的谣言。保尔到朗斯特拉克去做生意，顺便利用这个机会和波尔多的几个年轻人去狩猎——好似是在告别他的单身生活。大家却都认为这次狩猎更进一步证实了公众的猜疑。 The occasion was excellent to add up the spendings of the handsome widow and prove, categorically, her ruin.Rumors were so rife that bets were made for and against the marriage.By the laws of worldly jurisprudence this gossip was not allowed to reach the ears of the parties concerned.No one was enemy or friend enough to Paul or to Madame Evangelista to inform either of what was being said.Paul had some business at Lanstrac, and used the occasion to make a hunting-party for several of the young men of Bordeaux,—a sort of farewell, as it were, to his bachelor life.This hunting party was accepted by society as a signal confirmation of public suspicion.
狩猎结束后，有一个女儿待字闺中的德吉亚斯夫人，觉得该是探明虚实的时候了，并且应该安慰安慰受到打击的埃旺热利斯塔家，虽然吉亚斯夫人自己对这番打击很高兴。纳塔莉和母亲看到侯爵夫人拉长的脸孔时，有点惊诧，便问她是否遇到了什么不开心的事。 When this event occurred, Madame de Gyas, who had a daughter to marry, thought it high time to sound the matter, and to condole, with joyful heart, the blow received by the Evangelistas.Natalie and her mother were somewhat surprised to see the lengthened face of the marquise, and they asked at once if anything distressing had happened to her.
她回答道：“你们没听说外界的那些谣传？虽然我认为那都是假的，但是我还是来搞清真相，来制止那些谣传。至少我的朋友圈里的人不会再有人说了。被谣传所欺骗，或成为以讹传讹的帮凶，真正的朋友是不会这么干的。” “Can it be,” she replied, “that you are ignorant of the rumors that are circulating?Though I think them false myself, I have come to learn the truth in order to stop this gossip, at any rate among the circle of my own friends.To be the dupes or the accomplices of such an error is too false a position for true friends to occupy.”
“不过到底是怎么回事啊？发生什么事了？”母女两人异口同声问道。 “But what is it? what has happened?” asked mother and daughter.
因此吉亚斯夫人万分愉悦地把外面的所有谣言都重复了一遍，任何一句伤人的话都没漏掉。纳塔莉和埃旺热利斯塔夫人笑着看着对方，对这位朋友说的这番话意欲何在，动机何在，她们完全心知肚明了。这个西班牙夫人开始了像塞莉梅纳对阿尔西诺艾一样的报复： Madame de Gyas thereupon allowed herself the happiness of repeating all the current gossip, not sparing her two friends a single stab.Natalie and Madame Evangelista looked at each other and laughed, but they fully understood the meaning of the tale and the motives of their friend.The Spanish lady took her revenge very much as Celimene took hers on Arsinoe.
“亲爱的，你如此见多识广，却不知道这些吗？一个母亲有一个女儿要出嫁，却又嫁不出，或是没有‘嫁妆’，或是没有合适的对象，或是没有美貌，或是考虑不足，再或者什么都没有，你难道不知道她能做些什么吗？一个处于这种境地的母亲会怎么办呢，她会拦路枪击甚至杀人都可以，她会在大街的转角等待一个男人——这个女人愿意牺牲无数次，只要她还是个母亲。你我都知道，在波尔多城，现在有很多处于这种环境下的人，无疑是他们把自己的想法和行为强加到了我们身上。自然学家描述过许多猛禽野兽的生活习惯，但是他们却忘记了帮女儿寻找丈夫的母亲们。如大卫王所说，这些妇女就像鬣狗，她们寻觅可以吞噬的对象，她们有野禽的本能、男人的智力和女人的天分。我明白那些小蜘蛛像德贝洛尔小姐、德特朗小姐之类的人，辛辛苦苦地编了半天的网却一只苍蝇都没捕到，甚至连嗡嗡声都没听到，于是便狂怒起来；我能原谅她们恶毒的语言。但是你不同，你想嫁女的话，随时都可以。你家庭殷实，又有贵族称号，没有一点儿乡土气息。你的女儿聪明美丽，集各项优点于一身，当然可以慢慢地选择——你的巴黎式优雅是如此与众不同，你本应该不去留意这些流言蜚语的，可你真是令我吃惊不小啊。我是不是得向公众解释婚约中的那些细则？而我们的公证人认为，那些细则对我家女婿的未来政治生涯是很有帮助的。这种公众争论的疯狂行为是不是已经干涉家庭内务了呢？难道我还得把当地的所有父亲和母亲都叫来，叫他们对我家婚约的各项细则都一一投票通过吗？” “My dear, are you ignorant—you who know the provinces so well—can you be ignorant of what a mother is capable when she has on her hands a daughter whom she cannot marry for want of ‘dot’ and lovers, want of beauty, want of mind, and, sometimes, want of everything?Why, a mother in that position would rob a diligence or commit a murder, or wait for a man at the corner of a street—she would sacrifice herself twenty times over, if she was a mother at all.Now, as you and I both know, there are many such in that situation in Bordeaux, and no doubt they attribute to us their own thoughts and actions.Naturalists have depicted the habits and customs of many ferocious animals, but they have forgotten the mother and daughter in quest of a husband.Such women are hyenas, going about, as the Psalmist says, seeking whom they may devour, and adding to the instinct of the brute the intellect of man, and the genius of woman.I can understand that those little spiders, Mademoiselle de Belor, Mademoiselle de Trans, and others, after working so long at their webs without catching a fly, without so much as hearing a buzz, should be furious; I can even forgive their spiteful speeches.But that you, who can marry your daughter when you please, you, who are rich and titled, you who have nothing of the provincial about you, whose daughter is clever and possesses fine qualities, with beauty and the power to choose—that you, so distinguished from the rest by your Parisian grace, should have paid the least heed to this talk does really surprise me.Am I bound to account to the public for the marriage stipulations which our notaries think necessary under the political circumstances of my son-inlaw’s future life?Has the mania for public discussion made its way into families?Ought I to convoke in writing the fathers and mothers of the province to come here and give their vote on the clauses of our marriage contract?”
对波尔多的哀怨如奔腾洪水，一发而不可收拾。埃旺热利斯塔夫人反正也打算离开这座城市了，她大可以列出她的友人和敌人，毫无后顾之忧地、极尽所能地讽刺和攻击他们。因此，她在寻找这个人或者那个人颠倒黑白的原因的同时，也把这段时间以来的秘密观察和以前没有说出的对某人的厌恶都发泄了出来。 A torrent of epigram flowed over Bordeaux.Madame Evangelista was about to leave the city, and could safely scan her friends and enemies, caricature them and lash them as she pleased, with nothing to fear in return.Accordingly, she now gave vent to her secret observations and her latent dislikes as she sought for the reason why this or that person denied the shining of the sun at mid-day.
“不过，亲爱的，”吉亚斯侯爵夫人说道，“这种情况下，他在朗斯特拉克和年轻人混在一起——” “But, my dear,” said the Marquise de Gyas, “this stay of the count at Lanstrac, these parties given to young men under such circumstances—”
“唉！亲爱的，”贵妇人打断侯爵夫人的话说起来，“难道你认为我们会注重那些庸俗的繁文缛节吗？难道还能像锁一个试图逃跑的囚犯一样锁住保尔伯爵吗？难道你认为我该让警察看住他，以防所谓外省的阴谋诡计把他从我们身边夺走吗？” “Ah! my dear,” said the great lady, interrupting the marquise, “do you suppose that we adopt the pettiness of bourgeois customs?Is Count Paul held in bonds like a man who might seek to get away?Think you we ought to watch him with a squad of gendarmes lest some provincial conspiracy should get him away from us?”
“相信我，我亲爱的朋友，听你这一番话，我真是高兴多了——” “Be assured, my dearest friend, that it gives me the greatest pleasure to—”
此时，一个男仆进来打断了她的话，他报告保尔已经到了。像许多热恋中的人一样，保尔觉得骑上十二里的路来与纳塔莉共度一个小时是件快乐的事。他离开一起打猎的朋友们，穿着马靴，配着马刺，握着马鞭进来了。 Here her words were interrupted by a footman who entered the room to announce Paul.Like many lovers, Paul thought it charming to ride twelve miles to spend an hour with Natalie.He had left his friends while hunting, and came in booted and spurred, and whip in hand.
“亲爱的保尔，”纳塔莉说，“你还不知道你的到来会为这位女士带来什么答案。” “Dear Paul,” said Natalie, “you don’t know what an answer you are giving to madame.”
当保尔听到这些正在波尔多流传的谣言时，一点儿也不生气，反而禁不住笑了起来。 When Paul heard of the gossip that was current in Bordeaux, he laughed instead of being angry.
“这些无聊的人们也许发现不再有按照外省习俗操办的婚礼盛宴，也没有午间举行的教堂式婚礼，所以他们恼火了。嗯，我亲爱的母亲，”他亲吻了岳母的手，接着说下去，“我们会让他们安静的，签婚约那天，我们举行一场舞会，就像政府组织人们在爱丽舍田园大道广场上庆祝节日一样。那天我们将为我们亲爱的朋友们带来苦涩的快乐，这在外省可是件稀罕事。” “These worthy people have found out, perhaps, that there will be no wedding festivities, according to provincial usages, no marriage at mid-day in the church, and they are furious.Well, my dear mother,” he added, kissing her hand, “let us pacify them with a ball on the day when we sign the contract, just as the government flings a fete to the people in the great square of the Champs–Elysees, and we will give our dear friends the dolorous pleasure of signing a marriage-contract such as they have seldom heard of in the provinces.”
这件小事却有重大的意义。埃旺热利斯塔夫人要让全波尔多城的人都见证婚约的签署，并且要最后的奢侈铺张一次，好给社会上的那些荒谬的谣传迎头一击。 This little incident proved of great importance.Madame Evangelista invited all Bordeaux to witness the signature of the contract, and showed her intention of displaying in this last fete a luxury which should refute the foolish lies of the community.
这次舞会的准备时间超过了一个月，而这次的盛会也被称作“茶花盛会”。大量的茶花被摆设在楼梯间、前厅里和用餐室里。正好在这一个月里，有关不动产的限嗣继承的手续问题也办妥了，朗斯特拉克旁的那块土地也买了，舞会的通知也公开发布了，所有的猜忌都被驱散了。朋友和敌人都只一心在考虑这次盛宴的着装问题。 The preparations for this event required over a month, and it was called the fete of the camellias.Immense quantities of that beautiful flower were massed on the staircase, and in the antechamber and supper-room.During this month the formalities for constituting the entail were concluded in Paris; the estates adjoining Lanstrac were purchased, the banns were published, and all doubts finally dissipated.Friends and enemies thought only of preparing their toilets for the coming fete.
第一次争论中的导火索似乎也被这些忙碌的事宜淡化了，那次针锋相对的谈话中的言语和争论也被慢慢地淡忘了。无论是保尔还是他的岳母都不愿再回想起那些争论了。毕竟，就如埃旺热利斯塔夫人所言，难道这些不都是两位公证人的事情吗？ The time occupied by these events obscured the difficulties raised by the first discussion, and swept into oblivion the words and arguments of that stormy conference.Neither Paul nor his mother-inlaw continued to think of them.Were they not, after all, as Madame Evangelista had said, the affair of the two notaries?
但是当生活正顺风顺水时，突然回忆的声音敲响了你的警钟，也许敲得太晚了，那声音使你想起某件重要的事实，一个潜在的威胁——谁没碰到过这样的事呢？在签署婚约和举办舞会的那天早上，埃旺热利斯塔夫人在半睡半醒中，脑海中闪了一下这样的念头。当马蒂亚斯妥协同意索洛内提出的条件时，她说了一句“节外生枝”。此时，她的耳边似乎又听到一个声音在说同样的话。虽然埃旺热利斯塔夫人在生意方面没什么本事，但却头脑精明。她暗想道： But—to whom has it never happened, when life is in its fullest flow, to be suddenly changed by the voice of memory, raised, perhaps, too late, reminding us of some important new fact, some threatened danger?On the morning of the day when the contract was to be signed and the fete given, one of these flashes of the soul illuminated the mind of Madame Evangelista during the semi-somnolence of her waking hour.The words that she herself had uttered at the moment when Mathias acceded to Solonet’s conditions, “Questa coda non e di questo gatto,” were cried aloud in her mind by that voice of memory.In spite of her incapacity for business, Madame Evangelista’s shrewdness told her:—
“连如此聪明的马蒂亚斯都心平气和地接受条件了，他肯定看到在别的地方可以得到的补偿。” “If so clever a notary as Mathias was pacified, it must have been that he saw compensation at the cost of some one.”
而利益受损方也不可能是保尔，虽然她以前是这么希望的。是否她女儿的财产会成为这场战争的开销？她之前要求索洛内给她解释婚约中的细则条文，却没有想到如果她的利益受到严重侵害时该如何应对。这一天将对保尔·德马内维尔日后的夫妻生活有至关重要的影响，那么也应该就随之而来的外界情况给出必要的说明。 That some one could not be Paul, as she had blindly hoped.Could it be that her daughter’s fortune was to pay the costs of war?She resolved to demand explanations on the tenor of the contract, not reflecting on the course she would have to take in case she found her interests seriously compromised.This day had so powerful an influence on Paul de Manerville’s conjugal life that it is necessary to explain certain of the external circumstances which accompanied it.
埃旺热利斯塔夫人对这次令人眼花缭乱的盛宴不惜代价。大院里铺满了砾石，支起了帐篷，尽管是冬天，也用灌木装饰起来。从昂古莱姆到达克斯都很流行的茶花，所以也被用来铺满了楼梯和大厅。为了扩大用餐室和用来跳舞的舞厅，好几处墙体隔断都被事先拆除了。波尔多，一个因殖民者奢侈斗富而闻名的地方，正翘首盼望着仙境的降临。八点左右，由于这将是人们最后一次在这幢房子里讨论这次婚约了，爱看热闹的人们早早走出马车，在马车通道边排成了两侧人墙，迫不及待地等着观赏盛装打扮的贵妇们。在这即将签署婚约的时刻，人们的思维都沉浸于华丽的节日气氛；五颜六色的灯笼照亮了点缀用的灌木，庭院里客人的马车喧嚣不止。两位公证人和未婚夫妻以及他们的母亲一起用过晚膳。那天晚上，马蒂亚斯的得力手下负责客人的签到（同时也要防止婚约的内容被签到者偷窥到）。这个得力助手本人也是座上宾客之一。 Madame Evangelista had shrunk from no expense for this dazzling fete.The court-yard was gravelled and converted into a tent, and filled with shrubs, although it was winter.The camellias, of which so much had been said from Angouleme to Dax, were banked on the staircase and in the vestibules.Wall partitions had disappeared to enlarge the supper-room and the ball-room where the dancing was to be.Bordeaux, a city famous for the luxury of colonial fortunes, was on a tiptoe of expectation for this scene of fairyland.About eight o’clock, as the last discussion of the contract was taking place within the house, the inquisitive populace, anxious to see the ladies in full dress getting out of their carriages, formed in two hedges on either side of the porte-cochere.Thus the sumptuous atmosphere of a fete acted upon all minds at the moment when the contract was being signed, illuminating colored lamps lighted up the shrubs, and the wheels of the arriving guests echoed from the court-yard.The two notaries had dined with the bridal pair and their mother.Mathias’s head-clerk, whose business it was to receive the signatures of the guests during the evening (taking due care that the contract was not surreptitiously read by the signers), was also present at the dinner.
没有哪个新娘的妆容有纳塔莉那么漂亮。她穿着满是花边的绸缎，精致的头发卷成无数个小圈垂到颈脖上，就像一朵包在绿叶中的鲜花。埃旺热利斯塔夫人穿着一件樱桃红的羽绒长裙，这个颜色很配她的肤色，让她显得更加光彩动人。她有着黝黑的头发，深邃的眼珠，虽然是四十岁的女人了，但风韵犹存。她戴着珍珠项链，链子上挂着她家那颗祖传的钻石，显然是为了反驳那些诽谤她财务状况的谣言。 No bridal toilet was ever comparable with that of Natalie, whose beauty, decked with laces and satin, her hair coquettishly falling in a myriad of curls about her throat, resembled that of a flower encased in its foliage.Madame Evangelista, robed in a gown of cherry velvet, a color judiciously chosen to heighten the brilliancy of her skin and her black hair and eyes, glowed with the beauty of a woman at forty, and wore her pearl necklace, clasped with the “Discreto,” a visible contradiction to the late calumnies.
有关当时的场面，还有一点必须说明的是，保尔和纳塔莉正坐在壁炉边的沙发上，根本没注意听有人在朗读着婚约条例。两人无忧无虑，稚气十足，认为生活不过是一片万里无云的天空。他们年轻、富裕并且相互爱慕，不时低声谈论着什么。所爱之人即将成为他的合法妻子，保尔欣喜若狂。他亲吻着纳塔莉的指尖，轻轻地抚摸着她光洁的肩膀和波浪状的卷发，他却不想被外人发觉他这种尚不合法的大胆举止的快乐。纳塔莉把玩着保尔送她的孔雀羽毛屏风——按某些国家的迷信信仰来说，这样的礼品作为爱情信物是不吉利的，就如同送剪刀或其他利器一样。这样的礼品肯定会使人想起古神话中的帕尔卡。 To fully explain this scene, it is necessary to say that Paul and Natalie sat together on a sofa beside the fireplace and paid no attention to the reading of the documents.Equally childish and equally happy, regarding life as a cloudless sky, rich, young, and loving, they chattered to each other in a low voice, sinking into whispers.Arming his love with the presence of legality, Paul took delight in kissing the tips of Natalie’s fingers, in lightly touching her snowy shoulders and the waving curls of her hair, hiding from the eyes of others these joys of illegal emancipation.Natalie played with a screen of peacock’s feathers given to her by Paul,—a gift which is to love, according to superstitious belief in certain countries, as dangerous an omen as the gift of scissors or other cutting instruments, which recall, no doubt, the Parces of antiquity.
埃旺热利斯塔夫人坐在两位公证人旁边，正全神贯注地听着婚约条律的宣读。在宣读到大多由能干的索洛内起草的监护人账目这一段时，里面提及本来埃热利斯塔先生是留给女儿三百多万法郎的，但最后只剩下了颇具争议的一百一十五万六千法郎。听完这里，埃旺热利斯塔夫人对根本没注意听的小两口说： Seated beside the two notaries, Madame Evangelista gave her closest attention to the reading of the documents.After listening to the guardianship account, most ably written out by Solonet, in which Natalie’s share of the three million and more francs left by Monsieur Evangelista was shown to be the much-debated eleven hundred and fifty-six thousand, Madame Evangelista said to the heedless young couple:—
“喂，我的孩子们，听听啊，这可是你们的婚约。” “Come, listen, listen, my children; this is your marriage contract.”
助手喝了一杯冰水，索洛内和马蒂亚斯抹了抹鼻子。保尔和纳塔莉看了看面前的这四个人，稍微听了一下开头部分，然后又继续聊起来了。夫妻双方各自带来多少财产；假如死亡时无后裔总赠予是多少；无论有多少子女，法律允许范围内的以终身权益的方式赠予的四分之一和以现金方式赠予的四分之一各是多少；夫妻共有资金是多少；妻方首饰价值多少；夫方书籍、马匹价值多少；所有这些枯燥的数字都被一一宣读，大家也没怎么在意这些。接下来是不动产的限嗣继承的内容了。等宣读完所有条例，唯一剩下的只是签署婚约了。埃旺热利斯塔夫人要求知道这不动产的限嗣继承究竟会带来什么最终结果。 The clerk drank a glass of iced-water, Solonet and Mathias blew their noses, Paul and Natalie looked at the four personages before them, listened to the preamble, and returned to their chatter.The statement of the property brought by each party; the general deed of gift in the event of death without issue; the deed of gift of one-fourth in life-interest and one-fourth in capital without interest, allowed by the Code, whatever be the number of the children; the constitution of a common fund for husband and wife; the settlement of the diamonds on the wife, the library and horses on the husband, were duly read and passed without observations.Then followed the constitution of the entail.When all was read and nothing remained but to sign the contract, Madame Evangelista demanded to know what would be the ultimate effect of the entail.
“不动产的限嗣继承，夫人，”索洛内答道，“意味着一份财产不得转让，属于夫妻双方共同所有，最后这份财产将由一代一代的长子继承，但是长子无权分割其他财产。” “An entail, madam,” replied Solonet, “means an inalienable right to the inheritance of certain property belonging to both husband and wife, which is settled from generation to generation on the eldest son of the house, without, however, depriving him of his right to share in the division of the rest of the property.”
“那对我女儿的权力会有什么影响？” “What will be the effect of this on my daughter’s rights?”
马蒂亚斯总管眼看真相掩盖不住了，答道： Maitre Mathias, incapable of disguising the truth, replied:—
“夫人，不动产的限嗣继承财产是从夫妻两人的财产中单独抽取设立出来的一笔财产。未来如果妻子先死，留下几个子女，其中一个是男孩的话，马内维尔伯爵就欠这些子女三十六万法郎，他以终身权益方式的四分之一赠予和以现金方式的四分之一赠予都从这笔钱里扣除。这样的话，不算夫妻共同资产的利益和盈余，对子女的债务就减少到了十六万法郎。如果情况相反，男方先死，留下男性继承人，德马内维尔夫人也只有权支配三十六万法郎，还有她丈夫赠予她的那部分，因为赠予这部分是不包括在限嗣继承的不动产里的，另外还可支配夫妻共有资金所带来的利润和利息。” “Madame, an entail being an appanage, or portion of property set aside for this purpose from the fortunes of husband and wife, it follows that if the wife dies first, leaving several children, one of them a son, Monsieur de Manerville will owe those children three hundred and sixty thousand francs only, from which he will deduct his fourth in life-interest and his fourth in capital.Thus his debt to those children will be reduced to one hundred and sixty thousand francs, or thereabouts, exclusive of his savings and profits from the common fund constituted for husband and wife.If, on the contrary, he dies first, leaving a male heir, Madame de Manerville has a right to three hundred and sixty thousand francs only, and to her deeds of gift of such of her husband’s property as is not included in the entail, to the diamonds now settled upon her, and to her profits and savings from the common fund.”
马蒂亚斯总管的精明强干和深谋远虑如今已清楚显现了。 The effect of Maitre Mathias’s astute and far-sighted policy were now plainly seen.
”我的女儿就破产了。“埃旺热利斯塔夫人低声说道。 “My daughter is ruined,” said Madame Evangelista in a low voice.
一老一少两位公证人都听到了这句话。 The old and the young notary both overheard the words.
“破产，”马蒂亚斯温柔地答道，“为家庭建立一份坚不可摧的财富怎么能说是破产呢？” “Is it ruin,” replied Mathias, speaking gently, “to constitute for her family an indestructible fortune?”
年轻的公证人看到自己主顾脸上的表情，知道该轮到他用平和的语言来诠释这场灾难了。 The younger notary, seeing the expression of his client’s face, thought it judicious in him to state the disaster in plain terms.
“我们本来计算从他们身上搞到三十万法郎的，”他对愤愤不平的夫人耳语道，“但是他们却从我们这儿得到了八十万；为了孩子的利益，我们得损失四十万。现在你要么终止这项婚姻，要么继续下去。”索洛内最后说道。 “We tried to trick them out of three hundred thousand francs,” he whispered to the angry woman.“They have actually laid hold of eight hundred thousand; it is a loss of four hundred thousand from our interests for the benefit of the children.You must now either break the marriage off at once, or carry it through,” concluded Solonet.
紧接着的寂静甚至无法用语言来描述。马蒂亚斯总管以胜利者的姿势等着两人签约，而这两人之前还指望能盘剥他的主顾保尔一番。纳塔莉无法理解她自己已经损失了一半的身家，保尔也搞不懂马内维尔家得到了这一半的财产，两人仍然在说说笑笑。索洛内和埃旺热利斯塔夫人互相看着对方，一个努力地隐藏着自己毫不在乎的心思，另一个则在压抑着自己满腔的哀怨。 It is impossible to describe the moment of silence that followed.Maitre Mathias waited in triumph the signature of the two persons who had expected to rob his client.Natalie, not competent to understand that she had lost half her fortune, and Paul, ignorant that the house of Manerville had gained it, were laughing and chattering still.Solonet and Madame Evangelista gazed at each other; the one endeavoring to conceal his indifference, the other repressing the rush of a crowd of bitter feelings.
起初，她心中万分懊悔，责备保尔才是导致自己不诚实的起因，后来埃旺热利斯塔夫人打定主意，要做些见不得光的事，好把自己在作为监护人的时候犯的错都推到保尔身上，使保尔成为她的牺牲品。但是现在她才发现，原本以为自己旗开得胜，结果却是一败涂地，而真正的牺牲品则是她自己的女儿。一点儿好处都没得到，她明白自己算是被这个表面老实可靠的老头给耍了。无疑，她对这老头不再有任何敬意了。肯定是她隐秘的行为促使老马蒂亚斯想出这些条例，而马蒂亚斯接着又启发了保尔。想着都好可怕啊！即使马蒂亚斯至今还没有说明，只要婚约一签，这只老狐狸就会告诉他的主顾，当时是多么的危险，而现在已经安全地躲开。或者这么做，只是为了听到主顾的几声赞美。他会叫保尔提防这个阴险的女人，这个不惜降低身份、擅长阴谋诡计的女人。假使这女人已经完全地控制了保尔，他也会摧毁这个绝对统治！天性软弱的人们，一旦被人警告，就会变得执拗，而且不会再被拉拢了。一开始讨论婚约的时候，她就想抓住保尔的弱点，保尔不可能在婚约谈到八九不离十的时候来毁约的。但是如今，反而是她自己被牢牢地束缚了。如果是三个月前，保尔要推掉这门婚事是没什么真正困难的。但是如今，波尔多城的人都知道困难已经被公证人解决，婚礼通知已经昭告全城，婚礼也将马上举行，两家的友人也都来参加这次盛宴并见证婚约的签署。她怎么好在这个节骨眼上说推迟婚礼呢？那样的话，大家都会知道这次谈崩的原因。马蒂亚斯总管德高望重，大家肯定情愿相信马蒂亚斯的话，而不是她的话。那些造谣者更要变本加厉地跟她和她女儿做对了。不行，她不能这么做，她只有退步了！ After suffering in her own mind the struggles of remorse, after blaming Paul as the cause of her dishonesty, Madame Evangelista had decided to employ those shameful manoeuvres to cast on him the burden of her own unfaithful guardianship, considering him her victim.But now, in a moment, she perceived that where she thought she triumphed she was about to perish, and her victim was her own daughter.Guilty without profit, she saw herself the dupe of an honorable old man, whose respect she had doubtless lost.Her secret conduct must have inspired the stipulation of old Mathias; and Mathias must have enlightened Paul.Horrible reflection!Even if he had not yet done so, as soon as that contract was signed the old wolf would surely warn his client of the dangers he had run and had now escaped, were it only to receive the praise of his sagacity.He would put him on his guard against the wily woman who had lowered herself to this conspiracy; he would destroy the empire she had conquered over her son-inlaw!Feeble natures, once warned, turn obstinate, and are never won again.At the first discussion of the contract she had reckoned on Paul’s weakness, and on the impossibility he would feel of breaking off a marriage so far advanced.But now, she herself was far more tightly bound.Three months earlier Paul had no real obstacles to prevent the rupture; now, all Bordeaux knew that the notaries had smoothed the difficulties; the banns were published; the wedding was to take place immediately; the friends of both families were at that moment arriving for the fete, and to witness the contract.How could she postpone the marriage at this late hour?The cause of the rupture would surely be made known; Maitre Mathias’s stern honor was too well known in Bordeaux; his word would be believed in preference to hers.The scoffers would turn against her and against her daughter.No, she could not break it off; she must yield!
思前想后，这些残酷的想法使埃旺热利斯塔夫人觉得大脑就像一个喷水管，就要炸裂了。表面上她仍然保持着外交家的风度，她的下巴却如中风一样的颤抖起来。当初叶卡捷琳娜女王二世坐在皇座上，当着臣子的面被瑞典国王挑衅时，也是这个动作，以表达她的愤怒（和埃旺热利斯塔夫人此刻的情形如出一辙）。索洛内注意到了主顾这异常的表现，他知道这意味着一种致命的恨意，一场可怕的没有闪电的疾风骤雨即将到来。此时，埃旺热利斯塔夫人对她的女婿产生了一种难以泯灭的仇恨，这种仇恨的种子就来自于西班牙民族的本性。 These reflections, so cruelly sound, fell upon Madame Evangelista’s brain like a water-spout and split it.Though she still maintained the dignity and reserve of a diplomatist, her chin was shaken by that apoplectic movement which showed the anger of Catherine the Second on the famous day when, seated on her throne and in presence of her court (very much in the present circumstances of Madame Evangelista), she was braved by the King of Sweden.Solonet observed that play of the muscles, which revealed the birth of a mortal hatred, a lurid storm to which there was no lightning.At this moment Madame Evangelista vowed to her son-inlaw one of those unquenchable hatreds the seeds of which were left by the Moors in the atmosphere of Spain.
“先生，”她弯腰对着自己的公证人耳语道，“你曾把这些婚约条例称作胡说八道，我觉得没有什么可以说得更清楚了。” “Monsieur,” she said, bending to the ear of her notary, “you called that stipulation balderdash; it seems to me that nothing could have been more clear.”
“夫人，请允许我——” “Madame, allow me—”
“先生，”她丝毫不理会索洛内的插话，继续说道，“即使你在我们第一次交谈的时候没想到不动产的限嗣继承的后果，那么奇怪的是居然你在安静的书房里也没想到。这不应该是无能造成的吧。” “Monsieur,” she continued, paying no heed to his interruption, “if you did not perceive the effect of that entail at the time of our first conference, it is very extraordinary that it did not occur to you in the silence of your study.This can hardly be incapacity.”
年轻的公证人一边把他的主顾拉到隔壁房间，一边在心中暗想道： The young notary drew his client into the next room, saying to himself, as he did so:—
“从监护人账目上，我可以得到三千法郎，从婚约上得到三千法郎，卖房上得到六千法郎，总共是一万五——我可不能因为她的愤怒而泡汤了。” “I get a three-thousand franc fee for the guardianship account, three thousand for the contract, six thousand on the sale of the house, fifteen thousand in all—better not be angry.”
他关上门，像个生意人一样面无表情地看着埃旺热利斯塔夫人，开始说起来： He closed the door, cast on Madame Evangelista the cool look of a business man, and said:—
“夫人，为了您，我可是尽心竭力了，难道您真的准备用如此的言语来回报我的忠心不二吗？” “Madame, having, for your sake, passed—as I did—the proper limits of legal craft, do you seriously intend to reward my devotion by such language?”
“但是，先生——” “But, monsieur—”
“夫人，没错，我是没有算好这些赠予带来的影响。但是如若你不指望保尔做你的乘龙快婿，你大可不接受这些条例。婚约还没签。宴会照常，签字仪式可以推迟。在波尔多人面前丢脸也总比牺牲自己要好得多。” “Madame, I did not, it is true, calculate the effect of the deeds of gift.But if you do not wish Comte Paul for your son-inlaw you are not obliged to accept him.The contract is not signed.Give your fete, and postpone the signing.It is far better to brave Bordeaux than sacrifice yourself.”
“那我怎么为此事找个理由呢？更何况外界本来就有谣言说这桩婚事拖拖拉拉。” “How can I justify such a course to society, which is already prejudiced against us by the slow conclusion of the marriage?”
“可以说巴黎那边有了点儿小错，或是有些文件找不到了。”索洛内答道。 “By some error committed in Paris; some missing document not sent with the rest,” replied Solonet.
“但是朗斯特拉克附近的那块地不是已经买了吗？” “But those purchases of land near Lanstrac?”
“德马内维尔先生又没什么损失，他可以找个带着嫁妆的新娘。” “Monsieur de Manerville will be at no loss to find another bride and another dowry.”
“是的，他是丝毫无损，不过我们却是满盘皆输，一败涂地！” “Yes, he’ll lose nothing; but we lose all, all!”
“你吗？”索洛内答道，“如果联姻的目的是为了得到贵族的称号，那么你可以轻易地再找一个伯爵，不会花你很多钱的伯爵。” “You?” replied Solonet; “why, you can easily find another count who will cost you less money, if a title is the chief object of this marriage.”
“不，绝对不行！我们不能拿我们的声誉来冒险。我这是中圈套了，先生。全波尔多的人明天都会把这作为话柄的。我们可是作出过慎重承诺的。” “No, no! we can’t stake our honor in that way.I am caught in a trap, monsieur.All Bordeaux will ring with this tomorrow.Our solemn words are pledged—”
“你希望纳塔莉小姐以后生活幸福吧。” “You wish the happiness of Mademoiselle Natalie.”
“这是最重要的。” “Above all things.”
“在法国要幸福，”公证人说，“就是要做一家之主。如果她愿意，她能完全控制那个德马内维尔；他如此迟钝，什么都看不懂的。即使他现在还不信任你，但是他总会信任自己的妻子吧。他的妻子不就是属于你的人吗？只要你把手里的牌打好，伯爵的命运还是由你来控制的。” “To be happy in France,” said the notary, “means being mistress of the home.She can lead that fool of a Manerville by the nose if she chooses; he is so dull he has actually seen nothing of all this.Even if he now distrusts you, he will always trust his wife; and his wife is YOU, is she not?The count’s fate is still within your power if you choose to play the cards in your hand.”
“如果真如你所说的话，我真不知道如何向你表达我的谢意。”她情绪明显好转了，面颊微红地说道。 “If that were true, monsieur, I know not what I would not do to show my gratitude,” she said, in a transport of feeling that colored her cheeks.
“我们回大厅去吧，夫人，”索洛内说，“我说的，你可得仔细听好了。事后你愿意的话，再来骂我没用好了。” “Let us now return to the others, madame,” said Solonet.“Listen carefully to what I shall say; and then—you shall think me incapable if you choose.”
“我亲爱的朋友，”年轻的公证人回来后，对马蒂亚斯说，“虽说你业务能力精湛，不过你既没有考虑到德马内维尔总管身后万一无儿无女怎么办，也没有考虑到他身后只有女性继承人怎么办。无论上述哪种情况发生，限嗣继承的财产都仍然还在德马内维尔家，而且很可能引起家庭内部官司。因此我认为需要规定好，若是第一种情况，限嗣继承财产应纳入夫妻赠予财产。若是第二种情况，限嗣继承则被宣布无效废除。这一条款与妻子的利益息息相关。” “My dear friend,” said the young notary to Maitre Mathias, “in spite of your great ability, you have not foreseen either the case of Monsieur de Manerville dying without children, nor that in which he leaves only female issue.In either of those cases the entail would pass to the Manervilles, or, at any rate, give rise to suits on their part.I think, therefore, it is necessary to stipulate that in the first case the entailed property shall pass under the general deed of gift between husband and wife; and in the second case that the entail shall be declared void.This agreement concerns the wife’s interest.”
“这两种情况在我看来非常公正，”马蒂亚斯总管说，“至于批准的事，如果有需要，伯爵先生肯定会和司法部达成共识的。” “Both clauses seem to me perfectly just,” said Maitre Mathias.“As to their ratification, Monsieur le comte can, doubtless, come to an understanding with the chancellor, if necessary.”
索洛内拿起笔在婚约的空白处加上了这一至关重要的条例。保尔和纳塔莉都没怎么注意到这事。倒是当马蒂亚斯总管大声宣读这条新加条款时，埃旺热利斯塔夫人低下了眼睛。 Solonet took a pen and added this momentous clause on the margin of the contract.Paul and Natalie paid no attention to the matter; but Madame Evangelista dropped her eyes while Maitre Mathias read the added sentence aloud.
“现在我们签字吧。”母亲说道。 “We will now sign,” said the mother.
说这话时，埃旺热利斯塔夫人虽然压低了嗓音，但言语中却透露出她激动的情绪。她心中暗念道：“我女儿不会倾家荡产的——要破产的是他！我女儿将拥有姓氏、贵族称号和所有财产。如果那一天她发现自己不再爱保尔了，或说她难以抗拒地爱上另外一个男人了，保尔就得被驱赶出法国！我的女儿将变得自由、快乐而富裕。” The volume of voice which Madame Evangelista repressed as she uttered those words betrayed her violent emotion.She was thinking to herself: “No, my daughter shall not be ruined—but he!My daughter shall have the name, the title, and the fortune.If she should some day discover that she does not love him, that she loves another, irresistibly, Paul shall be driven out of France!My daughter shall be free, and happy, and rich.”
虽然马蒂亚斯总管善于分析利益得失，但是对人的情感却知之不多。他接受了埃旺热利斯塔夫人的话，以为这只是一种体面的“修改”，却没算到其实她是要宣战。在索洛内和他的助手的照看下，纳塔莉正在文献上一一签字署名，这是要花点时间的。趁这时间，马蒂亚斯把保尔拉到一旁，告诉他这些婚约条款将保证他将来无后顾之忧。 If Maitre Mathias understood how to analyze business interests, he knew little of the analysis of human passions.He accepted Madame Evangelista’s words as an honorable “amende,” instead of judging them for what they were, a declaration of war.While Solonet and his clerk superintended Natalie as she signed the documents,—an operation which took time,—Mathias took Paul aside and told him the meaning of the stipulation by which he had saved him from ultimate pain.
“整件事都办好了。婚约由我保管。但是婚约中包括一条钻石的收据，你得向她们要回来。公事还是得公办。钻石目前是在涨价，但以后或许会跌的。因为要买新的地皮，你可以借机把所有东西都变卖成现款。因此，伯爵先生，这件事上你可不要妇人之仁。手续办完之后，就要付第一笔款项了。总数是二十万法郎，把变卖钻石的钱算进去吧。这座房子即将被出售，可以用这个钱来付剩余的款项。如果你有勇气在未来的三年内只用五万法郎的话，你就可以存下二十万法郎来还你现在的债务。如果你在你的新土地上种点葡萄，你还能就此多得两万五千法郎。这样说来，你才算结了一门好亲事。” “The whole affair is now ‘en regle.’I hold the documents.But the contract contains a rescript for the diamonds; you must ask for them.Business is business.Diamonds are going up just now, but may go down.The purchase of those new domains justifies you in turning everything into money that you can.Therefore, Monsieur le comte, have no false modesty in this matter.The first payment is due after the formalities are over.The sum is two hundred thousand francs; put the diamonds into that.You have the lien on this house, which will be sold at once, and will pay the rest.If you have the courage to spend only fifty thousand francs for the next three years, you can save the two hundred thousand francs you are now obliged to pay.If you plant vineyards on your new estates, you can get an income of over twenty-five thousand francs upon them.You may be said, in short, to have made a good marriage.”
保尔动情地紧握住这个老朋友的手，这一举动正好被过来递笔给保尔的埃旺热莉斯塔夫人收在眼底。这更加证实了她的猜疑。她确信保尔和马蒂亚斯肯定是合起伙来欺骗她的。愤怒和仇恨使她热血澎湃。最糟的事情不过如此。 Paul pressed the hand of his old friend very affectionately, a gesture which did not escape Madame Evangelista, who now came forward to offer him the pen.Suspicion became certainty to her mind.She was confident that Paul and Mathias had come to an understanding about her.Rage and hatred sent the blood surging through her veins to her heart.The worst had come.
马蒂亚斯总管仔细地查看是否所有的文件都签字署名了，是否每页的眉脚都署上了各方的姓名。之后他看看保尔和他的岳母，发现他并没有打算提及钻石的事，于是他开口道： After verifying that all the documents were duly signed and the initials of the parties affixed to the bottom of the leaves, Maitre Mathias looked from Paul to his mother-inlaw, and seeing that his client did not intend to speak of the diamonds, he said:—
“你们如今已经是一家人了，我想交接钻石的事应该没有问题了吧。” “I do not suppose there can be any doubt about the transfer of the diamonds, as you are now one family.”
“既然是由德马内维尔先生负责监护人资金了，而且我们也不知道谁活得更长，还是由埃旺热利斯塔夫人交出钻石更符合规矩些。”索洛内说道。他认为此刻正好借机挑拨岳母与女婿的关系。 “It would be more regular if Madame Evangelista made them over now, as Monsieur de Manerville has become responsible for the guardianship funds, and we never know who may live or die,” said Solonet, who thought he saw in this circumstance fresh cause of anger in the mother-inlaw against the son-inlaw.
“噢！母亲，”保尔高声道，“这样做岂不是对我们的侮辱——过分循规蹈矩反而不公平，先生。”他对索洛内说。 “Ah! mother,” cried Paul, “it would be insulting to us all to do that,—‘Summum jus, summum injuria,’ monsieur,” he said to Solonet.
“我嘛，”埃旺热利斯塔夫人说道，她本就怒火中烧，眼见着马蒂亚斯总管拐弯抹角的就是要侮辱她，“如果你不接受这些钻石，我可得毁约了。” “And I,” said Madame Evangelista, led by the hatred now surging in her heart to see a direct insult to her in the indirect appeal of Maitre Mathias, “I will tear that contract up if you do not take them.”
她满腔怒火地离开了房间，这种怒火来自于摧毁一切的权利欲望，来自于无能为力的感觉所引发的疯狂。 She left the room in one of those furious passions which long for the power to destroy everything, and which the sense of impotence drives almost to madness.
“看在上帝的份上，把钻石收去吧，保尔，”纳塔莉俯身耳语道。“我母亲生气了，今晚我就会搞清楚是怎么回事，回头再告诉你。我们再安慰安慰她。” “For Heaven’s sake, take them, Paul,” whispered Natalie in his ear.“My mother is angry; I shall know why to-night, and I will tell you.We must pacify her.”
慢慢地夫人也平静下来了，她留下了随身佩戴的项链和耳环，把埃利·玛古斯估价为十五万法郎的珠宝首饰拿了出来。以前在办理遗产交接的时候，马蒂亚斯总管和索洛内也经常看到各种各样的钻石首饰，这一次检查着这些盒装的宝物时，他们也不禁惊叹不已。 Calmed by this first outburst, madame kept the necklace and earrings, which she was wearing, and brought the other jewels, valued at one hundred and fifty thousand francs by Elie Magus.Accustomed to the sight of family diamonds in all valuations of inheritance, Maitre Mathias and Solonet examined these jewels in their cases and exclaimed upon their duty.
“你可是一点儿损失都没有，伯爵先生。”索洛内说道，保尔听完也不好意思地脸红了。 “You will lose nothing, after all, upon the ‘dot,’ Monsieur le comte,” said Solonet, bringing the color to Paul’s face.
“是的，”马蒂亚斯说道，“这些珠宝够用来支付买地的第一笔款项了。” “Yes,” said Mathias, “these jewels will meet the first payment on the purchase of the new estate.”
“加上婚约的费用都够了，”索洛内补充道。 “And the costs of the contract,” added Solonet.
仇恨就像爱情一样，来源于生活细微，再细微的事情也能使其生长发芽。正如你爱一个人不会对他使坏，恨一个人也不会做一丁点儿对他有利的事。保尔不愿意接受这些珠宝，也不知道把这些珠宝盒放在哪里，真恨不得从窗户中扔出去。埃旺热利斯塔把他的尴尬认为是在假装正经。埃旺热利斯塔夫人盯着他看着，就好像在说：“从这里拿走你的财产就是了。” Hatred feeds, like love, on little things; the least thing strengthens it; as one beloved can do no evil, so the person hated can do no good.Madame Evangelista assigned to hypocrisy the natural embarrassment of Paul, who was unwilling to take the jewels, and not knowing where to put the cases, longed to fling them from the window.Madame Evangelista spurred him with a glance which seemed to say, “Take your property from here.”
“亲爱的纳塔莉，”保尔说，“把珠宝收到，这些都是你的啦，我送给你的。” “Dear Natalie,” said Paul, “put away these jewels; they are yours; I give them to you.”
纳塔莉把珠宝都锁好，放在桌子的抽屉里。此时院子里车水马龙，客厅里也已是人声鼎沸；纳塔莉和母亲必须得出场了。大厅里坐满了人，盛典开始了。 Natalie locked them into the drawer of a console.At this instant the noise of the carriages in the courtyard and the murmur of voices in the reception rooms became so loud that Natalie and her mother were forced to appear.The salons were filled in a few moments, and the fete began.
“度蜜月的时候记得趁机把钻石给卖了。”老公证人临走前嘱咐保尔道。 “Profit by the honeymoon to sell those diamonds,” said the old notary to Paul as he went away.
人们正等着舞会的正式开始，有些人正七嘴八舌地议论着这桩婚事，也有些人表达了对这对未婚夫妇未来前景的担忧。 While waiting for the dancing to begin, whispers went round about the marriage, and doubts were expressed as to the future of the promised couple.
“全部都安排妥当了？”城里一位有头有脸的人物对埃旺热利斯塔夫人问道。 “Is it finally arranged?” said one of the leading personages of the town to Madame Evangelista.
“有太多的文件要宣读和签署，恐怕我们来得太晚了，”她答道，“不过也是情有可原嘛。” “We had so many documents to read and sign that I fear we are rather late,” she replied; “but perhaps we are excusable.”
“我可什么都没听到。”纳塔莉向保尔伸出了手邀请他，准备开启舞会的序幕。 “As for me, I heard nothing,” said Natalie, giving her hand to her lover to open the ball.
“两个年轻人都爱花钱，他们母亲也不是节制他们的人。”一个遗孀说道。 “Both of those young persons are extravagant, and the mother is not of a kind to check them,” said a dowager.
“可是据说他们设立了一份不动产的限嗣继承，每年可带来五万法郎的收入。” “But they have founded an entail, I am told, worth fifty thousand francs a year.”
“哇！” “Pooh!”
“这还不是拜托我们尊敬的马蒂亚斯先生。”一个地区检察官说。“如果真是这么回事，肯定是他挽救了这个家庭的未来。” “In that I see the hand of our worthy Monsieur Mathias,” said a magistrate.“If it is really true, he has done it to save the future of the family.”
“纳塔莉太美丽了，梳妆打扮肯定不会马虎的。不出几年，”一位年轻妇女说道，“我敢说，在这个家里，德马内维尔先生是快活不下去的。” “Natalie is too handsome not to be horribly coquettish.After a couple of years of marriage,” said one young woman, “I wouldn’t answer for Monsieur de Manerville’s happiness in his home.”
“那到时，时尚之尊的称号就得加注啦。”索洛内笑着说道。 “The Pink of Fashion will then need staking,” said Solonet, laughing.
“你们不觉得埃旺热利斯塔夫人看起来不太高兴吗？”有人问道。 “Don’t you think Madame Evangelista looks annoyed?” asked another.
“亲爱的，刚刚有人跟我说，她每年只有两万五千法郎可供开销了，那对她意味着什么？” “But, my dear, I have just been told that all she is able to keep is twenty-five thousand francs a year, and what is that to her?”
“窘迫吧！” “Penury!”
“是啊，为了纳塔莉，她可是没剩几个子啦。德马内维尔先生真是苛求得厉害呀——” “Yes, she has robbed herself for Natalie.Monsieur de Manerville has been so exacting—”
“相当厉害！”索洛内总管插嘴道，“但是不久以后他将成为法兰西贵族院的议员。摩冷古家族和德帕米埃尔主教都将利用他们的影响力来帮他。他可是属于圣日耳曼的人。”“噢！那里只是接待他而已，仅此而已。”一位曾试图把女儿嫁给保尔的女士说道，“埃旺热利斯塔小姐是商人的女儿，不可能为他打开科隆的牧师会礼堂的大门的！” “Extremely exacting,” put in Maitre Solonet.“But before long he will be peer of France.The Maulincours and the Vidame de Pamiers will use their influence.He belongs to the faubourg Saint–Germain.”“Oh! he is received there, and that is all,” said a lady, who had tried to obtain him as a son-inlaw.“Mademoiselle Evangelista, as the daughter of a merchant, will certainly not open the doors of the chapter-house of Cologne to him!”
“她可是卡萨－雷阿尔公爵的外甥女啊。” “She is grand-niece to the Duke of Casa–Reale.”
“那只是从母亲的血统来说而已！” “Through the female line!”
谈话到此，已经没有什么好说下去的了。打牌的上桌了，年轻人跳舞去了，晚餐也开始供应了。舞会一直持续到黎明，等第一道曙光映在了窗户上时才慢慢地散场了。 The topic was presently exhausted.The card-players went to the tables, the young people danced, the supper was served, and the ball was not over till morning, when the first gleams of the coming day whitened the windows.
送别了最后一个走的保尔，埃旺热利斯塔夫人走进了她女儿的房间；她自己的房间被建筑师用来扩建场地迎接这次舞会。尽管纳塔莉和母亲都睡意朦胧，趁着单独相处，还是谈了几句。 Having said adieu to Paul, who was the last to go away, Madame Evangelista went to her daughter’s room; for her own had been taken by the architect to enlarge the scene of the fete.Though Natalie and her mother were overcome with sleep, they said a few words to each other as soon as they were alone.
“跟我讲讲，亲爱的妈妈，你刚刚是怎么了？” “Tell me, mother dear, what was the matter with you?”
“我的宝贝，我今天晚上算是明白了，作为一个母亲，为了孩子可以作出多大的让步。你不了解生意，你也不知道别人是如何怀疑我的德行。我冒着名誉扫地的危险忍气吞声，都是为了能让你幸福。” “My darling, I learned this evening to what lengths a mother’s tenderness can go.You know nothing of business, and you are ignorant of the suspicions to which my integrity has been exposed.I have trampled my pride under foot, for your happiness and my reputation were at stake.”
“你是在说钻石的事吗？可怜的小伙子，他哭了；他本不想要的，钻石都由我保存的。” “Are you talking of the diamonds?Poor boy, he wept; he did not want them; I have them.”
“睡吧，孩子。这些事我们醒后再谈吧，因为，”她叹道，“你我都有事要办，我们之间已经出现第三个人了。” “Sleep now, my child.We will talk business when we wake—for,” she added, sighing, “you and I have business now; another person has come between us.”
“啊！我亲爱的母亲大人，保尔绝不会成为我们幸福的障碍的，绝不会。”纳塔莉呢喃着睡着了。 “Ah! my dear mother, Paul will never be an obstacle to our happiness, yours and mine,” murmured Natalie, as she went to sleep.
“我可怜的宝贝！她根本不知道那个人已经掏空了她的家财。” “Poor darling! she little knows that the man has ruined her.”
贪婪的念头一出现就很难抑制，埃旺热利斯塔夫人的灵魂也被这念头所俘虏，这是上了点年纪的人的通病。她脑子中想的都是为了女儿的利益，恢复她丈夫留下的财产。她告诉自己，这事关她的声誉。以前她对金钱毫不在意，肆意挥霍。但是此刻，她对女儿的钟爱使她顿时变得精明而精于算计了。之前她已经拿一部分钱买了国债，现值八十法郎。她决定把剩下的资金也拿出去投资。激情往往能在片刻之间转变一个人的性格。一个口无遮掩的人能变成一个外交家，一个懦夫能突然成为一个勇士。仇恨使惯于奢侈的女人变成了铁公鸡。有机会或者运气好的话，复仇计划还是能实现的。虽然现在这个计划还不明朗，比较模糊，但将会在她脑海中渐渐成熟。她一边慢慢地沉睡过去，一边喃喃地说着：“就在明天！”一个无法解释的现象是，正如所有的思想家一样，在睡梦中她整理了思路，想出了一些主意，并对其进行了分类，她准备以此来主宰保尔未来的生活。她想出了一个完整的计划，并将在第二天一开始就正式实施。 Madame Evangelista’s soul was seized at that moment with the first idea of avarice, a vice to which many become a prey as they grow aged.It came into her mind to recover in her daughter’s interest the whole of the property left by her husband.She told herself that her honor demanded it.Her devotion to Natalie made her, in a moment, as shrewd and calculating as she had hitherto been careless and wasteful.She resolved to turn her capital to account, after investing a part of it in the Funds, which were then selling at eighty francs.A passion often changes the whole character in a moment; an indiscreet person becomes a diplomatist, a coward is suddenly brave.Hate made this prodigal woman a miser.Chance and luck might serve the project of vengeance, still undefined and confused, which she would now mature in her mind.She fell asleep, muttering to herself, “To-morrow!”By an unexplained phenomenon, the effects of which are familiar to all thinkers, her mind, during sleep, marshalled its ideas, enlightened them, classed them, prepared a means by which she was to rule Paul’s life, and showed her a plan which she began to carry out on that very tomorrow.
第五章 婚约——第三日 CHAPTER V THE MARRIAGE CONTRACT—THIRD DAY
舞会上的激动虽然暂时驱散了保尔的忧愁，但是当他一个人躺在床上时，这种忧愁又卷土重来，开始折磨他了。 Though the excitement of the fete had driven from Paul’s mind the anxious thoughts that now and then assailed it, when he was alone with himself and in his bed they returned to torment him.
“依我看来，”他寻思道，“如果不是好心的马蒂亚斯来帮忙，我早就被我岳母给耍了。哎，这种事可信吗？是什么样的利益关系驱使她来欺骗我呢？难道我们不是应该把财产合并在一起共同生活吗？罢了，罢了，为什么要担心这些呢？两天之后，纳塔莉将成为我的妻子，我们的财产关系已经完全确定了，我们之间不会有任何障碍。随它去吧——不过我以后还是得多加小心。要是马蒂亚斯说的是对的可怎么办？嗯，如果真如他所说的话，我婚后就没必要跟岳母共同生活。” “It seems to me,” he said to himself, “that without that good Mathias my mother-inlaw would have tricked me.And yet, is that believable?What interest could lead her to deceive me?Are we not to join fortunes and live together?Well, well, why should I worry about it?In two days Natalie will be my wife, our money relations are plainly defined, nothing can come between us.Vogue la galere—Nevertheless, I’ll be upon my guard.Suppose Mathias was right?Well, if he was, I’m not obliged to marry my mother-inlaw.”
第二次交锋过后，保尔的前途已经被彻底改变了，但是他自己却毫无察觉。随着这场联姻而来到他身边的二人中，最聪明的那个如今已经成为他的死敌，而且正在考虑着如何保全自己的利益呢。克里奥尔人的天性使他的岳母与其他妇女大相径庭，保尔根本看不出他岳母的高深手段。克里奥尔人的本性非常与众不同，智力方面来源于欧洲，不合逻辑的暴力和激情来源于热带，对世间善恶的冷漠无睹来源于东方——这种优雅的本性同时也是极其危险的，正如一个无人看管的小孩一样危险。克里奥尔妇女就如同一个小孩，任何她想要的东西必须马上得到。她可以烧掉一个房子，仅仅是为了煮熟一个鸡蛋。惯于安逸舒适的生活，她很少动脑子思考，但是一旦激情迸发，她就思前想后。她还处于襁褓的时候就生活在黑人当中，她有着黑人的恶毒，但有时也像黑人一样幼稚和平和。像黑人和小孩一样，当她想要拥有一件物品时，她的欲望会越来越强烈，直到她得到为止。多么奇怪的一个善恶体的结合啊！西班牙的天性在埃旺热利斯塔夫人身上得到了强化，而她在法国的经历又给罩上了一层彬彬有礼的光环。 In this second battle of the contract Paul’s future had completely changed in aspect, though he was not aware of it.Of the two persons whom he was marrying, one, the cleverest, was now his mortal enemy, and meditated already withdrawing her interests from the common fund.Incapable of observing the difference that a Creole nature placed between his mother-inlaw and other women, Paul was far from suspecting her craftiness.The Creole nature is apart from all others; it derives from Europe by its intellect, from the tropics by the illogical violence of its passions, from the East by the apathetic indifference with which it does, or suffers, either good or evil, equally,—a graceful nature withal, but dangerous, as a child is dangerous if not watched.Like a child, the Creole woman must have her way immediately; like a child, she would burn a house to boil an egg.In her soft and easy life she takes no care upon her mind; but when impassioned, she thinks of all things.She has something of the perfidy of the Negroes by whom she has been surrounded from her cradle, but she is also as naive and even, at times, as artless as they.Like them and like the children, she wishes doggedly for one thing with a growing intensity of desire, and will brood upon that idea until she hatches it.A strange assemblage of virtues and defects!which her Spanish nature had strengthened in Madame Evangelista, and over which her French experience had cast the glaze of its politeness.
这种性格由于幸福的婚姻而潜伏了十六年，之后又被社交生活的琐事所占据。之前的第一次仇恨已经揭示出了这种性格的力量，如今它就如同大火一样再次苏醒了；在生命中的这个时刻，她正在失去自己最宝贵的感情，并且需要另一个因素来消耗她多余的精力，性格的火焰燃烧得更烈了。她对纳塔莉的影响只剩下三天了！战败了的埃旺热利斯塔夫人觉得只剩一天了，一个女儿完全呆在母亲身边的最后一天。只要一言半语，这个克里奥尔性格的女人就能影响两个人的一生。而这两个人正打算去经历巴黎社会的荆棘小路和满是灰尘的大道，因为纳塔莉完全盲目地信任母亲。只消一条建议，对一个如此恭顺的人会产生多么深远的影响啊！单单一通言语就能决定这些人的未来前程。没有任何法规和人类的法律可以阻止恶语伤人。这就是社会司法的漏洞，就体现在上层社会和广大民众之间道德习俗的差异上，一个坦率，另一个虚伪；一个兵刃相见，一个恶语相加；一个被判死刑，另一个却能逍遥法外。 This character, slumbering in married happiness for sixteen years, occupied since then with the trivialities of social life, this nature to which a first hatred had revealed its strength, awoke now like a conflagration; at the moment of the woman’s life when she was losing the dearest object of her affections and needed another element for the energy that possessed her, this flame burst forth.Natalie could be but three days more beneath her influence!Madame Evangelista, vanquished at other points, had one clear day before her, the last of those that a daughter spends beside her mother.A few words, and the Creole nature could influence the lives of the two beings about to walk together through the brambled paths and the dusty high-roads of Parisian society, for Natalie believed in her mother blindly.What far-reaching power would the counsel of that Creole nature have on a mind so subservient!The whole future of these lives might be determined by one single speech.No code, no human institution can prevent the crime that kills by words.There lies the weakness of social law; in that is the difference between the morals of the great world and the morals of the people: one is frank, the other hypocritical; one employs the knife, the other the venom of ideas and language; to one death, to the other impunity.
第二天快到中午的时候，埃旺热利斯塔夫人正半卧在纳塔莉的床沿上。醒来以后，她们拥抱着，一起回忆起她们以前幸福快乐的生活；在共同的生活中，她们感情和谐，情投意合，快乐地享受着这一切。 The next morning, about mid-day, Madame Evangelista was half seated, half lying on the edge of her daughter’s bed.During that waking hour they caressed and played together in happy memory of their loving life; a life in which no discord had ever troubled either the harmony of their feelings, the agreement of their ideas, or the mutual choice and enjoyment of their pleasures.
“可怜的小宝贝！”母亲动情地留下了眼泪说道，“你的每一个愿望，我都是尽力满足的。明晚你就要属于另外一个男人了，一个你必须俯首听命的男人。一想到这个，我就情不自禁地为你感到悲哀。” “Poor little darling!” said the mother, shedding true tears, “how can I help being sorrowful when I think that after I have fulfilled your every wish during your whole life you will belong, tomorrow night, to a man you must obey?”
“哦，我亲爱的妈妈，您说要对他俯首听命！”纳塔莉轻轻地摇了摇头，优雅地表示出自己对此的不赞同，“您开玩笑吧，”她接着说道，“父亲不是总是满足您所有的要求吗？为什么不呢？他爱您。同样保尔也爱我。” “Oh, my dear mother, as for obeying!—” and Natalie made a little motion of her head which expressed a graceful rebellion.“You are joking,” she continued.“My father always gratified your caprices; and why not? he loved you.And I am loved, too.”
“是的，保尔是对你有些爱意。但是，如果一个妇女不注意的话，没有什么东西比夫妻之间的爱情消失得更快了。一个妻子对她丈夫有多大的影响完全取决于她开始怎么对他。你需要人给你提好建议。” “Yes, Paul has a certain love for you.But if a married woman is not careful nothing more rapidly evaporates than conjugal love.The influence a wife ought to have over her husband depends entirely on how she begins with him.You need the best advice.”
“不过您会跟我一起生活啊。” “But you will be with us.”
“有可能，我的孩子。昨晚舞会时，我就考虑了我跟你们住一起这回事。如果我的存在会给你带来伤害，如果你作为妻子建立权威的一点一滴的行为都被人归结于我的影响，你的家庭将变成地狱。只要一看到你丈夫微微皱眉，像我这么高傲的人肯定会马上离开这个家的。我认为，与其被人赶出去，不如从不踏进去更好。如果你丈夫引起我们之间的不和，我是决不会原谅他的。然而，只要你能成为这个家的女主人，你丈夫和你的关系如同你父亲和我的关系一样，这种危险就无需害怕了。这样是明智的策略。不过你这样的年轻人心肠软，也许不忍心这么做。但是你必须拥有家中的绝对主动权，这也是你幸福的必备条件。” “Possibly, my child.Last night, while the ball was going on, I reflected on the dangers of our being together.If my presence were to do you harm, if the little acts by which you ought slowly, but surely, to establish your authority as a wife should be attributed to my influence, your home would become a hell.At the first frown I saw upon your husband’s brow I, proud as I am, should instantly leave his house.If I were driven to leave it, better, I think, not to enter it.I should never forgive your husband if he caused trouble between us.Whereas, when you have once become the mistress, when your husband is to you what your father was to me, that danger is no longer to be feared.Though this wise policy will cost your young and tender heart a pang, your happiness demands that you become the absolute sovereign of your home.”
“那么，妈妈，您刚刚不是说我要听命于他吗？” “Then why, mamma, did you say just now I must obey him?”
“我亲爱的小姑娘，一个妻子想要统治家庭，首先她得摆出一副随从丈夫的样子。如果没人告诉过你这个，你一气之下的反抗就可能自毁前程。保尔是个意志软弱的小伙子，他也许会听从一个朋友的支配，甚至被另外一个女人控制，而那个女人会令你吃尽苦头。要避免这样的灾难，一开始你就得掌握住他。与其让别人来支配他，不如让你来支配他岂不更好？” “My dear little daughter, in order that a wife may rule, she must always seem to do what her husband wishes.If you were not told this you might by some impulsive opposition destroy your future.Paul is a weak young man; he might allow a friend to rule him; he might even fall under the dominion of some woman who would make you feel her influence.Prevent such disasters by making yourself from the very start his ruler.Is it not better that he be governed by you than by others?”
“是的，那是当然，”纳塔莉说，“我只想让他幸福。” “Yes, certainly,” said Natalie.“I should think only of his happiness.”
“宝贝，我的特权就是只为你着想。只是希望在这个你必须掌舵的暗礁遍布的关键时刻，不要没有指南针。” “And it is my privilege, darling, to think only of yours, and to wish not to leave you at so crucial a moment without a compass in the midst of the reefs through which you must steer.”
“但是，亲爱的母亲，只要我们合力，不就足够强大吗？那样的话，即使跟他住一起，也无需害怕他不高兴。保尔是爱你的，妈妈。” “But, dearest mother, are we not strong enough, you and I, to stay together beside him, without having to fear those frowns you seem to dread.Paul loves you, mamma.”
噢！噢！他对我的恐惧胜过爱。今天你仔细看好了，只要我跟他说你们去巴黎，我不跟着。他无论怎么掩饰，内心的欢乐还是能看得出。” Oh !Oh! He fears me more than he loves me.Observe him carefully today when I tell him that I shall let you go to Paris without me, and you will see on his face, no matter what pains he takes to conceal it, his inward joy.”
“为什么他会有这种感觉呢？” “Why should he feel so?”
