“为什么？亲爱的孩子！我要当着你的面跟他说这个。” “Why? Dear child!I will tell that to himself, and before you.”
“不过如果我提出结婚就一定要跟你同住呢？”纳塔莉追问道。 “But suppose I marry on condition that you do not leave me?” urged Natalie.
“我们肯定得分开的，”她母亲答复道，“还有一些顾虑大大地改变了我的未来。我现在已经没什么钱了。你们在巴黎将过上如意的日子，我跟你们在一起的话，就得把我剩下的那点财产都花掉。然而，如果我去朗斯特拉克，我既能照看你们的产业，又能恢复我的财产，只要我节约点儿。” “Our separation is necessary,” replied her mother.“Several considerations have greatly changed my future.I am now poor.You will lead a brilliant life in Paris, and I could not live with you suitably without spending the little that remains to me.Whereas, if I go to Lanstrac, I can take care of your property there and restore my fortune by economy.”
“你，妈妈！你节约！”纳塔莉笑着喊起来，“现在还不是过老祖母生活的时候。什么嘛！你就是因为这些原因离开我吗？亲爱的妈妈，也许你看保尔觉得有点儿笨头笨脑的，但是他绝不是一个计较钱财、贪婪的人。” “You, mamma! You practise economy!” cried Natalie, laughing.“Don’t begin to be a grandmother yet.What! do you mean to leave me for such reasons as those?Dear mother, Paul may seem to you a trifle stupid, but he is not one atom selfish or grasping.”
“唉！”夫人叹道，语调中大有哀怨，让女孩听了心慌意乱，“那番有关婚约的讨论使我疑心重重。我对他是有顾虑的——不过不要担心，亲爱的孩子，”她搂过女儿的颈脖，轻吻了一下说道，“我不会丢下你一个人的。什么时候我回来不会引起你们夫妻的不快，什么时候保尔能正确地评判我，我就回来，到时我们又能过上我们幸福的小生活，晚上能好好地倾吐秘密——” “Ah!” replied Madame Evangelista, in a tone of voice big with suggestions which made the girl’s heart throb, “those discussions about the contract have made me distrustful.I have my doubts about him—But don’t be troubled, dear child,” she added, taking her daughter by the neck and kissing her.“I will not leave you long alone.Whenever my return can take place without making difficulty between you, whenever Paul can rightly judge me, we will begin once more our happy little life, our evening confidences—”
“噢！妈妈，没有你的纳塔莉，你可怎么活啊？” “Oh! Mother, how can you think of living without your Natalie?”
“那是因为，亲爱的，我活着都是为了你。作为一个母亲，只要一想到能为你带来未来的幸福，我就心满意足了。” “Because, dear angel, I shall live for her.My mother’s heart will be satisfied in the thought that I contribute, as I ought, to your future happiness.”
“可是，我亲爱的、可爱的妈妈，我就必须马上跟保尔独自生活了吗？我以后怎么办？会发生什么样的事？我必须做些什么？什么样的事我一定不能做？” “But, my dear, adorable mother, must I be alone with Paul, here, now, all at once?What will become of me? what will happen? what must I do? what must I not do?”
“可怜的孩子！难道你认为第一次战役后我就会丢下你不管吗？我们会像热恋中的人一样，每周写三封信。这样我们才能长期地呆在对方的心里。你发生什么事，我都会知道。我还能使你免遭厄运。而且如果我从不去看望你们，也太荒谬了；那不是明摆着说我不喜欢和不尊重你的丈夫嘛；我每年都会在巴黎跟你们一起呆上一两个月的。” “Poor child! do you think that I would utterly abandon you to your first battle?We will write to each other three times a week like lovers.We shall thus be close to each other’s hearts incessantly.Nothing can happen to you that I shall not know, and I can save you from all misfortune.Besides, it would be too ridiculous if I never went to see you; it would seem to show dislike or disrespect to your husband; I will always spend a month or two every year with you in Paris.”
“一个人，一个人，那我岂不是一个人跟他在一起了！”纳塔莉恐惧地打断了母亲的话。 “Alone, already alone, and with him!” cried Natalie in terror, interrupting her mother.
“但是你不是希望做他妻子吗？” “But you wish to be his wife?”
“是的，我是这么想的。可是告诉我，我应该怎么做——您跟父亲在一起时，是高兴做什么就做什么的。您是深谙其道的，您说什么，我都会听的。” “Yes, I wish it.But tell me how I should behave,—you, who did what you pleased with my father.You know the way; I’ll obey you blindly.”
埃旺热利斯塔夫人亲了女儿的前额。她巴不得有这样的请求。 Madame Evangelista kissed her daughter’s forehead.She had willed and awaited this request.
“孩子，我会给你忠告，不过你还是得随机应变。每个男人都是不一样的。我的意思是，从道德层面讲，一个男人与另一个男人的差异就如同狮子和青蛙一样巨大。我今天怎么可能知道你明天会遇到什么事情呢？不可能知道的。因此我只能对你的行为举止提些泛泛的建议。” “Child, my counsels must adept themselves to circumstances.All men are not alike.The lion and the frog are not more unlike than one man compared with another,—morally, I mean.Do I know today what will happen to you tomorrow?No; therefore I can only give you general advice upon the whole tenor of your conduct.”
“亲爱的母亲，告诉我，快点儿把您知道的都讲给我听。” “Dear mother, tell me, quick, all that you know yourself.”
“首先，我亲爱的孩子，那些希望守住丈夫的心的已婚妇女的失败原因——”，她说到这里插了一句，“守住他们的心和控制好他们是一码子事——哦，夫妻不和的首要原因是两人整天厮守在一起，这种情况在旧时是不存在的，而是近些年来，随着组建家庭的潮流才进入这个国家的。大革命以后，中产阶级的风俗习惯影响了贵族家庭。这种不幸来源于他们中的一个叫卢梭的作家。他是个臭名昭著的异教徒，满脑子都是反社会的念头。我也不知道他怎么说的，反正他能把最荒谬的事情说得头头是道。他宣扬所有的女子都拥有同样的权利和能力。他认为生活在这样的社会里，我们应该服从自己的天性——哪怕是西班牙贵族的妻子，你我这样的人，似乎跟普通妇女都差不多！从那以后，养尊处优的妇女也开始自己给孩子喂奶，亲自教育女儿，还得足不出户。生活有太多事情要做，以致于毫无幸福可言——因为，像我们这样和谐共处、如同朋友一样是个例外。夫妻长相厮守，就像父母和子女朝夕相处一样危险。这个万能规律以外幸存下来的爱情不多。所以我说，你得在你自己和保尔之间装上社交的篱笆。去参加舞会，去听听歌剧，上午散步，晚上在外面就餐，多出门拜访朋友，反正就是不要跟你丈夫相处太久。这样你才对他有吸引力。两个人只凭感情而打算携手终老，感情最终会耗尽的。冷漠、厌倦和反感将接踵而来。当感情枯萎时，你能怎么办呢？记住，感情一旦被浇灭就只会变成冷漠和蔑视。所以你得青春常驻，对他永远有新鲜感。他也许会使你感到厌倦——这种事经常发生的——但是你决不能使他对你感到厌倦。心中烦恼而不动声色，具备这个能力是一切物种中掌握力量的一个先决条件。打理好财产和干家务活并不会给你带来更多的幸福。如果你不能和丈夫一起分享自己的社交兴趣，如果你不能让他一直感到愉悦，那么你将陷入一种令人恐惧的死气沉沉中。然后爱情的低迷期就到了。反正一个男人总是会爱上令他快乐、使他幸福的女子。给予幸福和接受幸福是女性行为的两条原则，其中却隔着一条鸿沟。” “In the first place, my dear child, the cause of the failure of married women who desire to keep their husbands’ hearts—and,” she said, making a parenthesis, “to keep their hearts and rule them is one and the same thing—Well, the principle cause of conjugal disunion is to be found in perpetual intercourse, which never existed in the olden time, but which has been introduced into this country of late years with the mania for family.Since the Revolution the manners and customs of the bourgeois have invaded the homes of the aristocracy.This misfortune is due to one of their writers, Rousseau, an infamous heretic, whose ideas were all anti-social and who pretended, I don’t know how, to justify the most senseless things.He declared that all women had the same rights and the same faculties; that living in a state of society we ought, nevertheless, to obey nature—as if the wife of a Spanish grandee, as if you or I had anything in common with the women of the people!Since then, well-bred women have suckled their children, have educated their daughters, and stayed in their own homes.Life has become so involved that happiness is almost impossible,—for a perfect harmony between natures such as that which has made you and me live as two friends is an exception.Perpetual contact is as dangerous for parents and children as it is for husband and wife.There are few souls in which love survives this fatal omnipresence.Therefore, I say, erect between yourself and Paul the barriers of society; go to balls and operas; go out in the morning, dine out in the evenings, pay visits constantly, and grant but little of your time to your husband.By this means you will always keep your value to him.When two beings bound together for life have nothing to live upon but sentiment, its resources are soon exhausted, indifference, satiety, and disgust succeed.When sentiment has withered what will become of you?Remember, affection once extinguished can lead to nothing but indifference or contempt.Be ever young and ever new to him.He may weary you,—that often happens,—but you must never weary him.The faculty of being bored without showing it is a condition of all species of power.You cannot diversify happiness by the cares of property or the occupations of a family.If you do not make your husband share your social interests, if you do not keep him amused you will fall into a dismal apathy.Then begins the SPLEEN of love.But a man will always love the woman who amuses him and keeps him happy.To give happiness and to receive it are two lines of feminine conduct which are separated by a gulf.”
“亲爱的母亲，我正听着呢，但是我不明白您究竟是什么意思。” “Dear mother, I am listening to you, but I don’t understand one word you say.”
“如果你深爱着保尔，以致于他说什么你都照做，如果你使你的幸福完全取决于他，那你未来的生活就完了；你永远成不了家里的主人，再怎么劝诫你也是无济于事的。” “If you love Paul to the extent of doing all he asks of you, if you make your happiness depend on him, all is over with your future life; you will never be mistress of your home, and the best precepts in the world will do you no good.”
“您这样说就好懂多了，不过我虽然明白了规矩，却还不会应用。”纳塔莉笑着说，“我已经懂了理论，总会有机会实践的吧。” “That is plainer; but I see the rule without knowing how to apply it,” said Natalie, laughing.“I have the theory; the practice will come.”
“我可怜的妮妮，”母亲想到女儿就要出嫁了，流下了发自肺腑的眼泪，说道，“生活中发生的事情会教你的——”她停了一下，母女两人真诚地拥抱在一起，她接着说道，“记住，我的纳塔莉，我们女人有自己的命运，正如男人有他们自己的使命一样。女人生来就是要见识世界，成为一个魅力无穷的女主人，正如男人生来就要当将军或诗人一样。你的使命就是讨人欢心。你所受的教育也使你适于社交场合。如今，应该教育女人去广交朋友，正如以前教育她们要呆在闺房之中一样。你生来不是做生育机器或家庭主妇的。如果你要生小孩，我希望不要生得太早，破坏了你的身材。只有中产阶级才一结婚就生儿育女。结婚后两到三年再生育，是比较好的；女管家和私人教师会负责抚养教育他们。你，就当你的贵妇，代表家庭奢华和享乐的贵妇。不过记住一件事——你的能干必须只能在迎合男人的自尊心上表现出来，在大事上你得隐藏你的本领。” “My poor Ninie,” replied the mother, who dropped an honest tear at the thought of her daughter’s marriage, “things will happen to teach it to you—And,” she continued, after a pause, during which the mother and daughter held each other closely embraced in the truest sympathy, “remember this, my Natalie: we all have our destiny as women, just as men have their vocation as men.A woman is born to be a woman of the world and a charming hostess, as a man is born to be a general or a poet.Your vocation is to please.Your education has formed you for society.In these days women should be educated for the salon as they once were for the gynoecium.You were not born to be the mother of a family or the steward of a household.If you have children, I hope they will not come to spoil your figure on the morrow of your marriage; nothing is so bourgeois as to have a child at once.If you have them two or three years after your marriage, well and good; governesses and tutors will bring them up.YOU are to be the lady, the great lady, who represents the luxury and the pleasure of the house.But remember one thing—let your superiority be visible in those things only which flatter a man’s self-love; hide the superiority you must also acquire over him in great things.”
“但是你吓到我了，妈妈，”纳塔莉叫起来，“这么多条例，我哪里全记得住啊？我多么小孩子气，多么鲁莽，哪里做得到事前三思，步步盘算？” “But you frighten me, mamma,” cried Natalie.“How can I remember all these precepts?How shall I ever manage, I, such a child, and so heedless, to reflect and calculate before I act?”
“但是，我亲爱的小姑娘，我今天跟你讲的，日后你肯定会学到，但是那时你会付出惨痛的代价，会犯下致命的错误，并给你终生都带来苦涩的遗憾和尴尬。” “But, my dear little girl, I am telling you today that which you must surely learn later, buying your experience by fatal faults and errors of conduct which will cause you bitter regrets and embarrass your whole life.”
“但是我应该怎么开始呢？”纳塔莉天真地问道。 “But how must I begin?” asked Natalie, artlessly.
“跟着你的本能走，”母亲答道，“这一时刻，与其说保尔爱你，不如说他更想占有你；占有欲的爱情只是一种期望，占有以后的爱情才是现实。亲爱的，问题的关键就在于此，你的力量就体现在这方面。哪个女人在结婚前不是被爱的对象呢？但婚后仍然被爱，你才会永远被人所爱。保尔是个文弱书生，很容易就会被培养出这个习惯的。只要他向你让一次步，以后就总会让步的。一个被丈夫热切渴望着的女人可以提任何要求。许多女人不知道两人刚开始相处时占有支配权的重要性，不要做这种傻事——把你的力量浪费在一些无谓的小事或没有结果的蠢事上。利用好丈夫对你最初的激情，使他习惯什么事情都顺着你。当你想让他顺从你的时候，挑些最不讲理的事情，好测试他对你的让步达到了哪种程度，以此来衡量你掌控力的程度。让他做一件合情合理的事，算得上什么胜利啊？那能叫对你服服帖帖吗？正如卡斯蒂利亚语中的一条谚语——迎面抓住牛角。当它发现无论怎么挣扎都无济于事的时候，它就是被击败了。一旦你的丈夫为你做了蠢事，你就能管制住他了。” “Instinct will guide you,” replied her mother.“At this moment Paul desires you more than he loves you; for love born of desires is a hope; the love that succeeds their satisfaction is the reality.There, my dear, is the question; there lies your power.What woman is not loved before marriage?Be so on the morrow and you shall remain so always.Paul is a weak man who is easily trained to habit.If he yields to you once he will yield always.A woman ardently desired can ask all things; do not commit the folly of many women who do not see the importance of the first hours of their sway,—that of wasting your power on trifles, on silly things with no result.Use the empire your husband’s first emotions give you to accustom him to obedience.And when you make him yield, choose that it be on some unreasonable point, so as to test the measure of your power by the measure of his concession.What victory would there be in making him agree to a reasonable thing?Would that be obeying you?We must always, as the Castilian proverb says, take the bull by the horns; when a bull has once seen the inutility of his defence and of his strength he is beaten.When your husband does a foolish thing for you, you can govern him.”
“为什么这么说呢？” “Why so?”
“我的孩子，因为婚姻是要持续一辈子的，丈夫也不是世间随随便便的一个男人。所以，在任何事情上都不要完全随从他的意愿。言行都得格外慎重小心。你甚至可以对他表现得冷淡些，这样是没有任何危险的，因为你随时可以改变你冷漠的态度。再说，没有什么事情比保持尊严更容易了。‘身为人妻不应该做这个，不应该做那个。’——这句话是护身符。女人一生就在于‘我不愿意’这几个字。这是最终话语权。女性的力量就在于此，所以只能在关键的时候才能用。但是，这句话意味着统治，而不是结论或讨论。我亲爱的孩子，我就是用你父亲对我的信念来管制他的。如果你丈夫信赖你，跟他在一起时，你想做什么就做什么。为了使他信赖你，你就得让他觉得你是理解他的。可不要认为这是件容易的差事。一个女人总是能够使男人相信她爱着他，但是要使他承认她理解他却要困难得多。我现在什么都要跟你说清楚，我的孩子，因为明天你的生活将开始充满变数，两个人的生活只能由一个人做主。一定要时刻留意这个难题。把两个人的意志协调好的唯一方法就是一开始就只有一种意志，而那种意志就是你的意志。很多人宣扬如果一个女人转换角色就会给自己造成不幸。但是亲爱的，女人只有掌控局面，而非被动地接受事情。这一有利条件就足以弥补所有的不利。” “Because, my child, marriage lasts a lifetime, and a husband is not a man like other men.Therefore, never commit the folly of giving yourself into his power in everything.Keep up a constant reserve in your speech and in your actions.You may even be cold to him without danger, for you can modify coldness at will.Besides, nothing is more easy to maintain than our dignity.The words, ‘It is not becoming in your wife to do thus and so,’ is a great talisman.The life of a woman lies in the words, ‘I will not.’They are the final argument.Feminine power is in them, and therefore they should only be used on real occasions.But they constitute a means of governing far beyond that of argument or discussion.I, my dear child, reigned over your father by his faith in me.If your husband believes in you, you can do all things with him.To inspire that belief you must make him think that you understand him.Do not suppose that that is an easy thing to do.A woman can always make a man think that he is loved, but to make him admit that he is understood is far more difficult.I am bound to tell you all now, my child, for tomorrow life with its complications, life with two wills which must be made one, begins for you.Bear in mind, at all moments, that difficulty.The only means of harmonizing your two wills is to arrange from the first that there shall be but one; and that will must be yours.Many persons declare that a wife creates her own unhappiness by changing sides in this way; but, my dear, she can only become the mistress by controlling events instead of bearing them; and that advantage compensates for any difficulty.”
纳塔莉留下了感激的泪水，并亲吻了母亲的手。就像所有感情胜过理智的女人一样，她突然明白了这项所谓的女性为人处世之道，但是她又像一个被惯坏了的孩子，固执己见而不听任何道理。孩童般的逻辑又促使她说出了个人的意见—— Natalie kissed her mother’s hands with tears of gratitude.Like all women in whom mental emotion is never warmed by physical emotion, she suddenly comprehended the bearings of this feminine policy; but, like a spoiled child that never admits the force of reason and returns obstinately to its one desire, she came back to the charge with one of those personal arguments which the logic of a child suggests:—
“亲爱的妈妈，”她说道，“就在前几天，你还说你光凭一己之力就能照管好保尔的前途。为什么现在你又突然改变立场，弃我们于不顾呢？” “Dear mamma,” she said, “it is only a few days since you were talking of Paul’s advancement, and saying that you alone could promote it; why, then, do you suddenly turn round and abandon us to ourselves?”
“因为那时我还不知道我的应尽义务和我负债的具体数额。”母亲答道，她不想说出自己离开的真正动机，“而且一两年之后，我会重新负起这个责任的。来，我们梳妆打扮吧，保尔就要到了。你一定要表现得温柔体贴，就像——你知道吧？——就像讨论婚约那天晚上一样。因为今天我们必须保留我们家最后的一点儿财产。我对这件东西已经到了痴迷的地步，也准备日后把这件东西留给你的。” “I did not then know the extent of my obligations nor the amount of my debts,” replied the mother, who would not suffer her real motive to be seen.“Besides, a year or two hence I can take up that matter again.Come, let us dress; Paul will be here soon.Be as sweet and caressing as you were,—you know?—that night when we first discussed this fatal contract; for today we must save the last fragments of our fortune, and I must win for you a thing to which I am superstitiously attached.”
“是什么东西？” “What is it?”
“祖传钻石。” “The ‘Discreto.’”
四点左右，保尔来了。尽管他努力在岳母面前表现出亲切的姿态，埃旺热利斯塔夫人仍然能看出他彻夜掂量和清晨思考后的阴云密布。 Paul arrived about four o’clock.Though he endeavored to meet his mother-inlaw with a gracious look upon his face, Madame Evangelista saw traces of the clouds which the counsels of the night and the reflections of the morning had brought there.
“马蒂亚斯肯定跟他说了什么！”她想道，决定要彻底地击败老公证人的行动计划。“我亲爱的孩子，”她说，“你把钻石留在桌子的抽屉里，我坦白地承认，我不想再看到那些东西了，那些东西差点儿引起我们关系间的阴影。而且，正如马蒂亚斯先生所说，钻石得即刻卖掉用来支付你买地的第一笔款项。” “Mathias has told him!” she thought, resolving to defeat the old notary’s action.“My dear son,” she said, “you left your diamonds in the drawer of the console, and I frankly confess that I would rather not see again the things that threatened to bring a cloud between us.Besides, as Monsieur Mathias said, they ought to be sold at once to meet the first payment on the estates you have purchased.”
“钻石已经不是我的了，”他说道，“我已经送给纳塔莉，当你看到她佩戴这些钻石时，就会忘了它们曾给你带来的痛苦。” “They are not mine,” he said.“I have given them to Natalie, and when you see them upon her you will forget the pain they caused you.”
埃旺热利斯塔夫人紧握住保尔的手，感动得热泪盈眶。 Madame Evangelista took his hand and pressed it cordially, with a tear of emotion.
“听我说，我的乖孩子们，”她看了看保尔，又看了看纳塔莉说道，“既然你们都这么认为，那我要对你们提一项建议。我觉得我必须要卖掉我的珍珠项链和耳环的。是的，保尔，这是必然的。我不会把一分钱资产投入终身年金的，我知道我欠你多少钱。不过，我承认我的弱点，要卖掉我那颗祖传钻石，对我来说可真是一场灾难。这颗钻石曾经为腓力二世所拥有，点缀过他那皇室之手。这颗钻石具有历史意义，阿尔伯公爵的宝剑上就镶有这颗宝石，并被他抚摸了十年光阴——不，不能卖！埃利·玛古斯把我的项链和耳环估价在十万法郎还要多几千。你愿不愿意用之前我移交给你的那些珠宝来交换这些？这个交易，你能得到好处，但是这又怎样？我不是一个自私的人。保尔，你的妻子将得到璀璨绚丽的钻石，从中享受真正的快乐，而不是那些花俏的新奇首饰。我把那些过时的装饰品都卖了，你留下这些无价的宝石，岂不是更好？” “Listen to me, my dear children,” she said, looking from Paul to Natalie; “since you really feel thus, I have a proposition to make to both of you.I find myself obliged to sell my pearl necklace and my earrings.Yes, Paul, it is necessary; I do not choose to put a penny of my fortune into an annuity; I know what I owe to you.Well, I admit a weakness; to sell the ‘Discreto’ seems to me a disaster.To sell a diamond which bears the name of Philip the Second and once adorned his royal hand, an historic stone which the Duke of Alba touched for ten years in the hilt of his sword—no, no, I cannot!Elie Magus estimates my necklace and earrings at a hundred and some odd thousand francs without the clasps.Will you exchange the other jewels I made over to you for these? you will gain by the transaction, but what of that?I am not selfish.Instead of those mere fancy jewels, Paul, your wife will have fine diamonds which she can really enjoy.Isn’t it better that I should sell those ornaments which will surely go out of fashion, and that you should keep in the family these priceless stones?”
“但是我亲爱的母亲，你也得考虑考虑自己啊！”保尔说。 “But, my dear mother, consider yourself,” said Paul.
“我啊，”埃旺热利斯塔夫人答道，“我不再需要这样的东西了。是的，保尔，我准备到朗斯特拉克去当你家的管家。这个时候我应该在这儿清算我的财产，解决剩下的事宜，我发了疯才会去巴黎呢。为了我的孙辈们，我得厉行节约了。” “I,” replied Madame Evangelista, “I want such things no longer.Yes, Paul, I am going to be your bailiff at Lanstrac.It would be folly in me to go to Paris at the moment when I ought to be here to liquidate my property and settle my affairs.I shall grow miserly for my grandchildren.”
“亲爱的母亲，”保尔异常感动地说，“我接受这样的馈赠，难道不应该付给你差价吗？” “Dear mother,” said Paul, much moved, “ought I to accept this exchange without paying you the difference?”
“天啊！你们俩难道不是我最宝贵的财产吗？当我坐在壁炉边想着：在今晚贝里公爵夫人的舞会上，纳塔莉真是美艳动人，你认为我不感到幸福吗？当她看到我的钻石挂在她的项链上，耳环吊在她的耳朵上，她小小的虚荣将被满足。这种虚荣使女人幸福快乐、光彩迷人。没什么比压抑一个女人的虚荣心更令她伤心难过。我从来没见过一个打扮寒酸的女人能够表现得和蔼可亲或心情愉悦。” “Good heavens! are you not, both of you, my dearest interests?Do you suppose I shall not find happiness in thinking, as I sit in my chimney-corner, ‘Natalie is dazzling to-night at the Duchesse de Berry’s ball’?When she sees my diamond at her throat and my earrings in her ears she will have one of those little enjoyments of vanity which contribute so much to a woman’s happiness and make her so gay and fascinating.Nothing saddens a woman more than to have her vanity repressed; I have never seen an ill-dressed woman who was amiable or good-humored.”
“上帝啊！马蒂亚斯居然还那么想？”保尔寻思着。“那，妈妈，”他小声说道，“我接受您的建议。” “Heavens! what was Mathias thinking about?” thought Paul.“Well, then, mamma,” he said, in a low voice, “I accept.”
“不过我都搞糊涂了！”纳塔莉说。 “But I am confounded!” said Natalie.
此时索洛内来了，带来一则好消息。他在波尔多的投机商中找到两个承包商，他们有意购买这座房产，因为后院可以改建成供居住的房子。 At this moment Solonet arrived to announce the good news that he had found among the speculators of Bordeaux two contractors who were much attracted by the house, the gardens of which could be covered with dwellings.
“他们报价二十五万法郎，”他说道，“但是如果你同意这笔买卖的话，我可以叫他们出三十万。花园面积可是有三公顷。” “They offer two hundred and fifty thousand francs,” he said; “but if you consent to the sale, I can make them give you three hundred thousand.There are three acres of land in the garden.”
“我丈夫当初买这两块地花了二十万，所以我同意卖，”她答道，“但是请你一定为我留下家具和镜子。” “My husband paid two hundred thousand for the place, therefore I consent,” she replied.“But you must reserve the furniture and the mirrors.”
“啊！”索洛内说道，“你开始懂做生意了。” “Ah!” said Solonet, “you are beginning to understand business.”
“哎！我必须得会，”她叹道。 “Alas! I must,” she said, sighing.
“我听说等一下会有很多人来你家做半夜弥撒。”索洛内说道，他觉得自己不便久呆，准备离开。 “I am told that a great many persons are coming to your midnight service,” said Solonet, perceiving that his presence was inopportune, and preparing to go.
埃旺热利斯塔夫人送他到大门口，然后小声跟他说： Madame Evangelista accompanied him to the door of the last salon, and there she said, in a low voice:—
“我随身物品值二十五万法郎，如果我能从卖房款里面得到二十万，总共就是很可观的一笔资产了。我会拿去投资，以得到最佳回报。这件事我就指望你了。以后我或许会住在朗斯特拉克。” “I now have personal property to the amount of two hundred and fifty thousand francs; if I can get two hundred thousand for my share of the house it will make a handsome capital, which I shall want to invest to the very best advantage.I count on you for that.I shall probably live at Lanstrac.”
年轻的公证人充满感激地吻了一下主顾的手。从寡妇的语气中，索洛内觉得他们之间的这种利益联盟，也许会发展得更深一步。 The young notary kissed his client’s hand with a gesture of gratitude; for the widow’s tone of voice made Solonet fancy that this alliance, really made from self-interest only, might extend a little farther.
“你可以依靠我，”他答道，“我能找到商品用以投资，无需承担任何风险，而且利润可观。” “You can count on me,” he replied.“I can find you investments in merchandise on which you will risk nothing and make very considerable profits.”
“明天见，”她说，“你知道，你和吉亚斯侯爵先生是我们的证婚人。” “Adieu until tomorrow,” she said; “you are to be our witness, you know, with Monsieur le Marquis de Gyas.”
“我亲爱的母亲，”当埃旺热利斯塔夫人送完索洛内回来时，保尔对她说道，“您为什么不愿搬到巴黎住呢？纳塔莉因此生我气，好像是我引起你作此决定的。” “My dear mother,” said Paul, when she returned to them, “why do you refuse to come to Paris?Natalie is provoked with me, as if I were the cause of your decision.”
“我是这么考虑的，我的孩子们，我确信我去了会妨碍你们的。你们做任何事情都被迫要带着我这个第三者在身边。年轻人有年轻人的想法，我可能会无意中就与你们想法不同。你们去巴黎吧。以前纳塔莉凡事都听我的，我可不想继续管着德马内维尔夫人。我要把她彻底地送给你。保尔，你不明白吗？我们之间的一些生活方式和生活习惯必须被打破。现在应该是你做主，而不是我了。我希望你爱我，也希望你相信我比你所想的更在乎你的利益。女儿疼爱母亲，年轻的丈夫迟早会有所妒忌的。也许丈夫们这么想也是有道理的。当你们完全彻底地融合，当爱情使你们融为一体时，那时我亲爱的孩子，你就不会再担心我住在你们家会造成什么不快了。我深谙世事，阅人无数。我曾经见过许多家庭中，母亲对女儿盲目地宠爱，最终使女儿和女婿都无法承受。上了年纪的人的感情总是琐碎而令人心烦的。我不应该再抛头露面了，但也许我做不到。我的弱点在于自以为风韵犹存，有些善于迎合拍马屁的人也说我还有几分容貌。我怕我的这些虚荣会干扰你们的生活。所以，让我再为你们的幸福做一次牺牲吧。我已经把我的财产都给你了，现在我希望能把我最后的一点虚荣心也交给你。你的公证人马蒂亚斯越来越老了。他无法像我一样照看你的家产。我来做你的管家，人老了最乐于做这些事。如果有必要的话，日后我会到巴黎，帮你在事业上一展宏图。算了，保尔，坦白地说，我的建议对你还是适合的，不是吗？” “I have thought it all over, my children, and I am sure that I should hamper you.You would feel obliged to make me a third in all you did, and young people have ideas of their own which I might, unintentionally, thwart.Go to Paris.I do not wish to exercise over the Comtesse de Manerville the gentle authority I have held over Natalie.I desire to leave her wholly to you.Don’t you see, Paul, that there are habits and ways between us which must be broken up?My influence ought to yield to yours.I want you to love me, and to believe that I have your interests more at heart than you think for.Young husbands are, sooner or later, jealous for the love of a wife for her mother.Perhaps they are right.When you are thoroughly united, when love has blended your two souls into one, then, my dear son, you will not fear an opposing influence if I live in your house.I know the world, and men, and things; I have seen the peace of many a home destroyed by the blind love of mothers who made themselves in the end as intolerable to their daughters as to their sons-inlaw.The affection of old people is often exacting and querulous.Perhaps I could not efface myself as I should.I have the weakness to think myself still handsome; I have flatterers who declare that I am still agreeable; I should have, I fear, certain pretensions which might interfere with your lives.Let me, therefore, make one more sacrifice for your happiness.I have given you my fortune, and now I desire to resign to you my last vanities as a woman.Your notary Mathias is getting old.He cannot look after your estates as I will.I will be your bailiff; I will create for myself those natural occupations which are the pleasures of old age.Later, if necessary, I will come to you in Paris, and second you in your projects of ambition.Come, Paul, be frank; my proposal suits you, does it not?”
保尔不愿承认这一点，不过一想到能自由自在地生活，他打心底里还是很高兴的。马蒂亚斯叫他要防着岳母，但是，这一次对话完全驱散了他对岳母的怀疑。埃旺热利斯塔夫人保持着同样的口气继续唠唠叨叨地说着。 Paul would not admit it, but he was at heart delighted to get his liberty.The suspicions which Mathias had put into his mind respecting his mother-inlaw were, however, dissipated by this conversation, which Madame Evangelista carried on still longer in the same tone.
“我母亲是正确的，”看着保尔脸上的表情，纳塔莉想道，“他巴不得我跟母亲分开——为什么呢？” “My mother was right,” thought Natalie, who had watched Paul’s countenance.“He is glad to know that I am separated from her—why?”
这个“为什么”正是一种不信任感的第一个信号，不是正好证明了母亲之前的种种教诲吗？ That “why” was the first note of a rising distrust; did it prove the power of those maternal instructions?
有些人的性格就是只凭一件单一的事情就相信他人的友谊。这些人总认为，北风很快就能赶走乌云，正如南风很快就能把这些乌云带回来。他们只看结果，从不回想原因。保尔就是这类人中的一员，他没有坏心思，容易轻信他人，而且没有远见。他的弱点主要在于他的仁慈，崇尚与人为善，而不是他意志的真正软弱。 There are certain characters which on the faith of a single proof believe in friendship.To persons thus constituted the north wind drives away the clouds as rapidly as the south wind brings them; they stop at effects and never hark back to causes.Paul had one of those essentially confiding natures, without ill-feelings, but also without foresight.His weakness proceeded far more from his kindness, his belief in goodness, than from actual debility of soul.
纳塔莉陷入沉思当中，心里满是悲伤。她不知道母亲不在身边时她该怎么办。爱情使保尔禁不住自鸣得意起来，对她的莫名悲伤暗中嘲笑。他想着婚姻的快乐和巴黎的灯红酒绿将很快驱散她的这种情绪。埃旺热利斯塔满意地看到保尔就要同意她的提议了。她已经走完了两大步。保尔将为她女儿的首饰付出二十万的代价。除了这两个孩子不符合逻辑的爱情外，她已经无法给他们什么指点。她的复仇计划就这样悄悄地准备着，女儿也被蒙在鼓里，而且迟早会成为她的帮手。纳塔莉爱保尔吗？这个问题仍然没有答案，答案或许会影响她的全盘计划，因为她是如此深爱自己的女儿，不可能不尊重女儿的终身幸福。所以说，保尔的未来仍然由他自己决定。如果他能让他的妻子爱上他，他还是有救的。 Natalie was sad and thoughtful, for she knew not what to do without her mother.Paul, with that self-confident conceit which comes of love, smiled to himself at her sadness, thinking how soon the pleasures of marriage and the excitements of Paris would drive it away.Madame Evangelista saw this confidence with much satisfaction.She had already taken two great steps.Her daughter possessed the diamonds which had cost Paul two hundred thousand francs; and she had gained her point of leaving these two children to themselves with no other guide than their illogical love.Her revenge was thus preparing, unknown to her daughter, who would, sooner or later, become its accomplice.Did Natalie love Paul?That was a question still undecided, the answer to which might modify her projects, for she loved her daughter too sincerely not to respect her happiness.Paul’s future, therefore, still depended on himself.If he could make his wife love him, he was saved.
第二天午夜，在四位证婚人的见证下举行了婚礼，履行了法律的手续，然后是晚宴，整整花了一个晚上。半夜时分，打着火炬，新婚夫妇在友人们的陪伴下在教堂听了结婚弥撒，旁边围着一群爱看热闹的人们。晚上庆祝婚礼总给人一种不祥的预兆。光是生命和快乐的象征，而午夜举行的婚礼却没有这样的象征。问问那英勇的灵魂为什么会颤抖；为什么漆黑拱门的寒意会让它软弱无力；为什么脚步声会让它受惊；为什么它会留神蝙蝠的嚎叫和猫头鹰的鸣叫。虽然根本没有任何颤抖的理由，所有在场的人却抖个不停。黑暗这个死亡的象征物，使大家都感到哀愁。纳塔莉流着泪与母亲告别。即将进入一种新的生活，女孩心中各种疑惑使她不得安宁。对于这个年轻的妻子来说，虽然幸福得到层层保障，但也有千万个陷阱迎面等着她。她感觉寒冷，想披上一件披风。埃旺热利斯塔夫人和新婚夫妻的神情和举止引起了围在圣坛周围的一群文雅之士的品评。 The next day, at midnight, after an evening spent together, with the addition of the four witnesses, to whom Madame Evangelista gave the formal dinner which follows the legal marriage, the bridal pair, accompanied by their friends, heard mass by torchlight, in presence of a crowd of inquisitive persons.A marriage celebrated at night always suggests to the mind an unpleasant omen.Light is the symbol of life and pleasure, the forecasts of which are lacking to a midnight wedding.Ask the intrepid soul why it shivers; why the chill of those black arches enervates it; why the sound of steps startles it; why it notices the cry of bats and the hoot of owls.Though there is absolutely no reason to tremble, all present do tremble, and the darkness, emblem of death, saddens them.Natalie, parted from her mother, wept.The girl was now a prey to those doubts which grasp the heart as it enters a new career in which, despite all assurances of happiness, a thousand pitfalls await the steps of a young wife.She was cold and wanted a mantle.The air and manner of Madame Evangelista and that of the bridal pair excited some comment among the elegant crowd which surrounded the altar.
“索洛内跟我说，新娘和新郎明早就启程去巴黎，就他们两个去。” “Solonet tells me that the bride and bridegroom leave for Paris tomorrow morning, all alone.”
“我还以为埃旺热利斯塔夫人也会跟着一起去呢。” “Madame Evangelista was to live with them, I thought.”
“保尔伯爵已经把她甩了。” “Count Paul has got rid of her already.”
“多大的一个错误啊！”吉亚斯侯爵夫人说道，“把妻子的母亲关在门外，就相当于打开了妻子与情夫的大门。难道他不知道一个母亲对女儿意味着什么？” “What a mistake!” said the Marquise de Gyas.“To shut the door on the mother of his wife is to open it to a lover.Doesn’t he know what a mother is?”
“他对埃旺热利斯塔夫人可太铁石心肠了；这个可怜的女人卖掉了她的房子和首饰，准备去朗斯特拉克生活。” “He has been very hard on Madame Evangelista; the poor woman has had to sell her house and her diamonds, and is going to live at Lanstrac.”
“纳塔莉看上去很忧伤。” “Natalie looks very sad.”
“一结婚就远走他乡，要是你，能开心得起来吗？” “Would you like to be made to take a journey the day after your marriage?”
“那的确很不合适。” “It is very awkward.”
“真是高兴我今晚来了，”一位女士说道，“我现在确信把婚礼和婚宴搞得绚丽喧哗的必要性了；这样的场面空洞而令人悲戚。如果允许我发表我的见解，”她对着邻近的一个人低声说道，“我觉着这桩婚事不妥。” “I am glad I came here to-night,” said a lady.“I am now convinced of the necessity of the pomps of marriage and of wedding fetes; a scene like this is very bare and sad.If I may say what I think,” she added, in a whisper to her neighbor, “this marriage seems to me indecent.”
埃旺热利斯塔夫人亲自驾着马车，把纳塔莉送到了保尔家。 Madame Evangelista took Natalie in her carriage and accompanied her, alone, to Paul’s house.
“唉，母亲，一切都已成定局了！” “Well, mother, it is done!”
“记住，我亲爱的孩子，记住我对你最后的嘱托，你会成为一个幸福的女人的。你是他的妻子，不是他的情妇。” “Remember, my dear child, my last advice, and you will be a happy woman.Be his wife, and not his mistress.”
待纳塔莉休息去了，这位母亲演了一出戏给保尔看，她眼泪汪汪地扑到了她的女婿怀里。这是她做的唯一一件带有外省风味的事，但是她这么做也是有原因的。在她那显然半是疯癫半是绝望的眼泪和言语中，保尔对她作出了所有丈夫都会做的退步。 When Natalie had retired, the mother played the little comedy of flinging herself with tears into the arms of her son-inlaw.It was the only provincial thing that Madame Evangelista allowed herself, but she had her reasons for it.Amid tears and speeches, apparently half wild and despairing, she obtained of Paul those concessions which all husbands make.
第二天，她让新婚夫妇坐在马车上，陪他们去坐渡船，走水路渡过吉伦特河到巴黎去。纳塔莉的表情和言语让她的母亲知道，即使保尔在婚约这场博弈中取胜了，她的复仇才刚刚开始。纳塔莉已经让她的丈夫对她彻底俯首帖耳了。 The next day she put the married pair into their carriage, and accompanied them to the ferry, by which the road to Paris crosses the Gironde.With a look and a word Natalie enabled her mother to see that if Paul had won the trick in the game of the contract, her revenge was beginning.Natalie was already reducing her husband to perfect obedience.
埃旺热利斯塔夫人亲自驾着马车，把纳塔莉送到了保尔家。 Madame Evangelista took Natalie in her carriage and accompanied her, alone, to Paul’s house.
“唉，母亲，一切都已成定局了！” “Well, mother, it is done!”
“记住，我亲爱的孩子，记住我对你最后的嘱托，你会成为一个幸福的女人的。你是他的妻子，不是他的情妇。” “Remember, my dear child, my last advice, and you will be a happy woman.Be his wife, and not his mistress.”
待纳塔莉休息去了，这位母亲演了一出戏给保尔看，她眼泪汪汪地扑到了她的女婿怀里。这是她做的唯一一件带有外省风味的事，但是她这么做也是有原因的。在她那半是疯癫半是绝望的眼泪和言语中，保尔对她作出了所有的丈夫都会做的退步。 When Natalie had retired, the mother played the little comedy of flinging herself with tears into the arms of her son-inlaw.It was the only provincial thing that Madame Evangelista allowed herself, but she had her reasons for it.Amid tears and speeches, apparently half wild and despairing, she obtained of Paul those concessions which all husbands make.
第二天，她让新婚夫妇坐在马车上，送他们去坐渡船，走水路渡过吉伦特河到巴黎去。纳塔莉的表情似乎在告诉母亲，即使保尔在婚约这场博弈中取胜了，她的复仇才刚刚开始。保尔对纳塔莉已经是彻彻底底地俯首帖耳了。 The next day she put the married pair into their carriage, and accompanied them to the ferry, by which the road to Paris crosses the Gironde.With a look and a word Natalie enabled her mother to see that if Paul had won the trick in the game of the contract, her revenge was beginning.Natalie was already reducing her husband to perfect obedience.
第六章 尾声 CHAPTER VI CONCLUSION
五年后，十一月的一个午后，保尔·德马内维尔伯爵穿着一件大衣，低着头神秘地走进位于波尔多的马蒂亚斯先生家中。 Five years later, on an afternoon in the month of November, Comte Paul de Manerville, wrapped in a cloak, was entering, with a bowed head and a mysterious manner, the house of his old friend Monsieur Mathias at Bordeaux.
这位令人尊重的公证人因为年事已高已经不再继续从业，卖掉了他的事务所，在一处僻静的房子中静心养老，过着隐居的日子。马蒂亚斯先生因为急事正好出门了，不过他的管家被事先通知保尔会到，便把他带到已过世一年的马蒂亚斯夫人房中休息。旅途仓促劳顿，保尔一觉睡到天黑。老人回家以后，走到他的主顾床前，静静地看着他睡觉的样子，就像是一个母亲看着自己入睡的孩子。老管家若赛特陪着主人也站在床前，双手叉在腰间。 Too old to continue in business, the worthy notary had sold his practice and was ending his days peacefully in a quiet house to which he had retired.An urgent affair had obliged him to be absent at the moment of his guest’s arrival, but his housekeeper, warned of Paul’s coming, took him to the room of the late Madame Mathias, who had been dead a year.Fatigued by a rapid journey, Paul slept till evening.When the old man reached home he went up to his client’s room, and watched him sleeping, as a mother watches her child.Josette, the old housekeeper, followed her master and stood before the bed, her hands on her hips.
“今天正好一年了，若赛特，我看着我深爱的妻子咽下最后一口气。当时我哪里知道我在同一个地方居然会看到伯爵先生也是半死不活的样子。” “It is a year today, Josette, since I received my dear wife’s last sigh; I little knew then that I should stand here again to see the count half dead.”
“可怜的人啊！他在睡觉的时候还呻吟着呢！”若赛特说道。 “Poor man! he moans in his sleep,” said Josette.
“要命啊！”老公证人骂道，他这一声并无恶意的咒骂表现出他了的绝望，是一个人在碰到了无法应付的棘手事时的神情。“再怎么说，”他暗想道，“我挽救了他在朗斯特拉克、欧扎克、圣弗鲁和他自己的住处共四处房产的所有权，虽然使用权已经没有了。”马蒂亚斯扳起手指一算。“五年了！五年前也是这个月，他那已经去世的姑婆，为人善良的德·摩冷古太太，代他向那口蜜腹剑的小女人求婚。这个女人最终毁了他——如我所料。” “Sac a papier!” cried the old notary, an innocent oath which was a sign with him of the despair on a man of business before insurmountable difficulties.“At any rate,” he thought, “I have saved the title to the Lanstrac estate for him, and that of Ausac, Saint–Froult, and his house, though the usufruct has gone.”Mathias counted his fingers.“Five years!Just five years this month, since his old aunt, now dead, that excellent Madame de Maulincour, asked for the hand of that little crocodile of a woman, who has finally ruined him—as I expected.”
这位患了痛风病的老绅士拄着拐杖到小花园散步去了，等着他的客人醒来。九点的时候，晚餐做好了，因为马蒂亚斯习惯吃晚餐的。当保尔来到他面前时，老公证人吃惊地发现，虽然保尔的样子变化很大，但是面容依然平静而安详。三十三岁的德马内维尔伯爵看上去像一个四十开外的人，容貌上的变化完全是精神上的打击造成的，就身体而言他还是健康得很。他满怀深情地紧握住老人的手，不让他起身，说道： And the gouty old gentleman, leaning on his cane, went to walk in the little garden till his guest should awake.At nine o’clock supper was served, for Mathias took supper.The old man was not a little astonished, when Paul joined him, to see that his old client’s brow was calm and his face serene, though noticeably changed.If at the age of thirty-three the Comte de Manerville seemed to be a man of forty, that change in his appearance was due solely to mental shocks; physically, he was well.He clasped the old man’s hand affectionately, and forced him not to rise, saying:—
“亲爱的，善良的马蒂亚斯总管，你也承受了生活的痛苦吧。” “Dear, kind Maitre Mathias, you, too, have had your troubles.”
“我的痛苦是不可避免的，伯爵先生，但是你的痛苦却是——” “Mine were natural troubles, Monsieur le comte; but yours—”
“等一下我们吃晚饭时再谈这个吧。” “We will talk of that presently, while we sup.”
“如果不是我有一个在司法部门工作的儿子，一个已经嫁人的女儿，”心地善良的老人家说道，“相信我，伯爵先生，你在老马蒂亚斯这里得到的将远不只是热情款待而已。现在波尔多所有的墙壁上都贴着公告宣布扣押你在格拉索尔、居阿尔、美丽玫瑰葡萄园和你自己的房产，为什么这个时候你还来波尔多？我无法跟你说清当我看到这些公告时的悲伤——四十年来，我精心照看这些房产，就像它们都是我的一样。当初我还只是我的前任谢诺先生手下的三等职员，为你母亲买下这些房产，并亲手工整地用圆体字写下契约。我把这些契约放在我的继任者的办公室里。我第一次看到你时，你才这么大！”老人边说着，边把手放到接近地面的高度。 “If I had not a son in the magistracy, and a daughter married,” said the good old man, “you would have found in old Mathias, believe me, Monsieur le comte, something better than mere hospitality.Why have you come to Bordeaux at the very moment when posters are on all the walls of the seizure of your farms at Grassol and Guadet, the vineyard of Belle–Rose and the family mansion?I cannot tell you the grief I feel at the sight of those placards,—I, who for forty years nursed that property as if it belonged to me; I, who bought it for your mother when I was only third clerk to Monsieur Chesnau, my predecessor, and wrote the deeds myself in my best round hand; I, who have those titles now in my successor’s office; I, who have known you since you were so high”; and the old man stopped to put his hand near the ground.
“唉！只有当了四十一年半的公证人，如今看到自己的名字在大庭广众之下印在那些扣押公告和财产待售文件中，才能体会到这样的悲伤。每当我从街上路过，看到人们正在关注那些可怕的黄色公告时，就感到羞愧难当，好像事关我自己的荣誉和财产一般。有些混蛋故意站在旁边大声读出来，好引起另外一些混蛋的注意——你不知道他们说的话有多难听！就好像一个男人无权处置自己的财产一样！你父亲之前花光了两笔财产，后来留给了你一份家业；如果你要是不走他的老路，你就不是德马内维尔家族的人了。而且，民法本身就有一大章专讲扣押不动产的，这是法律中明文规定的。你的问题也是法律允许范围内的。如果我不是一个满头白发的老头子，我一定会朝那些大声宣读布告的混蛋扇一巴掌，”好心的公证人拿起一张纸继续说下去，“应纳塔莉·埃旺热利斯塔即保尔·弗朗索瓦·约瑟夫·德马内维尔伯爵之妻的请求，塞纳省初级法院判决其与丈夫财产分开——” “Ah! a man must have been a notary for forty-one years and a half to know the sort of grief I feel to see my name exposed before the face of Israel in those announcements of the seizure and sale of the property.When I pass through the streets and see men reading these horrible yellow posters, I am ashamed, as if my own honor and ruin were concerned.Some fools will stand there and read them aloud expressly to draw other fools about them—and what imbecile remarks they make!As if a man were not master of his own property!Your father ran through two fortunes before he made the one he left you; and you wouldn’t be a Manerville if you didn’t do likewise.Besides, seizures of real estate have a whole section of the Code to themselves; they are expected and provided for; you are in a position recognized by the law.—If I were not an old man with white hair, I would thrash those fools I hear reading aloud in the streets such an abomination as this,” added the worthy notary, taking up a paper; “‘At the request of Dame Natalie Evangelista, wife of Paul–Francois-Joseph, Comte de Manerville, separated from him as to worldly goods and chattels by the Lower court of the department of the Seine—’”
“是的，现在人也分开了。”保尔说道。 “Yes, and now separated in body,” said Paul.
“啊！”老人惊叫起来。 “Ah!” exclaimed the old man.
“噢！不是我妻子的意愿，”伯爵急忙补充道，“我只好欺骗她，她不知道我离开的事。” “Oh! against my wife’s will,” added the count, hastily.“I was forced to deceive her; she did not know that I was leaving her.”
“你离开她了？” “You have left her?”
“我已经订好船票，坐‘艾米丽美人号’去加尔各答。” “My passage is taken; I sail for Calcutta on the ‘Belle–Amelie.’”
“那只剩两天了！”老人大声说道。“那样，伯爵先生，我们再也见不到彼此了。” “Two day’s hence!” cried the notary.“Then, Monsieur le comte, we shall never meet again.”
“你还只有七十三岁，我亲爱的马蒂亚斯，你有痛风病，那可是长寿的名誉晋级令。我回来时，肯定还能见到你的。到时你仍然还是头脑灵活、心智健全，你将帮助我重塑这座摇摇欲坠的大厦。我计划在七年内赚一笔数目可观的钱。我回来时只有四十岁。那个年龄，什么事我都能干的。” “You are only seventy-three, my dear Mathias, and you have the gout, the brevet of old age.When I return I shall find you still afoot.Your good head and heart will be as sound as ever, and you will help me to reconstruct what is now a shaken edifice.I intend to make a noble fortune in seven years.I shall be only forty on my return.All is still possible at that age.”
“你？”马蒂亚斯作出一个惊讶的表情说道，“——你，伯爵先生，想去做生意！你是怎么有这个想法的？” “You?” said Mathias, with a gesture of amazement, “—you, Monsieur le comte, to undertake commerce!How can you even think of it?”
“我已经不再是伯爵先生了，亲爱的马蒂亚斯。我船票上登记的名字是卡米亚，是我母亲受洗礼时的一个名字。我还有些技能，可以用于生意以外的途径去赚钱。经商，无论如何，都只是我最后迫不得已的选择。我手头还有一笔钱，我还可以极大程度地补偿我的未来。 “I am no longer Monsieur le comte, dear Mathias.My passage is taken under the name of Camille, one of my mother’s baptismal names.I have acquirements which will enable me to make my fortune otherwise than in business.Commerce, at any rate, will be only my final chance.I start with a sum in hand sufficient for the redemption of my future on a large scale.”
“那笔钱在哪里？” “Where is that money?”
“一个朋友会寄给我。” “A friend is to send it to me.”
老人听到“朋友”这个词时，手中的餐叉当的一声掉在了地下。他既不是惊讶，也不是嘲讽，而是悲伤；保尔还活在欺骗性的幻象之中，老人的表情和神态当中显示出了他的痛楚；伯爵只能看到结实的地面，而久经沧桑的老人却看到了无底的深渊。 The old man dropped his fork as he heard the word “friend,” not in surprise, not scoffingly, but in grief; his look and manner expressed the pain he felt in finding Paul under the influence of a deceitful illusion; his practised eye fathomed a gulf where the count saw nothing but solid ground.
“我做公证人五十年了，”他说道，“还从没看到过，有朋友愿意借钱给一个破了产的人。” “I have been fifty years in the notariat,” he said, “and I never yet knew a ruined man whose friend would lend him money.”
“你不了解德马尔赛。我确定他已经卖出了他的部分公债，明天你就能收到一张十五万法郎的汇票。” “You don’t know de Marsay.I am certain that he has sold out some of his investments already, and tomorrow you will receive from him a bill of exchange for one hundred and fifty thousand francs.”
“我希望我能收到吧。如果真是如你所言，难道你朋友不能在这里帮你解决问题吗？用你妻子的收入，你就可以在朗斯特拉克舒适地生活上五六年来休养生息。” “I hope I may.If that be so, cannot your friend settle your difficulties here?You could live quietly at Lanstrac for five or six years on your wife’s income, and so recover yourself.”
“经济上，我总共已欠下一百五十万法郎的外债，其中我妻子欠下了五十五万。” “No assignment or economy on my part could pay off fifteen hundred thousand francs of debt, in which my wife is involved to the amount of five hundred and fifty thousand.”
“你不会是说，你在四年的时间里欠下了一百五十万债务吧？” “You cannot mean to say that in four years you have incurred a million and a half of debt?”
“千真万确，马蒂亚斯。我不是把钻石都送给我妻子了吗？我不是把卖掉埃旺热利斯塔夫人的房子得来的十五万都用来修缮在巴黎的公馆了吗？婚约中约定的买地的头笔款项不是也得结清吗？我不得不卖掉纳塔莉的四万一年的公债来支付购买欧扎克和圣弗鲁的土地的费用。我们以八七折卖掉了，因此结婚才一个月，我已经负债二十万法郎。这样我们一年只有六七万法郎的收入，但是我们每年花的钱是那数目的整整三倍以上。所有的加在一起，包括借贷的利息，很快就满一百万了。” “Nothing is more certain, Mathias.Did I not give those diamonds to my wife?Did I not spend the hundred and fifty thousand I received from the sale of Madame Evangelista’s house, in the arrangement of my house in Paris?Was I not forced to use other money for the first payments on that property demanded by the marriage contract?I was even forced to sell out Natalie’s forty thousand a year in the Funds to complete the purchase of Auzac and Saint–Froult.We sold at eighty-seven, therefore I became in debt for over two hundred thousand francs within a month after my marriage.That left us only sixty-seven thousand francs a year; but we spent fully three times as much every year.Add all that up, together with rates of interest to usurers, and you will soon find a million.”
“哇！”老公证惊叫道，“继续说。后来呢？” “Br-r-r!” exclaimed the old notary.“Go on.What next?”
“嗯，刚开始我想帮我妻子配齐一套首饰，她有珍珠项链，上面镶有祖传的钻石，还有她母亲给她的耳环。我用十万法郎才给她配了一个冠状首饰。这就一百一十万法郎。现如今我欠我妻子的数额达到三十六万六千法郎，都是‘嫁妆’钱。” “Well, I wanted, in the first place, to complete for my wife that set of jewels of which she had the pearl necklace clasped by the family diamond, the ‘Discreto,’ and her mother’s earrings.I paid a hundred thousand francs for a coronet of diamond wheat-ears.There’s eleven hundred thousand.And now I find I owe the fortune of my wife, which amounts to three hundred and sixty-six thousand francs of her ‘dot.’”
“但是，”马蒂亚斯应道，“如果伯爵夫人放弃这些钻石和首饰，你把收入用来作抵押，是可以及时还上这些债务来平息你的债主们的怒火的。” “But,” said Mathias, “if Madame la comtesse had given up her diamonds and you had pledged your income you could have pacified your creditors and have paid them off in time.”
“马蒂亚斯，当一个男人没钱时，当他的财产都抵押出去了时，他的妻子赶在债主之前取走了自己的财产，他无力支付到期的十万法郎（当然我也希望我付得起），到了这个时候，你的建议是行不通的。” “When a man is down, Mathias, when his property is covered with mortgages, when his wife’s claims take precedence of his creditors’, and when that man has notes out for a hundred thousand francs which he must pay (and I hope I can do so out of the increased value of my property here), what you propose is not possible.”
“真可怕！”公证人叫起来，“你不会把玫瑰美人葡萄园连带其地窖里的1825年的葡萄酒一起卖了吧？” “This is dreadful!” cried Mathias; “would you sell Belle–Rose with the vintage of 1825 still in the cellars?”
“我是迫不得已的。” “I cannot help myself.”
“玫瑰美人庄园价值六十万法郎。” “Belle–Rose is worth six hundred thousand francs.”
“纳塔莉会把它买回来的，我已经向她提了建议。” “Natalie will buy it in; I have advised her to do so.”
“我可以把价格提到七十万，每个农场卖到十万。” “I might push the price to seven hundred thousand, and the farms are worth a hundred thousand each.”
“那么，如果波尔多的房产可以卖到二十一万——” “Then if the house in Bordeaux can be sold for two hundred thousand—”
“索洛内愿意高价买入的，他对这座房产已经垂涎已久。他已经不再干公证这一行，他从事公债投机已经赚了一大笔钱。他作价三十万法郎卖掉了事务所，跟一个黑白混血的女子结婚了。谁也不知道她的钱是怎么弄来的，反正大家都说她身家百万。一个公证人竟去从事股票投机！一个公证人居然跟一个有黑人血统的女子通婚。什么世道啊！据说，他是用你岳母的钱为你岳母打理财务的。” “Solonet will give more than that; he wants it.He is retiring with a handsome property made by gambling on the Funds.He has sold his practice for three hundred thousand francs, and marries a mulatto woman.God knows how she got her money, but they say it amounts to millions.A notary gambling in stocks!a notary marrying a black woman!What an age!It is said that he speculates for your mother-inlaw with her funds.”
“她把朗斯特拉克管理得很好，不遗余力地照看那里的土地。她还付了全额的租金。” “She has greatly improved Lanstrac and taken great pains with its cultivation.She has amply repaid me for the use of it.”
“我真没想到她这么能干。” “I shouldn’t have thought her capable of that.”
“她为人和蔼善良，深爱着我们。每次她到巴黎跟我们合住三个月时，还会帮纳塔莉还债。” “She is so kind and so devoted; she has always paid Natalie’s debts during the three months she spent with us every year in Paris.”
“她完全还得起这个债，朗斯特拉克的产业就足够支付她的生活费用。”马蒂亚斯说道，“她！居然变得节约起来！真是一个奇迹！我听说她刚刚买了朗斯特拉克和格拉索之间的红谷领地；这样的话，如果朗斯特拉克大道可以通到公路，你驱车赶四里半路穿过你的领地就可以到那所房子了。她花了十万法郎来买红谷那块地。” “She could well afford to do so, for she gets her living out of Lanstrac,” said Mathias.“She! grown economical! what a miracle!I am told she has just bought the domain of Grainrouge between Lanstrac and Grassol; so that if the Lanstrac avenue were extended to the high-road, you would drive four and a half miles through your own property to reach the house.She paid one hundred thousand francs down for Grainrouge.”
“她还像以前那样漂亮，”保尔说，“乡村生活使她依然光鲜照人。我不想去朗斯特拉克跟她道别，那样的话她会为我十分伤心的，” “She is as handsome as ever,” said Paul; “country life preserves her freshness; I don’t mean to go to Lanstrac and bid her good-bye; her heart would bleed for me too much.”
“你去了也没用，她人已经在巴黎。她到的时候，你也许刚离开。 “You would go in vain; she is now in Paris.She probably arrived there as you left.”
“她肯定是听说我卖了房产，特意来帮我的。马蒂亚斯，我对生活没有什么好抱怨的。我得到了一个男人所能得到的所有爱，两个女人的钟爱。她们比着看谁对我更好，她们甚至因此而妒忌对方，女儿怪母亲太溺爱我，母亲则怪女儿挥霍奢侈。我得说正是这种感情毁掉了我。对自己心爱的妻子，我如何做得到去拒绝她哪怕最小的一个请求呢？根本控制不住自己！同样我也接受不了她作出任何的牺牲。当然，我们可以如你所说，住到朗斯特拉克去，卖掉她的钻石首饰，但是我宁愿到印度去赚一笔钱带回来，也不愿让我的纳塔莉抛弃她喜欢的生活方式。所以是我提出财产分开的建议的。女人是天使，不应该被卷入这些肮脏的人世利益关系中。” “No doubt she had heard of the sale of my property and came to help me.I have no complaint to make of life, Mathias.I am truly loved,—as much as any man ever could be here below; beloved by two women who outdo each other in devotion; they are even jealous of each other; the daughter blames the mother for loving me too much, and the mother reproaches the daughter for what she calls her dissipations.I may say that this great affection has been my ruin.How could I fail to satisfy even the slightest caprice of a loving wife?Impossible to restrain myself!Neither could I accept any sacrifice on her part.We might certainly, as you say, live at Lanstrac, save my income, and part with her diamonds, but I would rather go to India and work for a fortune than tear my Natalie from the life she enjoys.So it was I who proposed the separation as to property.Women are angels who ought not to be mixed up in the sordid interests of life.”
老马蒂亚斯听到此话，脸上露出疑惑和吃惊的神情。 Old Mathias listened in doubt and amazement.
“我想你们还没生小孩吧。”他说道。 “You have no children, I think,” he said.
“幸好还没有。”保尔应道。 “Fortunately, none,” replied Paul.
“我认为婚姻不是这样的，”老公证人天真地说道，“依我看，一个妻子应该与丈夫有福同享，有难同当。我听说像情人一般相爱相处的年轻夫妻不想生小孩。难道享乐才是婚姻的唯一目的吗？我认为家庭的幸福才是婚姻的目的。恐怕你会觉得我三句话不离我这公证人本行。但是现在这种情况，你的婚约合同迫使你必须生个儿子。是的，伯爵先生，你应该尽快生下一个男性继承人来巩固你的限嗣继承制财产。为什么不呢？埃旺热利斯塔小姐健康强壮，怀孕生子这种事她没什么好怕的。你也许会说，这都是我们这些老古董的陈旧风气。但是在贵族家庭里面，伯爵先生，一个明媒正娶的妻子就有义务生儿育女并把后代好好地抚养长大。正如苏利的妻子，苏利公爵夫人所说：妻子不应该是享乐的工具，而应是贵族门楣的荣誉和美德。” “That is not my idea of marriage,” remarked the old notary, naively.“A wife ought, in my opinion, to share the good and evil fortunes of her husband.I have heard that young married people who love like lovers, do not want children.Is pleasure the only object of marriage?I say that object should be the joys of family.Moreover, in this case—I am afraid you will think me too much of notary—your marriage contract made it incumbent upon you to have a son.Yes, monsieur le comte, you ought to have had at once a male heir to consolidate that entail.Why not?Madame Evangelista was strong and healthy; she had nothing to fear in maternity.You will tell me, perhaps, that these are the old-fashioned notions of our ancestors.But in those noble families, Monsieur le comte, the legitimate wife thought it her duty to bear children and bring them up nobly; as the Duchesse de Sully, the wife of the great Sully, said, a wife is not an instrument of pleasure, but the honor and virtue of her household.”
“你不了解女人，我亲爱的马蒂亚斯，”保尔说道，“我们想要幸福就得像她们所要求的一样去爱她们。这么快就剥夺了一个妻子的魅力，当她才刚开始享受自己的美貌带来的好处，就去毁了她的容貌，是不是有点太残忍了？” “You don’t know women, my good Mathias,” said Paul.“In order to be happy we must love them as they want to be loved.Isn’t there something brutal in at once depriving a wife of her charms, and spoiling her beauty before she has begun to enjoy it?”
“如果你们有孩子了，你的妻子就不会再恣意挥霍你的财产，她会呆在家里好好照顾小孩。” “If you had had children your wife would not have dissipated your fortune; she would have stayed at home and looked after them.”
“如果被你不幸言中，亲爱的朋友，”保尔皱起眉头说道，“我将比现在更不幸。我才刚吃了大亏，你就不要对我说教，这样会使我更难过。让我走吧，不愿再回顾那些令人伤心的错误了。” “If you were right, dear friend,” said Paul, frowning, “I should be still more unhappy than I am.Do not aggravate my sufferings by preaching to me after my fall.Let me go, without the pang of looking backward to my mistakes.”
次日，马蒂亚斯收到了德马赛寄来的一张十五万法郎的汇票。 The next day Mathias received a bill of exchange for one hundred and fifty thousand francs from de Marsay.
“你瞧，”保尔说道，“他一个字也没有写给我。他给了我很大的恩惠。亨利的本性算不上最完美，但作为一个非婚生子，他又拥有最美好的品格。如果你知道他是一个自视甚高的人，一个年轻却不受感情的左右，不受利益驱使的人。你将跟我一样惊喜地发现，他是一个多么心胸宽广的人。” “You see,” said Paul, “he does not write a word to me.He begins by obliging me.Henri’s nature is the most imperfectly perfect, the most illegally beautiful that I know.If you knew with what superiority that man, still young, can rise above sentiments, above self-interests, and judge them, you would be astonished, as I am, to find how much heart he has.”
马蒂亚斯尽力劝阻保尔，却发现无济于事，而且保尔有如此多的理由，最终老人也不再试图挽留他的主顾。 Mathias tried to battle with Paul’s determination, but he found it irrevocable, and it was justified by so many cogent reasons that the old man finally ceased his endeavors to retain his client.
货轮一般很少准时出发的，可是这一次保尔却碰到了稀罕事。清晨微风和煦，“艾米丽美人号”货船准时启航了。码头上到处都是亲戚朋友和一些闲得无聊来看热闹的人。人群当中有几个以前就认识德马内维尔。过去他声名显赫，如今城里的墙上贴满了他破产的布告，使他再度成为一个名人。每个人的好奇心都被激起了，大家对他都有自己的看法。老马蒂亚斯陪着保尔到了码头，马蒂亚斯听到了一些只言片语，心中泛起一片苦楚—— It is seldom that vessels sail promptly at the time appointed, but on this occasion, by a fateful circumstance for Paul, the wind was fair and the “Belle–Amelie” sailed on the morrow, as expected.The quay was lined with relations, and friends, and idle persons.Among them were several who had formerly known Manerville.His disaster, posted on the walls of the town, made him as celebrated as he was in the days of his wealth and fashion.Curiosity was aroused; every one had their word to say about him.Old Mathias accompanied his client to the quay, and his sufferings were sore as he caught a few words of those remarks:—
“你们谁认得站在那边的那个男人吗？就是马蒂亚斯旁边那个，五年前被称作时尚之尊的花花公子，人们都说他在波尔多可是个‘翻手为云覆手为雨’的大人物。” “Who could recognize in that man you see over there, near old Mathias, the dandy who was called the Pink of Fashion five years ago, and made, as they say, ‘fair weather and foul’ in Bordeaux.”
“啊！那个又矮又胖的穿着个羊驼毛大衣的人，看起来真像个车夫——那是保尔·德马内维尔伯爵吗？” “What! that stout, short man in the alpaca overcoat, who looks like a groom,—is that Comte Paul de Manerville?”
“是的，亲爱的，就是那个娶了埃旺热利斯塔小姐的。他现在是完了，一文不名，准备去印度淘金。” “Yes, my dear, the same who married Mademoiselle Evangelista.Here he is, ruined, without a penny to his name, going out to India to look for luck.”
“但是他的财产怎么都没了呢？他过去可是有钱得很呀。” “But how did he ruin himself?he was very rich.”
“唉！巴黎、女人、纸醉金迷的生活、证劵交易所的豪赌——” “Oh! Paris, women, play, luxury, gambling at the Bourse—”
“再说，”另一个接口道，“德马内维尔真是倒霉，缺心眼，像一团纸那么软弱。他身上长出来的毛总是被他人剪走，他真是一无所长。他注定会破产。” “Besides,” said another, “Manerville always was a poor creature; no mind, soft as papier-mache, he’d let anybody shear the wool from his back; incapable of anything, no matter what.He was born to be ruined.”
保尔与老人握手道别后就上船了。马蒂亚斯矗立在码头上，默默地看着他的主顾。保尔依靠在船舷上，用不屑的目光扫视着面前的人群。当水手正准备起锚离开时，保尔注意到马蒂亚斯正挥动着他的手帕，似乎想要说什么。老管家急冲冲地跑到他的主人旁边，好像是有些什么事让马蒂亚斯很激动。保尔叫船长稍等片刻，并派出一艘小船回去搞明白怎么回事。马蒂亚斯身体太虚弱了，上不了船，便递给水手两封信代交给保尔。 Paul wrung the hand of the old man and went on board.Mathias stood upon the pier, looking at his client, who leaned against the shrouds, defying the crowed before him with a glance of contempt.At the moment when the sailors began to weigh anchor, Paul noticed that Mathias was making signals to him with his handkerchief.The old housekeeper had hurried to her master, who seemed to be excited by some sudden event.Paul asked the captain to wait a moment, and send a boat to the pier, which was done.Too feeble himself to go aboard, Mathias gave two letters to a sailor in the boat.
“我的朋友，”他边指着两封信中的一封边说道，”这封信很重要，是信使日夜兼程三十五个小时从巴黎送来的。把这个情况告诉伯爵先生，千万别忘记，或许能改变他的计划。” “My friend,” he said, “this packet” (showing one of the two letters) “is important; it has just arrived by a courier from Paris in thirty-five hours.State this to Monsieur le comte; don’t neglect to do so; it may change his plans.”
“他会下船上岸吗？” “Would he come ashore?”
“也许吧，我的朋友，”公证人不假思索地说道。 “Possibly, my friend,” said the notary, imprudently.
水手在任何地方都是有点儿与大众格格不入的人，他们鄙视身处陆地的人们。这个人碰巧是布列塔尼人，他从马蒂亚斯总管的托付中只看出一件事。 The sailor is, in all lands, a being of a race apart, holding all land-folk in contempt.This one happened to be a bas-Breton, who saw but one thing in Maitre Mathias’s request.
“真的下船上岸！”他边划着浆边想道，“让船长损失一个乘客！如果听这些怪人的话，我们就什么都不用干，就光叫他们上船下船了。他是害怕他的儿子会得感冒吧。” “Come ashore, indeed!” he thought, as he rowed.“Make the captain lose a passenger!If one listened to those walruses we’d have nothing to do but embark and disembark ’em.He’s afraid that son of his will catch cold.”
水手把信递给保尔，对要传达的信息却只字不提。保尔认出了是他妻子和德马尔赛的笔迹，他觉得他知道两个人会写些什么。信中应该大概都是些关心之类的话语，保尔不想受到这些信函的影响，装作毫不在意的样子直接把信塞进了大衣的口袋里。 The sailor gave Paul the letter and said not a word of the message.Recognizing the handwriting of his wife and de Marsay, Paul supposed that he knew what they both would urge upon him.Anxious not to be influenced by offers which he believed their devotion to his welfare would inspire, he put the letters in his pocket unread, with apparent indifference.
此情此景之下，即使是最坚强的人也会陷入悲思之中。保尔难过地与他的老友挥手告别，也在向法国告别，看着波尔多慢慢地从视野中消失。他坐在一圈缆绳的上面。暮色下，他陷入了沉思中。黄昏半明半暗的光线让人疑虑重重；他对未来充满了焦虑。展望未来，到处都是变数和危险，他不禁自问自己是否还有勇气去面对。一想到纳塔莉就要独自生活了，他就隐隐有些担心。他为当前他所做的事情而后悔，他怀念巴黎，怀念那里的生活。突然，他开始晕船了。晕船的感受每个人都知道。虽然没有生命危险，却极其难受，而且能够彻底地摧毁人的意志。一种无法说清的紊乱通过中枢系统使人活力全无，心智再也不能发挥作用。痛苦的人对一切都不在乎了，母亲忘记了自己的孩子，恋人忘记了自己的爱人，强悍的人也像一摊烂泥一样萎靡不振了。有人把保尔背回了船舱，在那里他躺了整整三天。他仰面躺着，不时被水手喂点用水稀释的朗姆酒，接着又恶心呕吐。他什么也不想，只知道昏昏沉沉地睡觉。后来他慢慢地康复了，又恢复了常态。一天早上，他感觉差不多好了。他走上甲板，踱步到船尾，大口地呼吸着海上微带咸味的空气。手刚插进口袋，他摸到了那两封信。他马上打开了妻子寄给他的那封。 Absorbed in the sad thoughts which assail the strongest man under such circumstances, Paul gave way to his grief as he waved his hand to his old friend, and bade farewell to France, watching the steeples of Bordeaux as they fled out of sight.He seated himself on a coil of rope.Night overtook him still lost in thought.With the semi-darkness of the dying day came doubts; he cast an anxious eye into the future.Sounding it, and finding there uncertainty and danger, he asked his soul if courage would fail him.A vague dread seized his mind as he thought of Natalie left wholly to herself; he repented the step he had taken; he regretted Paris and his life there.Suddenly sea-sickness overcame him.Every one knows the effect of that disorder.The most horrible of its sufferings devoid of danger is a complete dissolution of the will.An inexplicable distress relaxes to their very centre the cords of vitality; the soul no longer performs its functions; the sufferer becomes indifferent to everything; the mother forgets her child, the lover his mistress, the strongest man lies prone, like an inert mass.Paul was carried to his cabin, where he stayed three days, lying on his back, gorged with grog by the sailors, or vomiting; thinking of nothing, and sleeping much.Then he revived into a species of convalescence, and returned by degrees to his ordinary condition.The first morning after he felt better he went on deck and passed the poop, breathing in the salt breezes of another atmosphere.Putting his hands into his pockets he felt the letters.At once he opened them, beginning with that of his wife.
要完全理解德马内维尔夫人的信，就必须得先看看保尔离开巴黎时留给妻子的那封信。 In order that the letter of the Comtesse de Manerville be fully understood, it is necessary to give the one which Paul had written to her on the day that he left Paris.
保尔·德马内维尔致妻： From Paul de Manerville to his wife:
我的爱人，当你看到这封信时，我已经远走他乡，或许已经在去印度的船上。我要到那里去赚回我损失殆尽的财富。 My beloved,—When you read this letter I shall be far away from you; perhaps already on the vessel which is to take me to India, where I am going to repair my shattered fortune.
我没有勇气当面告诉你我要远行了。我是欺骗了你，但是也只好如此。如果不这样，你将过上贫苦的生活，你可能希望牺牲你的财产来使我过得舒适些。亲爱的纳塔莉，不要后悔，我也没有任何遗憾。当我带着我赚的百万财富回来时，我要效仿你的父亲，就像他把百万财富放在你母亲脚下一样，我将放在你的脚下，对你说：“我的就是你的。” I have not found courage to tell you of my departure.I have deceived you; but it was best to do so.You would only have been uselessly distressed; you would have wished to sacrifice your fortune, and that I could not have suffered.Dear Natalie, feel no remorse; I have no regrets.When I return with millions I shall imitate your father and lay them at your feet, as he laid his at the feet of your mother, saying to you: “All I have is yours.”
我疯狂地爱着你，纳塔莉。我这样说并不害怕会更扩大你的权力，只有软弱的男人才害怕。自从我认识你的第一天开始，你的权力就是无限大的。我的不幸就是因为我爱你太深。家财一步步地耗尽，我却有种赌徒般的疯狂快乐。钱财不断地减少，我的快乐感却不断地增长。我的每一一点财产换来了你小小的享乐，这让我感到了一种不可名状的幸福。我真希望你有更多的异想天开的念头，我都能全部满足。我知道我正一步步地迈向深渊，但是我却像戴着皇冠的国王那样快乐。这是一般人所无法体会到的。我的行为就好比那些坠入爱河的恋人，他们在湖边的小茅屋里过一两年隐居的生活，然后决定自杀殉情，这样临死时才能体会他们的爱情和幻想的荣誉感。我一直认为他们是完全理智的。 I love you madly, Natalie; I say this without fear that the avowal will lead you to strain a power which none but weak men fear; yours has been boundless from the day I knew you first.My love is the only accomplice in my disaster.I have felt, as my ruin progressed, the delirious joys of a gambler; as the money diminished, so my enjoyment grew.Each fragment of my fortune turned into some little pleasure for you gave me untold happiness.I could have wished that you had more caprices that I might gratify them all.I knew I was marching to a precipice, but I went on crowned with joys of which a common heart knows nothing.I have acted like those lovers who take refuge in a cottage on the shores of some lake for a year or two, resolved to kill themselves at last; dying thus in all the glory of their illusions and their love.I have always thought such persons infinitely sensible.
你对我的快乐和我的牺牲都一无所知。快乐的最高境界就是不让自己的爱人知道要满足她的愿望需要付出多大的代价。如今我可以把这些秘密都告诉你了，因为当你拿着这封充满爱意的信纸时，我已离你远去。尽管我已经失去了你的感激这笔财富，但当我跟你谈起这些事情时，我也不会再感觉到那种揪心的痛楚，让我无力承受。而且，我的爱人，这样回忆我们的过去，难道不是一种明智的计划吗？这样是不是可以使我们的爱情继续发展下去呢？——不过我们不需要这样的强心剂！我们之间的爱不需要任何证明，那是一种不在乎时间和空间的爱情，我们爱的就是对方那个人。 You have known nothing of my pleasures or my sacrifices.The greatest joy of all was to hide from the one beloved the cost of her desires.I can reveal these secrets to you now, for when you hold this paper, heavy with love, I shall be far away.Though I lose the treasures of your gratitude, I do not suffer that contraction of the heart which would disable me if I spoke to you of these matters.Besides, my own beloved, is there not a tender calculation in thus revealing to you the history of the past?Does it not extend our love into the future?—But we need no such supports!We love each other with a love to which proof is needless,—a love which takes no note of time or distance, but lives of itself alone.
唉！纳塔莉，我刚刚看着你入睡，就像孩子一样熟睡着，信赖地把你的手搭在我这边。我在枕头上留下了一滴泪水，那枕头见证了我们多少珍贵的快乐。怀着那样的态度和信念，我无牵无挂地离开了你。我要去为我们的爱情赢得巨额的金钱，以便满足你所有的欲望，不让担忧笼罩或干扰我们的快乐。我们的生活多么快乐，这点你我都无法否认。我的责任是去赚到足够的财富。我是个男人，我有这样的勇气。 Ah! Natalie, I have just looked at you asleep, trustful, restful as a little child, your hand stretched toward me.I left a tear upon the pillow which has known our precious joys.I leave you without fear, on the faith of that attitude; I go to win the future of our love by bringing home to you a fortune large enough to gratify your every taste, and let no shadow of anxiety disturb our joys.Neither you nor I can do without enjoyments in the life we live.To me belongs the task of providing the necessary fortune.I am a man; and I have courage.
也许你还想跟着我去吧。所以我没跟你提及我所坐的船只名称、出行的港口和出发的日期。等我走后，你已不可能追得到我时，我的一位朋友将告知你所有的一切。 Perhaps you might seek to follow me.For that reason I conceal from you the name of the vessel, the port from which I sail, and the day of sailing.After I am gone, when too late to follow me, a friend will tell you all.
纳塔莉！我对你的爱是无限的！我爱你如同一个母亲爱她的孩子，如同情人爱着他的情妇，完全无私地爱着你。苦活累活由我来干，美妙快乐由你来享；痛苦厄运我来承担，幸福生活你来享受。找点乐子，继续奢华的生活习惯吧。去戏院看戏剧，上剧院看歌剧，出去交际，出席舞会；我给你完全自由的生活。亲爱的天使，当你回到我们的爱巢，在那里我们曾享受了五年的爱情之果。思念你的朋友吧，想念一下我吧，在我的心中停驻片刻吧。 Natalie! my affection is boundless.I love you as a mother loves her child, as a lover loves his mistress, with absolute unselfishness.To me the toil, to you the pleasures; to me all sufferings, to you all happiness.Amuse yourself; continue your habits of luxury; go to theatres and operas, enjoy society and balls; I leave you free for all things.Dear angel, when you return to this nest where for five years we have tasted the fruits which love has ripened think of your friend; think for a moment of me, and rest upon my heart.
这就是我对你的要求。对于我来说，你就是我永远的思念！当我在炎热的气候下奔走劳作，当我面对必须克服的困难障碍时，或者当我疲于奋斗时，我只寄希望于能早日返家。我一定会想念你的，你就是我的生命——上帝赐予我的生命！是的，我就是为你而活。我每天都对自己说，你是无忧无虑、快乐幸福的。正如我们日常生活有日有夜、有睡有醒，我曾领略过巴黎阳光明媚的日子，现在要去印度过劳顿苦作的日子了——痛苦的梦境，快乐的现实；我就要去生活在现实世界里了，过去的日子就像一个梦一样过去了。我有过美好的回忆！我将一遍又一遍地重温我们这五年来如诗般的美妙生活。我还记得那些日子，你快乐地穿着新衣服或戴上新首饰，我看着你时也是眼前一亮。是的，亲爱的天使，我作为一个男人离开了，发誓要去干出一番事业。而事业的成功，会为男人带来美丽的情人。噢！我的心肝宝贝，纳塔莉，把我当作你所信仰的宗教一样记在心间吧。就一直做那个我看见的沉睡中的孩子吧！如果你背叛我的信任，我盲目的信任，你也无需害怕我发怒——这一点你可以放心，我会静静地死去。但是一个被丈夫宽容对待的妻子，反而不会去欺骗丈夫的——因为女人并不卑鄙。她会戏弄一个暴君，但是不会轻易地背叛，不会致人于死地，她不会这么做的——不，绝不会！我不会这样想的。请原谅我的呼声，一个男人发自内心的呼声！ That is all I ask of you.For myself, dear eternal thought of mine! whether under burning skies, toiling for both of us, I face obstacles to vanquish, or whether, weary with the struggle, I rest my mind on hopes of a return, I shall think of you alone; of you who are my life,—my blessed life!Yes, I shall live in you.I shall tell myself daily that you have no troubles, no cares; that you are happy.As in our natural lives of day and night, of sleeping and waking, I shall have sunny days in Paris, and nights of toil in India,—a painful dream, a joyful reality; and I shall live so utterly in that reality that my actual life will pass as a dream.I shall have memories!I shall recall, line by line, strophe by strophe, our glorious five years’ poem.I shall remember the days of your pleasure in some new dress or some adornment which made you to my eyes a fresh delight.Yes, dear angel, I go like a man vowed to some great emprize, the guerdon of which, if success attend him, is the recovery of his beautiful mistress.Oh! my precious love, my Natalie, keep me as a religion in your heart.Be the child that I have just seen asleep!If you betray my confidence, my blind confidence, you need not fear my anger—be sure of that; I should die silently.But a wife does not deceive the man who leaves her free—for woman is never base.She tricks a tyrant; but an easy treachery, which would kill its victim, she will not commit—No, no!I will not think of it.Forgive this cry, this single cry, so natural to the heart of man!
亲爱的妻子，你将看到德马尔赛，他是我们房子的承租人，不过房子的所有权还是你的。这种名义上的出租可以避免无谓的损失。我们的债主还不知道我们肯定还得了钱，只不过时间上得拖延一点。否则他们会扣押我们房产的家具和房屋的临时所有权。对德马尔赛好点儿，我完全相信他的能力和他的忠诚。把他当作你的保护神和顾问，有什么尽管叫他去做。不管他多忙，他总会找出时间来帮你的。我把财产清算和偿还债务问题都交给他打理。如果他提出日后需要用到一笔数目的钱，我希望你能如数把钱给他。记住，我并不是把你交给德马尔赛，而是让你自己照顾自己。我也并不是把他强加于你。 Dear love, you will see de Marsay; he is now the lessee of our house, and he will leave you in possession of it.This nominal lease was necessary to avoid a useless loss.Our creditors, ignorant that their payment is a question of time only, would otherwise have seized the furniture and the temporary possession of the house.Be kind to de Marsay; I have the most entire confidence in his capacity and his loyalty.Take him as your defender and adviser, make him your slave.However occupied, he will always find time to be devoted to you.I have placed the liquidation of my affairs and the payment of the debts in his hands.If he should advance some sum of which he should later feel in need I rely on you to pay it back.Remember, however, that I do not leave you to de Marsay, but to yourself; I do not seek to impose him upon you.
哎！我在你身边只能再呆一个小时了，不能再用来写这封信了——我要数着你的呼吸，我尽力地从你睡梦中轻微的动作来揣测你的思想。我希望我们能血脉相融，你能成为我身体的一部分。那样你的思想就是我的思想，你的心也就我的了——你睡梦中双唇发出的呢喃仿佛就是对我温柔的回应。你永远都要像此刻一样安详和美丽！啊！我多希望我能有神话故事中那样的魔力，我离开时挥挥我的魔杖让你睡去，回来后用我的吻将你唤醒。 Alas! I have but an hour more to stay beside you; I cannot spend that hour in writing business—I count your breaths; I try to guess your thoughts in the slight motions of your sleep.I would I could infuse my blood into your veins that you might be a part of me, my thought your thought, and your heart mine—A murmur has just escaped your lips as though it were a soft reply.Be calm and beautiful forever as you are now!Ah! would that I possessed that fabulous fairy power which, with a wand, could make you sleep while I am absent, until, returning, I should wake you with a kiss.
我多么爱你，需要多大的决心和毅力才能离开眼前的你啊！再见了，我唯一钟爱的人。你可怜的时尚之尊就要被暴风带走了——好运的翅膀会把他带回你的身边。不，我的妮妮，我不是在跟你说永别，因为我永远不会弃你不顾。难道你不是我所有行为的灵魂吗？我所有的努力难道不就是希望为你创造一份坚不可摧的幸福吗？难道不是这个愿望指引着我走的每一步吗？不管在什么地方，你将永远地陪伴在我左右。啊！照亮我前程的不是印度的骄阳，而是你火一般明媚的双眼。当爱人不在身边，女人能过多快活就多快活。你也应该这样。我最后亲吻了你温柔的嘴唇，我多希望你不是被动的接受这一吻啊！但是我的妮妮，我的心上人，我不会去唤醒你的。你醒来后，会在你的前额找到一滴泪水——把这滴泪水当作你的护身符吧！思念他吧，思念那个远离你，也许会为你而死的人吧。那个把你托付给上帝的人，与其说他是你的丈夫，不如说他是一个深爱着你的情人。 How much I must love you, how much energy of soul I must possess, to leave you as I see you now!Adieu, my cherished one.Your poor Pink of Fashion is blown away by stormy winds, but—the wings of his good luck shall waft him back to you.No, my Ninie, I am not bidding you farewell, for I shall never leave you.Are you not the soul of my actions?Is not the hope of returning with happiness indestructible for YOU the end and aim of my endeavor?Does it not lead my every step?You will be with me everywhere.Ah! it will not be the sun of India, but the fire of your eyes that lights my way.Therefore be happy—as happy as a woman can be without her lover.I would the last kiss that I take from those dear lips were not a passive one; but, my Ninie, my adored one, I will not wake you.When you wake, you will find a tear upon your forehead—make it a talisman!Think, think of him who may, perhaps, die for you, far from you; think less of the husband than of the lover who confides you to God.
德马内维尔伯爵夫人致夫： From the Comtesse de Manerville to her husband:
我的爱人——看完你的信，我是多么痛苦啊！难道你不征求我的同意就有权利作出这样的决定，一个同样影响我们两人的决定？你是自由的吗？你不是属于我的吗？如果你非要走，为什么不能让我跟随着你？保尔，你这是告诉我，我对你来说并不是不可或缺的。我到底做了什么，要这样被你夺走我的权利？财产没了，我肯定也是有责任的。我的奢侈品花了很多的钱。我们一起度过了五年快乐而无忧无虑的生活，你却使我诅咒过去那种生活。知道了你若干年内都不会回法国，我根本没办法活下去。你在印度赚一笔财富需要多久的时间？到时你还会不会回来？ Dear, beloved one,—Your letter has plunged me into affliction.Had you the right to take this course, which must affect us equally, without consulting me?Are you free?Do you not belong to me?If you must go, why should I not follow you?You show me, Paul, that I am not indispensable to you.What have I done, to be deprived of my rights?Surely I count for something in this ruin.My luxuries have weighed somewhat in the scale.You make me curse the happy, careless life we have led for the last five years.To know that you are banished from France for years is enough to kill me.How soon can a fortune be made in India?Will you ever return?
当时我本能地拒绝我母亲和你提出的什么财产分立，你们却一意孤行。那时候我跟你说了什么？我不是提醒过你这样做会使你颜面尽失、威名扫地的吗？直到后来，你非常生气，我才随了你愿。 I was right when I refused, with instinctive obstinacy, that separation as to property which my mother and you were so determined to carry out.What did I tell you then?Did I not warn you that it was casting a reflection upon you, and would ruin your credit?It was not until you were really angry that I gave way.
我亲爱的保尔，在我看来，你从来没有像此刻一样高尚伟大。永不气馁，开始勇敢地去追逐财富！只有你这样的性格和你这样的力量才能做到。我完全支持你。一个男人诚实地承认自己的弱点，因为爱，因为一种无法抵挡的激情，他挥霍了自己的财富。出于同样的爱和激情，他决定要重建他的财富。噢，保尔，那个男人太高尚了！去吧，什么都不用担心，克服所有的困难。不用怀疑你的纳塔莉——因为怀疑她就是怀疑你自己。可怜的宝贝，你是想活在我心上吗？而我也想留在你心里。我不会呆在这里，不管你到哪里，我都将伴你左右。 My dear Paul, never have you been so noble in my eyes as you are at this moment.To despair of nothing, to start courageously to seek a fortune!Only your character, your strength of mind could do it.I sit at your feet.A man who avows his weakness with your good faith, who rebuilds his fortune from the same motive that made him wreck it, for love’s sake, for the sake of an irresistible passion, oh, Paul, that man is sublime!Therefore, fear nothing; go on, through all obstacles, not doubting your Natalie—for that would be doubting yourself.Poor darling, you mean to live in me?And I shall ever be in you.I shall not be here; I shall be wherever you are, wherever you go.
虽然你的信使我体会到了切肤之痛，但是也让我的内心充满了快乐——你让我体验到了这两种极端的感觉！看到你是如此爱我，我自豪地知道你也能感受到我对你的爱。有时，我会想我爱远远超过你爱我。现在我承认我的想法是错误的。在你所有的优点上，还可以再加上这个令人愉悦的长处——深爱我。在信中，你敞开了你的心扉。那封珍贵的信在你不在我身边的日子里，将永远留在我的心中。而我的心思也在其中；那封信是我的荣耀。 Though your letter has caused me the keenest pain, it has also filled me with joy—you have made me know those two extremes!Seeing how you love me, I have been proud to learn that my love is truly felt.Sometimes I have thought that I loved you more than you loved me.Now, I admit myself vanquished, you have added the delightful superiority—of loving—to all the others with which you are blest.That precious letter in which your soul reveals itself will lie upon my heart during all your absence; for my soul, too, is in it; that letter is my glory.
我要到朗斯特拉克和我母亲一起生活。我将与世隔绝，过着勤俭节约的生活，以便存点钱来帮你还清债务。从今天开始，保尔，我已不再是过去那个女子了。我将告别社交界，我的快乐将悉数与你分享。而且保尔，我应该离开巴黎去过点儿安逸的生活。亲爱的人，你很快将有一个崇高的理由去积攒你的财富。如果你需要勇气以鼓励你前行，我永远在这里。你猜不到吧？我们就要有孩子啦。你最渴望的事情就要来到了。我不敢在没有把握之前告诉你，那样就太令人难过啦——在这件事上，我们不是已经伤透了心吗？这则好消息，我必须等万无一失才敢告诉你。今天我确定此事，我非常高兴能在你的哀伤中加入这份快乐。 I shall go to live at Lanstrac with my mother.I die to the world; I will economize my income and pay your debts to their last farthing.From this day forth, Paul, I am another woman.I bid farewell forever to society; I will have no pleasures that you cannot share.Besides, Paul, I ought to leave Paris and live in retirement.Dear friend, you will soon have a noble reason to make your fortune.If your courage needed a spur you would find it in this.Cannot you guess?We shall have a child.Your cherished desires are granted.I feared to give you one of those false hopes which hurt so much—have we not had grief enough already on that score?I was determined not to be mistaken in this good news.To-day I feel certain, and it makes me happy to shed this joy upon your sorrows.
今天早上我像往常一样，以为你还在家，我去教堂做礼拜。一切都还顺利，我哪里预测得到灾难已经降临？当我离开教堂时，正好碰到了我的母亲。她听说你的遭遇，特地驱车而来，带来她的三万法郎的积蓄，希望能帮你一把。啊！她多么为你着想啊，保尔！当时我很高兴，回到家中想趁着在温室中吃早饭的机会告诉你这个好消息。在温室里，我订了你最喜欢吃的甜点。此时，奥古斯丁把你的信带给了我。我们刚刚同床共枕了一夜，一觉醒来却收到你的一封信！我顿觉不寒而栗，就像一场梦！我看完了你的信！我边哭边看着你写的信，我的母亲也在旁边陪着我流泪。我就像垂死的人一般。多深的爱情，多大的勇气，多少幸福，多么悲伤的境遇啊！心灵上拥有巨大的财富，而物质利益上却是倾家荡产！我对你的崇高的品德敬仰不已，然而却得跟你短暂的分离。什么样的女人又受得了这样的情感风暴呢？如果把你的手放在我的胸口，你可以感觉到我的心在为你而悸动；你已不在我身边，不能再用我喜欢的目光看着我；不能与我一同展望美好的未来；我不能陪在你身边，你亲爱的纳塔莉不能再用她的爱抚缓解你的痛苦了！我真希望马上出发，飞到你的身边，永伴你左右。但是我的母亲告诉我，你第二天就要乘船离开波尔多。要赶上你，我只能做邮车。然而以我现在的状态车马劳顿地去追赶你太疯狂了，将危及我们的未来。我受不了感情上这么大的波动，开始生病了。现在我正躺在床上给你写信。 This morning, fearing nothing and thinking you still at home, I went to the Assumption; all things smiled upon me; how could I foresee misfortune?As I left the church I met my mother; she had heard of your distress, and came, by post, with all her savings, thirty thousand francs, hoping to help you.Ah! what a heart is hers, Paul!I felt joyful, and hurried home to tell you this good news, and to breakfast with you in the greenhouse, where I ordered just the dainties that you like.Well, Augustine brought me your letter,—a letter from you, when we had slept together!A cold fear seized me; it was like a dream!I read your letter!I read it weeping, and my mother shared my tears.I was half-dead.Such love, such courage, such happiness, such misery!The richest fortunes of the heart, and the momentary ruin of all interests!To lose you at a moment when my admiration of your greatness thrilled me!what woman could have resisted such a tempest of emotion?To know you far away when your hand upon my heart would have stilled its throbbings; to feel that YOU were not here to give me that look so precious to me, to rejoice in our new hopes; that I was not with you to soften your sorrows by those caresses which made your Natalie so dear to you!I wished to start, to follow you, to fly to you.But my mother told me you had taken passage in a ship which leaves Bordeaux tomorrow, that I could not reach you except by post, and, moreover, that it was madness in my present state to risk our future by attempting to follow you.I could not bear such violent emotions; I was taken ill, and am writing to you now in bed.
我母亲正竭尽所能阻止那些对你进行诽谤的流言蜚语。旺德奈斯兄弟、查尔斯和菲利克斯都真诚地维护着你，但是你的朋友德马尔赛却不把这当回事。他嘲笑那些造谣之人，而不是回击他们。当有人来势汹汹地挑衅时，他只是轻轻地挡一下。我不喜欢他这样的方式。你没有看错他吧？不过，我会服从你的，我会把他当作我的朋友。我的宝贝，只要是有关你的名誉的事情，你尽可放心。你的名誉不就是我的名誉吗？我的钻石首饰都会用来抵押钱财。母亲和我，我们会动用所有资源来帮你偿还欠款，还会尽力赎回玫瑰美人葡萄庄园。我的母亲像个律师一样对生意很在行。她对你颇有微词，说你有什么困难从来都不跟她说。如果不是为了取悦你，她就不会买入红谷粒领地了。而如果不买那块地，她本可以借给你三万法郎外加买地的钱。她对你的决定感到很失望，而且她很担心印度的气候会影响你的健康状况。她恳求你要保持清醒，不要上了女人的圈套——说到这里，我不禁笑起来，因为我很信赖你，同样也信赖我自己。忠诚的你将带着财富回到我身边。只有我了解你女子般的细腻感情和内心深处的情绪，也正是这些感情和情绪使你宛如一朵在人间盛开的天堂之花。波尔多给你起这个花一般的绰号是对的。 My mother is doing all she can to stop certain calumnies which seem to have got about on your disaster.The Vandenesses, Charles and Felix, have earnestly defended you; but your friend de Marsay treats the affair satirically.He laughs at your accusers instead of replying to them.I do not like his way of lightly brushing aside such serious attacks.Are you not deceived in him?However, I will obey you; I will make him my friend.Do not be anxious, my adored one, on the points that concern your honor; is it not mine as well?My diamonds shall be pledged; we intend, mamma and I, to employ our utmost resources in the payment of your debts; and we shall try to buy back your vineyard at Belle–Rose.My mother, who understands business like a lawyer, blames you very much for not having told her of your embarrassments.She would not have bought—thinking to please you—the Grainrouge domain, and then she could have lent you that money as well as the thirty thousand francs she brought with her.She is in despair at your decision; she fears the climate of India for your health.She entreats you to be sober, and not to let yourself be trapped by women—That made me laugh; I am as sure of you as I am of myself.You will return to me rich and faithful.I alone know your feminine delicacy, and the secret sentiments which make you a human flower worthy of the gardens of heaven.The Bordeaux people were right when they gave you your floral nickname.
但是啊！谁又来照顾我这枝娇弱的花朵呢？我的心被各种可怕的念头撕得四分五裂。我——他的妻子——纳塔莉在这里，而他可能在远方受苦。而我却分担不了你的痛苦，你的烦恼和你的危险！你的心里话向谁去说呢？没有了那个能够听你倾诉一切的耳朵，你怎么活呢？被暴风带走的亲爱的害羞草啊，离开了你的故土，在另外一片土壤上，你还能茁壮成长吗？ But alas! who will take care of my delicate flower?My heart is rent with dreadful ideas.I, his wife, Natalie, I am here, and perhaps he suffers far away from me!And not to share your pains, your vexations, your dangers!In whom will you confide? how will you live without that ear into which you have hitherto poured all?Dear, sensitive plant, swept away by this storm, will you be able to survive in another soil than your native land?
我仿佛已经孤独了好几个世纪了。我为之痛哭。因为我是你倾家荡产的罪魁祸首！这会对一个痴情女子的思想造成多大的影响啊！你对我就好像对一个小孩，满足小孩所有的要求，或者说把我当作高雅的情妇，轻率的年轻人愿意为此花光自己所有的财富。啊！这样的纵容其实是一种侮辱。我不穿华服艳妆，不再参加舞会，不再看歌剧，不再在社交场合出风头，你以为这样我就活不了吗？难道我是如此轻佻的一个女人吗？难道你认为我不会深思熟虑，不会像助你享乐一样助你发家致富吗？要不是你不在我身边，要不是你也心情郁闷，我真要对你的无礼好好训斥一番。为什么要那样贬低你的妻子？天啊！我出入交际场合究竟为何呢？还不是为了给你脸上添光——我精心打扮自己，也同样是为了你，这个你是知道的。如果我做错了什么，我已经收到残酷的惩罚了。你的离去，也算是为我们以前的生活赎罪了。 It seems to me that I have been alone for centuries.I have wept sorely.To be the cause of your ruin!What a text for the thoughts of a loving woman!You treated me like a child to whom we give all it asks, or like a courtesan, allowed by some thoughtless youth to squander his fortune.Ah! such indulgence was, in truth, an insult.Did you think I could not live without fine dresses, balls and operas and social triumphs?Am I so frivolous a woman?Do you think me incapable of serious thought, of ministering to your fortune as I have to your pleasures?If you were not so far away, and so unhappy, I would blame you for that impertinence.Why lower your wife in that way?Good heavens! what induced me to go into society at all?—to flatter your vanity; I adorned myself for you, as you well know.If I did wrong, I am punished, cruelly; your absence is a harsh expiation of our mutual life.
也许我们过去的生活太美满了，要为此付出巨大的代价——现在就是偿还代价的时候了。对于我，剩下的只有孤独。是的，我要住到朗斯特拉克去，生活在你父亲开发的土地上去，生活在你装饰豪华的城堡中去。在那里，我将和我的母亲、我的孩子生活在一起，等着你回来。每天清晨和傍晚向你送出我们的祈福。记住我们的爱就是你驱恶辟邪的护身符。你若是信任我，我也会同样地信任你。我还能再写下什么宽慰之语——我破碎的心是如此凄凉，未来若干年我得独自度过，就像一片尚待穿越的沙漠。但是绝不！我还不是最不幸的人，沙漠中的水源就是我们的儿子——是的，肯定是个儿子，不是吗？ Perhaps my happiness was too complete; it had to be paid by some great trial—and here it is.There is nothing now for me but solitude.Yes, I shall live at Lanstrac, the place your father laid out, the house you yourself refurnished so luxuriously.There I shall live, with my mother and my child, and await you,—sending you daily, night and morning, the prayers of all.Remember that our love is a talisman against all evil.I have no more doubt of you than you can have of me.What comfort can I put into this letter,—I so desolate, so broken, with the lonely years before me, like a desert to cross.But no! I am not utterly unhappy; the desert will be brightened by our son,—yes, it must be a son, must it not?
现在，别了，我的爱人。我们的爱情和我们的祷告将永远跟随着你。我滴在这封信上的泪水将告诉你许多我纸笔无法表达的心思。我在这张纸的角落里放进了我的亲吻，看到了吧！就在下面。带走这些吻吧。 And now, adieu, my own beloved; our love and prayers will follow you.The tears you see upon this paper will tell you much that I cannot write.I kiss you on this little square of paper, see! below.Take those kisses from
你的纳塔莉。 Your Natalie.
这封信让保尔陷入幻想中，回想起过去快乐的日子和相爱的片段。一个男人越是幸福，越是战栗着害怕失去幸福。对于心地善良的人来说——这种善良本身就是某种程度的弱点——妒忌与不安是和幸福以及幸福的程度成正比的。性格坚强的人从不妒忌，也不恐惧。妒忌是猜疑的体现，而恐惧是狭隘的表现。无限的信任是伟人的主要特性。如果他因此上当受骗了（因为力量和软弱都可以致人被骗），他将把藐视当作斧头，并用之砍出一条路来。不过，这样的伟大是很难碰见的。我们脆弱的身体由信念支持着，一个神秘的声音却在否认一切，我们中间的哪一个没有经历过被这种被信念遗弃的感觉呢？保尔回顾过去，想起了几件千真万确发生过的事实，半信半疑起来。保尔陷入苦思当中，一方面他不愿轻信妻子的所言所语，但是另一方面他对纳塔莉却有着纯洁的爱情和完全的信任。他一遍又一遍地阅读着这封冗长的来信，仍然搞不清楚妻子究竟意欲何在。有时，简短、有力的句型同冗长的辞藻一样，也能表达伟大而真实的爱情。 This letter threw Paul into a reverie caused as much by memories of the past as by these fresh assurances of love.The happier a man is, the more he trembles.In souls which are exclusively tender—and exclusive tenderness carries with it a certain amount of weakness—jealousy and uneasiness exist in direct proportion to the amount of the happiness and its extent.Strong souls are neither jealous nor fearful; jealousy is doubt, fear is meanness.Unlimited belief is the principal attribute of a great man.If he is deceived (for strength as well as weakness may make a man a dupe) his contempt will serve him as an axe with which to cut through all.This greatness, however, is the exception.Which of us has not known what it is to be abandoned by the spirit which sustains our frail machine, and to hearken to that mysterious Voice denying all?Paul, his mind going over the past, and caught here and there by irrefutable facts, believed and doubted all.Lost in thought, a prey to an awful and involuntary incredulity, which was combated by the instincts of his own pure love and his faith in Natalie, he read and re-read that wordy letter, unable to decide the question which it raised either for or against his wife.Love is sometimes as great and true when smothered in words as it is in brief, strong sentences.
