为了理解保尔·德马内维尔未来的处境，我们必须想想他此刻正在漂洋过海，正如他正飘浮在自己的过去中一样。看着面前一望无际的海水和万里无云的天空，他回顾这半辈子的人生，结束了刚才的幻想，从怀疑回归信仰。他那纯洁的、不掺杂任何杂物的、完整的基督教的信仰和对爱人的眷恋，使他内心的呼声更加坚定。 To understand the situation into which Paul de Manerville was about to enter we must think of him as he was at this moment, floating upon the ocean as he floated upon his past, looking back upon the years of his life as he looked at the limitless water and cloudless sky about him, and ending his reverie by returning, through tumults of doubt, to faith, the pure, unalloyed and perfect faith of the Christian and the lover, which enforced the voice of his faithful heart.
这里有必要把他离开巴黎时写给德马尔赛的信公开，他的朋友收到信后通过老马蒂亚斯在码头转交了回信。 It is necessary to give here his own letter to de Marsay written on leaving Paris, to which his friend replied in the letter he received through old Mathias from the dock:—
保尔·德马内维尔伯爵致亨利·德马尔赛侯爵： From Comte Paul de Manerville to Monsieur le Marquis Henri de Marsay:
亨利，我要告诉你一句可以跟朋友讲的最重要的话：我破产了。当你看到这封信时，我应该已经坐着“艾米丽美人号”航行在波尔多到加尔各答的海洋上了。 Henri,—I have to say to you one of the most vital words a man can say to his friend:—I am ruined.When you read this I shall be on the point of sailing from Bordeaux to Calcutta on the brig “Belle–Amelie.”
你的公证人将给你一纸契约，你签名后就具有法律效应。契约名义上规定，我把房子租给你六年。请送一张契约的副本给我妻子。我也是被迫采取这些预防措施的，可以让纳塔莉继续住在她自己的房子里，而不至于被债主赶走。 You will find in the hands of your notary a deed which only needs your signature to be legal.In it, I lease my house to you for six years at a nominal rent.Send a duplicate of that deed to my wife.I am forced to take this precaution that Natalie may continue to live in her own home without fear of being driven out by creditors.
契约中同时规定我的限嗣继承财产今后四年的收入都将直接给你，总数达十五万法郎。因此我恳求你先借十五万法郎给我，以汇票的形式寄到波尔多我的公证人马蒂亚斯总管家中。我的妻子将给你一张我署过名的保证书，以此证明你有权获得此收入。如果限嗣继承财产所带来的收益没有像我之前预料的一样及时偿付借款，那就等我回来后再清算。我向你借的这笔钱对我到印度去发财致富是必不可少的。以我对你的了解，出发的前夜我应该能在波尔多收到这笔钱。 I also convey to you by deed the income of my share of the entailed property for four years; the whole amounting to one hundred and fifty thousand francs, which sum I beg you to lend me and to send in a bill of exchange on some house in Bordeaux to my notary, Maitre Mathias.My wife will give you her signature to this paper as an endorsement of your claim to my income.If the revenues of the entail do not pay this loan as quickly as I now expect, you and I will settle on my return.The sum I ask for is absolutely necessary to enable me to seek my fortune in India; and if I know you, I shall receive it in Bordeaux the night before I sail.
如果你处于我今天的处境，我也会这么做的。破产之前，我苦苦支撑到最后一刻，没人知道我的财产状况。我波尔多的财产被扣押了，当这则消息传到巴黎的时候，我已经把一张十万的汇票兑成了现金，想靠这些钱来搏一把。如果当时运气好的话，或许我还能东山再起。结果我全输了。 I have acted as you would have acted in my place.I held firm to the last moment, letting no one suspect my ruin.Before the news of the seizure of my property at Bordeaux reached Paris, I had attempted, with one hundred thousand francs which I obtained on notes, to recover myself by play.Some lucky stroke might still have saved me.I lost.
我的身家财富究竟是如何毁掉的呢？我故意的，亨利。婚后第一个月，我就知道这种奢侈的生活方式是维持不了多久的。我早知道会是这样的后果，但是我选择了视而不见。我无法开口对妻子说：“我们离开巴黎，去朗斯特拉克生活吧。”我为了她倾家荡产，就像男人们为情妇而破产一样，但这一点我心知肚明。跟你说句心里话，我既不是傻瓜，也不是软弱的男人。一个傻瓜不会眼睁睁地看着自己被激情所控制，一个破产的男人并没有对着自己的太阳穴嘣一枪，而是去印度重新积累财富，这个男人算不上软弱的。 How have I ruined myself?By my own will, Henri.From the first month of my married life I saw that I could not keep up the style in which I started.I knew the result; but I chose to shut my eyes; I could not say to my wife, “We must leave Paris and live at Lanstrac.”I have ruined myself for her as men ruin themselves for a mistress, but I knew it all along.Between ourselves, I am neither a fool nor a weak man.A fool does not let himself be ruled with his eyes open by a passion; and a man who starts for India to reconstruct his fortune, instead of blowing out his brains, is not weak.
没赚到我要的财富，我决不回来。但是，亲爱的朋友，我赚钱只是为了她，因为我要离开至少六年的时间，我不想冒着被欺骗的危险，所以我只能把妻子托付给你了。我找不到比你更恰当的监护人了。她没有孩子，可能会陷入爱慕者的圈套。亨利！我疯狂地爱着她，卑微地、没有尊严地爱着她。我想就算她有不忠行为，我也是能宽容她的，倒不是因为我确信能报复，而是因为如果我无法给予她幸福的话，我会自杀以赋予她自由和幸福。不过我有什么好怕的呢？纳塔莉对我有一种友谊，而这种友谊是独立于我们的爱情之外的，却能够保持我们的爱情。我把她当作被宠坏的小孩来对待。我非常乐意为她牺牲，一个接着一个。这对于我来说是很自然的事情。她不会欺骗我的，如果她真骗我，那可就是个魔鬼了。投入了爱情，得到的应该也是爱情。 I shall return rich, or I shall never return at all.Only, my dear friend, as I want wealth solely for her, as I must be absent six years at least, and as I will not risk being duped in any way, I confide to you my wife.I know no better guardian.Being childless, a lover might be dangerous to her.Henri! I love her madly, basely, without proper pride.I would forgive her, I think, an infidelity, not because I am certain of avenging it, but because I would kill myself to leave her free and happy—since I could not make her happiness myself.But what have I to fear?Natalie feels for me that friendship which is independent of love, but which preserves love.I have treated her like a petted child.I took such delight in my sacrifices, one led so naturally to another, that she can never be false; she would be a monster if she were.Love begets love.
唉！我可以什么都跟你说吗，亨利？我刚刚写了封信给她，告诉她我是充满希望、喜笑颜开地离开的。我心中没有妒忌，没有疑惑，也没有恐惧——总而言之，就像一封儿子写给母亲的信，告诉母亲他毅然赴死。我的上帝啊！德马尔赛，我写这封信时真是心如刀绞！我算得上是这个世界上最倒霉的人了。是的，是的，我哭得牙齿都咯咯作响！我承认我是一个处于绝望中的情人。如果可以选的话，我情愿在她窗下扫六年大街，也不愿以六年分别的代价去做一个百万富翁。我深陷苦海之中，只是从一种痛苦过渡到另一种痛苦。除非我能收到你的来信，告诉我你接受我的托付。只有你才能执行和完成如此重托。 Alas! Shall I tell you all, my dear Henri?I have just written her a letter in which I let her think that I go with heart of hope and brow serene; that neither jealousy, nor doubt, nor fear is in my soul,—a letter, in short, such as a son might write to his mother, aware that he is going to his death.Good God! de Marsay, as I wrote it hell was in my soul!I am the most wretched man on earth.Yes, yes, to you the cries, to you the grinding of my teeth!I avow myself to you a despairing lover; I would rather live these six years sweeping the streets beneath her windows than return a millionaire at the end of them—if I could choose.I suffer agony; I shall pass from pain to pain until I hear from you that you will take the trust which you alone can fulfil or accomplish.
噢！我亲爱的德马尔赛，这个女人是我生命中不可缺少的部分；她就是我的太阳，就是我的空气。好好地保护她不受伤害，即使她不愿意，也要使她忠诚于我。是的，只要有半点幸福，我也心满意足。看好她，你就是她的监护人，我完全信任你。你要跟她说清，背叛是下流和卑鄙的行为，那样的话她就跟其他的庸脂俗粉没什么区别了，只有贞节才能证明心灵的高尚。 Oh! My dear de Marsay, this woman is indispensable to my life; she is my sun, my atmosphere.Take her under your shield and buckler, keep her faithful to me, even if she wills it not.Yes, I could be satisfied with a half-happiness.Be her guardian, her chaperon, for I could have no distrust of you.Prove to her that in betraying me she would do a low and vulgar thing, and be no better than the common run of women; tell her that faithfulness will prove her lofty spirit.
她的钱可能还能够继续维持她奢华舒适的生活。如果她想找什么乐趣或者有什么突发奇想却无法满足，请你出钱满足她的要求，不用担心，我会衣锦还乡的。 She probably has fortune enough to continue her life of luxury and ease.But if she lacks a pleasure, if she has caprices which she cannot satisfy, be her banker, and do not fear, I will return with wealth.
不过，这些担心都是杞人忧天！纳塔莉是个纯洁美丽和坚守妇道的天使。当初菲利克斯·德旺德奈斯深深地爱上了她并疯狂地追求她时，我仅仅提醒了她一句，叫她提防危险。她马上对我深表感激，使我感动得热泪盈眶。她说有人登门拜访，作为一个有名声和尊严的女子不应拒人于千里之外，但是她知道怎样打发走这个男人。事实上，她说到做到，此后待他都是冷若冰霜，最后这事也就圆满地画上了个句号。我跟她结婚这么久，从没有对任何话题发生过争辩——的确，如果友好的交谈也是争辩的话。 But, after all, these fears are in vain!Natalie is an angel of purity and virtue.When Felix de Vandenesse fell deeply in love with her and began to show her certain attentions, I had only to let her see the danger, and she instantly thanked me so affectionately that I was moved to tears.She said that her dignity and reputation demanded that she should not close her doors abruptly to any man, but that she knew well how to dismiss him.She did, in fact, receive him so coldly that the affair all ended for the best.We have never had any other subject of dispute—if, indeed, a friendly talk could be called a dispute—in all our married life.
就说到这儿吧，我亲爱的亨利，我以一个男子汉的身份跟你告别。不幸已经来临。不管是什么造成的，它已经来到了。我将迎接它带来的挑战。纳塔莉是受不了穷的。也许我的资产已够用来还债了，不过没人有理由来埋怨我。但是，如果有什么突如其来的事情威胁到了我的声誉，那我就全指望你了。 And now, my dear Henri, I bid you farewell in the spirit of a man.Misfortune has come.No matter what the cause, it is here.I strip to meet it.Poverty and Natalie are two irreconcilable terms.The balance may be close between my assets and my liabilities, but no one shall have cause to complain of me.But, should any unforeseen event occur to imperil my honor, I count on you.
你可以暗地里写信给我，寄到印度加尔各答总督那里。我跟他家关系不错，如果有从欧洲寄给我的信，他家会有人替我代为保存和转交给我的。亲爱的伙计，我希望回来时还能看到昔日的那个德马尔赛——那个藐视一切，却对自己认为的别人高尚庄严的情感欣然接受的男人。你还在巴黎，朋友，但是当你看到这些文字时，我说不定正在高喊着：“去迦太基吧！” Send letters under cover to the Governor of India at Calcutta.I have friendly relations with his family, and some one there will care for all letters that come to me from Europe.Dear friend, I hope to find you the same de Marsay on my return,—the man who scoffs at everything and yet is receptive of the feelings of others when they accord with the grandeur he is conscious of in himself.You stay in Paris, friend; but when you read these words, I shall be crying out, “To Carthage!”
亨利·德马尔赛侯爵致保尔·德马内维尔伯爵： The Marquis Henri de Marsay to Comte Paul de Manerville:
就这样，伯爵先生，你就这样把自己给毁了！大使先生就这样没落了！这些好事都是你干出来的？ So, so, Monsieur le comte, you have made a wreck of it!Monsieur l’ambassadeur has gone to the bottom!Are these the fine things that you were doing?
为什么，保尔，为什么你之前不跟我说？如果你早告诉我只言片语，我可怜的家伙，我早就给你出谋划策了。你妻子拒绝在保证书上署名。但愿你能擦亮你的眼睛看看！不过，如果这还不够的话，听说你的期票无法兑换，因为有个叫勒屈耶的人不同意，他是波尔多的公证人索洛内总管的首席助手。这个初来乍到的放高利贷者是从加斯科涅到巴黎从事投机的，也是你那位可敬的岳母的代理人。真正借给你十万高利贷的债主是你岳母。我还听说实际上她只借给了你七万。跟埃旺热利斯塔夫人比，高布赛克大叔就好比是法兰绒、天鹅绒、香草味的奶油蛋糕、一片促你入睡的安眠药。你名下的玫瑰美人葡萄庄园就要被你妻子占下了。拍卖价格和她用嫁妆做首付之间的差价将由她母亲来垫付。埃旺热利斯塔夫人还将获得居阿代和格拉索尔的领地，你波尔多的房子抵押出去，也已经被她得到了。索洛内找了个傀儡，用其名义买下了那栋房产。 Why, Paul, why have you kept away from me?If you had said a single word, my poor old fellow, I would have made your position plain to you.Your wife has refused me her endorsement.May that one word unseal your eyes!But, if that does not suffice, learn that your notes have been protested at the instigation of a Sieur Lecuyer, formerly head-clerk to Maitre Solonet, a notary in Bordeaux.That usurer in embryo (who came from Gascony for jobbery) is the proxy of your very honorable mother-inlaw, who is the actual holder of your notes for one hundred thousand francs, on which I am told that worthy woman doled out to you only seventy thousand.Compared with Madame Evangelista, papa Gobseck is flannel, velvet, vanilla cream, a sleeping draught.Your vineyard of Belle–Rose is to fall into the clutches of your wife, to whom her mother pays the difference between the price it goes for at the auction sale and the amount of her dower claim upon it.Madame Evangelista will also have the farms at Guadet and Grassol, and the mortgages on your house in Bordeaux already belong to her, in the names of straw men provided by Solonet.
这样一来，这两个聪明的女人从你的不幸和被迫卖出的产业上刮得的利益，加起来每年就要达到十二万法郎了，另外还有这两个狡猾的恶妇已经拥有的登记在总账上每年三万多法郎的收入。 Thus these two excellent women will make for themselves a united income of one hundred and twenty thousand francs a year out of your misfortunes and forced sale of property, added to the revenue of some thirty-odd thousand on the Grand-livre which these cats already possess.
你妻子其实也无需签署保证书了，因为今天早上，我提到过的那位勒屈耶先生来找我，主动提出把我借给你的那笔钱还给我，以此来换取我债权的合法转移。就光你岳母存在朗斯特拉克地窖里的那些1825年的葡萄酒就够还我的债了。 The endorsement of your wife was not needed; for this morning the said Sieur Lecuyer came to offer me a return of the sum I had lent you in exchange for a legal transfer of my rights.The vintage of 1825 which your mother-inlaw keeps in the cellars at Lanstrac will suffice to pay me.
这两个女人明显已经算到你现在已经漂洋过海了，但是我还是请了个信差来送这封信，或许你还有时间按我的计策行动。 These two women have calculated, evidently, that you are now upon the ocean; but I send this letter by courier, so that you may have time to follow the advice I now give you.
我跟那个勒屈耶聊起来过。从他的谎言、他的言语、他的谨慎中，我找到了一些蛛丝马迹，弄明白了她们全家针对你的整个阴谋诡计。今天晚上，我会去西班牙大使馆向你的岳母和妻子大献殷勤。我要完全地迎合埃旺热利斯塔夫人，当着她的面，我要卑鄙无耻地抛弃你，无中生有地诋毁你——但是不能太公开地说，否则那个穿着裙子的马斯卡里尔就会查明我的真实目的。你是怎么和她成为死敌的？我很想知道答案。如果你够聪明，应该先讨好这个女人，然后再迎娶她的女儿。那样也许今天你已经是法兰西贵族院议员、德马内维尔公爵或者是驻马德里大使了。 I made Lecuyer talk.I disentangled from his lies, his language, and his reticence, the threads I lacked to bring to light the whole plot of the domestic conspiracy hatched against you.This evening, at the Spanish embassy, I shall offer my admiring compliments to your mother-inlaw and your wife.I shall pay court to Madame Evangelista; I intend to desert you basely, and say sly things to your discredit,—nothing openly, or that Mascarille in petticoats would detect my purpose.How did you make her such an enemy?That is what I want to know.If you had had the wit to be in love with that woman before you married her daughter, you would today be peer of France, Duc de Manerville, and, possibly, ambassador to Madrid.
如果你结婚的时候，咨询一下我，我会帮你分析和了解这些即将进入你生活的女人。两个人一起观察思考，也许你现在就不会这样了。但当时没有这样，那两个女人看了我之后害怕我，并将我和你分开。如果不是你愚蠢地屈从她们，待我以冷漠，她们是毁不掉你的。是你妻子造成我们之间冷漠的关系，这些都是她母亲教她的。她每周写两封信给她母亲——你却没有注意。我的保尔，当我听到这些细节时马上就明白了。 If you had come to me at the time of your marriage, I would have helped you to analyze and know the women to whom you were binding yourself; out of our mutual observations safety might have been yours.But, instead of that, these women judged me, became afraid of me, and separated us.If you had not stupidly given in to them and turned me the cold shoulder, they would never have been able to ruin you.Your wife brought on the coldness between us, instigated by her mother, to whom she wrote two letters a week,—a fact to which you paid no attention.I recognized my Paul when I heard that detail.
一个月之内我就会和你的岳母打得火热，这样就方便找出她为什么对你——世界上最好，最善良的人——有种西班牙和意大利式的仇恨了！难道在她女儿爱上菲利克斯·德旺德奈斯之前就恨你了，我一直在考虑这个问题。如果不是我心血来潮，和蒙特里沃、龙克洛尔和其他几个你也相识的朋友去东方逛逛，我早就该告诉你这件风流韵事了。这件事在我离开时就已崭露头角了。那时我就看出你灾难即将到来。但是哪个绅士又会卑鄙到不问自答地跟你提及这个话题呢？谁会去损害一个女人的声誉？朋友正暗自欢喜地看着镜子中虚幻的幸福婚姻，谁又忍心去敲碎这面镜子呢？幻想只不过是内心的财富而已。 Within a month I shall be so intimate with your mother-inlaw that I shall hear from her the reasons of the hispano-italiano hatred which she feels for you,—for you, one of the best and kindest men on earth!Did she hate you before her daughter fell in love with Felix de Vandenesse; that’s a question in my mind.If I had not taken a fancy to go to the East with Montriveau, Ronquerolles, and a few other good fellows of your acquaintance, I should have been in a position to tell you something about that affair, which was beginning just as I left Paris.I saw the first gleams even then of your misfortune.But what gentleman is base enough to open such a subject unless appealed to?Who shall dare to injure a woman, or break that illusive mirror in which his friend delights in gazing at the fairy scenes of a happy marriage?Illusions are the riches of the heart.
亲爱的朋友，你的妻子，我相信正如我所说，确切地说是一个追逐时尚的女子。她只想着社交场合和穿着打扮，并且贪图享受。她去戏剧院、歌剧院，出席舞会。她很晚起床，然后坐车去博伊斯，在外面就餐或是在自家大办筵席。在我看来，这样的生活之于女子正如战争之于男人；大众只看到胜利者，却忘记了战场上的炮灰。许多娇嫩的女子处于这种利益冲突中，非得送命不行。幸存下来的都是有着钢铁意志的。她们心狠手辣，野心极大。所以，那些惯于社交场合中的人平时大都冷若冰霜。高尚的人们总是深居简出；软弱娇嫩的人们则会选择屈从；剩下的都是些鹅卵石，在社会上按部就班地生活，任流水冲击，棱角皆无，但不会被磨穿。你的妻子轻轻松松地就能应付这种生活。她似乎天生就是这块料；她总是容光焕发、光彩照人的样子。依我看，结论很简单——她从没爱过你，而你却像个疯子一样地爱她。 Your wife, dear friend, is, I believe I may say, in the fullest application of the word, a fashionable woman.She thinks of nothing but her social success, her dress, her pleasures; she goes to opera and theatre and balls; she rises late and drives to the Bois, dines out, or gives a dinner-party.Such a life seems to me for women very much what war is for men; the public sees only the victors; it forgets the dead.Many delicate women perish in this conflict; those who come out of it have iron constitutions, consequently no heart, but good stomachs.There lies the reason of the cold insensibility of social life.Fine souls keep themselves reserved, weak and tender natures succumb; the rest are cobblestones which hold the social organ in its place, water-worn and rounded by the tide, but never worn-out.Your wife has maintained that life with ease; she looks made for it; she is always fresh and beautiful.To my mind the deduction is plain,—she has never loved you; and you have loved her like a madman.
要使那个硅质的东西爱上别人，那这个男人必须像钢铁般强硬。菲利克斯虽然没有追求到杜德莱夫人，倒也没有继续强求，他倒是很适合纳塔莉。不需要多少法律依据就能看得出来，她对你很冷漠。你深爱着她，但是你却察觉不出一个少妇对你的冷漠。你试着去培养你中意的女子，却使她投向了像旺德奈斯那样的人。即使你感觉到妻子对你冷漠，你也会本着已婚人士的愚蠢原则，将她的冷漠归结与她的保守和纯真。女人们的风流韵事被女人们交耳相传，男人们却不敢提及。在这样的社会，你还像所有的为夫之人一样，认为自己的妻子会坚守妇道。 To strike out love from that siliceous nature a man of iron was needed.After standing, but without enduring, the shock of Lady Dudley, Felix was the fitting mate to Natalie.There is no great merit in divining that to you she was indifferent.In love with her yourself, you have been incapable of perceiving the cold nature of a young woman whom you have fashioned and trained for a man like Vandenesse.The coldness of your wife, if you perceived it, you set down, with the stupid jurisprudence of married people, to the honor of her reserve and her innocence.Like all husbands, you thought you could keep her virtuous in a society where women whisper from ear to ear that which men are afraid to say.
不，你的妻子虽然喜欢婚姻给她带来的社会利益，私下却觉得这负担过重。那些负担，那些赋税就是——你！你对此一无所知，你就是自掘坟墓（用这种平庸的语言说），然后用鲜花把坟墓给盖上了。你像其他普通男子一样，只知道逆来顺受，本来我是想保护你的。亲爱的伙计！凡夫俗子若是被妻子所欺骗也会大吃一惊、盛怒不已的。你跟他们一样愚蠢，你跟我提到你为她所做的牺牲，你对她的爱意，还像唱圣歌一样高唱着：“如果她背叛了我，可就是太忘恩负义了。我为她做了这个，为她做了那个，我还会为她做更多，为了她天涯海角我都愿去，现在要为她去印度了，我——我——”等等。我亲爱的保尔，难道你从没到巴黎住过？难道你拥有亨利·德马尔赛这样的朋友不觉荣幸？难道你连这些最简单不过的事也不知道？难道对于推动女性这种机械运转的基本规律和她们的心思中最简单的常识也不懂？那么请听我说： No, your wife has liked the social benefits she derived from marriage, but the private burdens of it she found rather heavy.Those burdens, that tax was—you!Seeing nothing of all this, you have gone on digging your abysses (to use the hackneyed words of rhetoric) and covering them with flowers.You have mildly obeyed the law which rules the ruck of men; from which I desired to protect you.Dear fellow! only one thing was wanting to make you as dull as the bourgeois deceived by his wife, who is all astonishment or wrath, and that is that you should talk to me of your sacrifices, your love for Natalie, and chant that psalm: “Ungrateful would she be if she betrayed me; I have done this, I have done that, and more will I do; I will go to the ends of the earth, to the Indies for her sake. I—I—” etc.My dear Paul, have you never lived in Paris, have you never had the honor of belonging by ties of friendship to Henri de Marsay, that you should be so ignorant of the commonest things, the primitive principles that move the feminine mechanism, the a-b-c of their hearts?Then hear me:—
葬送掉你自己的小命也好，为了一个女子的欠债进圣佩拉日监狱也好，杀死几十个男人也好，抛弃十几个女人也好，伺候拉班也好，横穿沙漠也好，美名远扬也好，臭名昭著也好，像纳尔逊一样为了亲吻到汉密尔顿的酥肩而拒绝出战也好，像波拿巴一样冲上阿尔科勒桥也好，像罗兰一样为了能和心爱的女子跳上舞而冒上生命危险也好——我亲爱的伙计，所有这一切又和爱情有何相关？如果做这些事情就能赢得爱情，那些男人就太幸福了。逞一时之勇就能让男人得到自己想要的女人。但是，爱情啊爱情，我的好保尔，是一种信仰，就像相信圣母无孕怀胎一样；信则有，不信则无。为了让人对你产生那种心不甘情不愿的、无法解释的感情，波托西的金矿也罢，抛头颅洒热血也罢，或是声名显赫也罢，又有什么用呢？像你这样的年轻人，希望凭着你丰厚的身家而被人爱，这和那些放高利贷的人是一丘之貉。我们的合法妻子应该坚守妇道，为我们生儿育女，但是在爱情上她并不亏欠我们。 Suppose you exterminate yourself, suppose you go to Saint–Pelagie for a woman’s debts, suppose you kill a score of men, desert a dozen women, serve like Laban, cross the deserts, skirt the galleys, cover yourself with glory, cover yourself with shame, refuse, like Nelson, to fight a battle until you have kissed the shoulder of Lady Hamilton, dash yourself, like Bonaparte, upon the bridge at Arcola, go mad like Roland, risk your life to dance five minutes with a woman—my dear fellow, what have all those things to do with love?If love were won by samples such as those mankind would be too happy.A spurt of prowess at the moment of desire would give a man the woman that he wanted.But love, love, my good Paul, is a faith like that in the Immaculate conception of the Holy Virgin; it comes, or it does not come.Will the mines of Potosi, or the shedding of our blood, or the making of our fame serve to waken an involuntary, an inexplicable sentiment?Young men like you, who expect to be loved as the balance of your account, are nothing else than usurers.Our legitimate wives owe us virtue and children, but they don’t owe us love.
我亲爱的保尔，爱情是要去感受给予和收获的快乐，是确信能够给予和收获这种快乐；爱情是一种欲望，不断地变化和成长，不断地得到满足，同时又永远不会心满意足。你从没拨动过你妻子心中那根叫做欲望的琴弦，现在到了旺德奈斯拨动那根琴弦的那天了。你的一厢情愿、你的礼物、你为她的所作所为、你的金钱甚至在她脑海中不留一丝痕迹。你对她的激情并没有换来她对你的爱意，你的激情在她看来只是一堆破铜烂铁而已。现在菲利克斯坐拥美人在怀。你被你自己的爱情蒙蔽了双眼，看不到她根本不爱你。 Love, my dear Paul, is the sense of pleasure given and received, and the certainty of giving and receiving it; love is a desire incessantly moving and growing, incessantly satisfied and insatiable.The day when Vandenesse stirred the cord of a desire in your wife’s heart which you had left untouched, all your self-satisfied affection, your gifts, your deeds, your money, ceased to be even memories; one emotion of love in your wife’s heart has cast out the treasures of your own passion, which are now nothing better than old iron.Felix has the virtues and the beauties in her eyes, and the simple moral is that blinded by your own love you never made her love you.
你的岳母和她女儿的情人是同一条战线上的，要与她女儿的丈夫做对。她秘密地或公开地、睁一只眼闭一只眼地视而不见。我不知道她究竟做了些什么——但是有一件事是确定的，她支持她的女儿，与你则是势不两立。根据我过去十五年对社交界的观察，还从没见过母亲在这种形式下会抛弃自己女儿的。这种豁达大度是女性代代相传的遗产。哪个男人又会去谴责这个呢？也许只有那些法规的制定者才只看条例而不看感情。 Your mother-inlaw is on the side of the lover against the husband,—secretly or not; she may have closed her eyes, or she may have opened them; I know not what she has done—but one thing is certain, she is for her daughter, and against you.During the fifteen years that I have observed society, I have never yet seen a mother who, under such circumstances, abandons her daughter.This indulgence seems to be an inheritance transmitted in the female line.What man can blame it?Some copyist of the Civil code, perhaps, who sees formulas only in the place of feelings.
再来说说你今天的局面：一个追求时尚的女人让你陷入了大肆挥霍的生活，你本性又好说话，再加上你的虚荣，正好让你的妻子和她的母亲步步设局，让你倾家荡产，好早日摆脱你。从这一切当中，我的好朋友，你应该看得出，你托付给我的任务必定是无用且无效的，虽然我本可以非常忠诚地替你完成，因为我觉得这使命很有意思。你希望我去阻止的灾祸已经来到了——“木已成舟”。 As for your present position, the dissipation into which the life of a fashionable woman cast you, and your own easy nature, possibly your vanity, have opened the way for your wife and her mother to get rid of you by this ruin so skilfully contrived.From all of which you will conclude, my good friend, that the mission you entrusted to me, and which I would all the more faithfully fulfil because it amused me, is, necessarily, null and void.The evil you wish me to prevent is accomplished,—“consummatum est.”
原谅我，亲爱的朋友，如你所说，我以所谓的德马尔赛的名义写信给你，告诉你这件非常严重的事情。我决不会像遗产继承人围着先人的坟墓跳舞那样，围着朋友的坟墓跳舞。但是，你写信跟我说，你要做个男子汉。我相信你，我把你当作一个胸怀天下的人，而不是一个陷入情网的人。对于你来说，这个打击就像囚犯的肩膀上被烙下一个印记，将使他永远彻底地反抗这个社会。你现在终于从这种苦难中超脱出来了。以前是婚姻控制你，现在应该是你控制婚姻的时候了。 Forgive me, dear friend, if I write to you, as you say, a la de Marsay on subjects which must seem to you very serious.Far be it from me to dance upon the grave of a friend, like heirs upon that of a progenitor.But you have written to me that you mean to act the part of a man, and I believe you; I therefore treat you as a man of the world, and not as a lover.For you, this blow ought to be like the brand on the shoulder of a galley-slave, which flings him forever into a life of systematic opposition to society.You are now freed of one evil; marriage possessed you; it now behooves you to turn round and possess marriage.
保尔，我是你真正意义上的挚友。如果在你结实的脑壳里面有智慧，如果你有充沛的精力，可惜你现在的精力已经来得太晚了，我早就推心置腹地跟你讲了，以此证明我们之间的友谊。这样你本可以像踩在地毯上一样，超脱于人性之上。可是，当我叫你要提防巴黎的文化，当我假借小说的形式向你描述我青年时代的真实经历时，你只把这些当作一段浪漫的历程，而不曾领会其真正的含义。我跟你讲过一个像你一样坠入情网的律师的故事，他深爱妻子就和你一样，为她伪造文件，并非法得到了三万法郎。东窗事发后，他妻子宣布与他脱离关系，并称有自由去爱另外的男人。当时我们正在吃晚饭，你和另外几个傻瓜听完后，大嚷着不同意我所说的话。好啦，我亲爱的保尔，你就像那个律师。 Paul, I am your friend in the fullest acceptation of the word.If you had a brain in an iron skull, if you had the energy which has come to you too late, I would have proved my friendship by telling you things that would have made you walk upon humanity as upon a carpet.But when I did talk to you guardedly of Parisian civilization, when I told you in the disguise of fiction some of the actual adventures of my youth, you regarded them as mere romance and would not see their bearing.When I told you that history of a lawyer at the galleys branded for forgery, who committed the crime to give his wife, adored like yours, an income of thirty thousand francs, and whom his wife denounced that she might be rid of him and free to love another man, you exclaimed, and other fools who were supping with us exclaimed against me.Well, my dear Paul, you were that lawyer.
你这里的友人们不会原谅你的。旺德奈斯兄弟的妹妹利斯托迈尔侯爵夫人和她的那伙人——小拉斯蒂涅这个混蛋也加入了他们——德哀格勒蒙特夫人和她那伙人、勒农家、费罗伯爵夫人、埃斯巴夫人、纽泌根家、西班牙大使，总之，大家都被人挑拨起来，往你身上泼污水。他们说你是个混球、一个赌徒、一个大肆挥霍的败家子。他们又说你的妻子是品高尚德的天使，已经为你还过很多次债了，虽然现在财产已与你分离，刚刚又替你兑现了十万法郎的汇票。幸运的是你终于干对了一件事，那就是消失。如果你还继续留在这里，你都要穷得让你妻子睡稻草了，这个可怜的女子便成了恪守夫妻忠心的牺牲者！ Your friends here are not sparing you.The sister of the two Vandenesses, the Marquise de Listomere and all her set, in which, by the bye, that little Rastignac has enrolled himself,—the scamp will make his way!—Madame d’Aiglemont and her salon, the Lenoncourts, the Comtesse Ferraud, Madame d’Espard, the Nucingens, the Spanish ambassador, in short, all the cliques in society are flinging mud upon you.You are a bad man, a gambler, a dissipated fellow who has squandered his property.After paying your debts a great many times, your wife, an angel of virtue, has just redeemed your notes for one hundred thousand francs, although her property was separate from yours.Luckily, you had done the best you could do by disappearing.If you had stayed here you would have made her bed in the straw; the poor woman would have been the victim of her conjugal devotion!
我亲爱的保尔，当一个男子大权在握的时候，墓志铭上刻的那些美德他都拥有；一旦他穷困潦倒了，他的罪行就罄竹难书；现在大家都说你的恶性堪比唐璜。他们传言说你到证劵交易所投机，你放荡不羁，并为满足你这种低级趣味而耗费了大笔的钱财；你的很多钱都用来支付高利贷的利息了。旺德奈斯兄弟到处宣扬，吉格涅特以六千法郎的价格卖给你了一个象牙雕质的战舰，然后从你贴身仆从那儿以三百法郎的价格买回，之后再倒卖给你。这件事本来是九年前发生在马克西姆·德特拉伊身上的，但是在目前这种情况下似乎是更适合你不过，于是马克西姆永远失去了对他战舰的指挥权。 When a man attains to power, my dear Paul, he has all the virtues of an epitaph; let him fall into poverty, and he has more sins than the Prodigal Son; society at the present moment gives you the vices of a Don Juan.You gambled at the Bourse, you had licentious tastes which cost you fabulous sums of money to gratify; you paid enormous interests to money-lenders.The two Vandenesses have told everywhere how Gigonnet gave you for six thousand francs an ivory frigate, and made your valet buy it back for three hundred in order to sell it to you again.The incident did really happen to Maxime de Trailles about nine years ago; but it fits your present circumstances so well that Maxime has forever lost the command of his frigate.
反正这些流言蜚语我一时也无法全部告诉你。你为流言蜚语提供了大百科全书一样的素材，女人们又不断地添油加醋，加以传播。你的妻子却因此出尽风头。昨晚在歌剧院，菲尔曼尼夫人又开始向我重复那些道听途说的故事。“不要再说了，”我答道，“你们对事实的真相根本一无所知。保尔抢劫了银行，骗了国库的钱，谋杀了伊丝林和三名圣丹尼斯街的梅朵拉人，而且私下跟你说，我觉得他还是迪克斯—米粒土匪群里的人。他的同伙是著名的雅克·科林，自从科林从苦役监狱逃出去以后，警察就一直抓不到他。保尔让他住在自己的房子里，你知道他什么都干得出来的。实际上，这两个人已经去印度打劫伟大的莫卧儿人了。”菲尔曼尼夫人听完我的话以后终于明白，作为一个有身份的女子，一些道听途说的小道消息不应该从她那小巧漂亮的嘴里吐出来。 In short, I can’t tell you one-half that is said; you have supplied a whole encyclopaedia of gossip which the women have an interest in swelling.Your wife is having an immense success.Last evening at the opera Madame Firmiani began to repeat to me some of the things that are being said.“Don’t talk of that,” I replied.“You know nothing of the real truth, you people.Paul has robbed the Bank, cheated the Treasury, murdered Ezzelin and three Medoras in the rue Saint–Denis, and I think, between ourselves, that he is a member of the Dix–Mille.His associate is the famous Jacques Collin, on whom the police have been unable to lay a hand since he escaped from the galleys.Paul gave him a room in his house; you see he is capable of anything; in fact, the two have gone off to India together to rob the Great Mogul.”Madame Firmiani, like the distinguished woman that she is, saw that she ought not to convert her beautiful lips into a mouthpiece for false denunciation.
许多人听到这悲喜交杂的人生故事时，也不肯相信。他们相信人性，相信人的美好情感。他们觉着那些流言蜚语都是假的。但是，我亲爱的伙计，塔莱朗说过一句名言：“任何事情都会发生的。”诚然，有些比你的这个家庭阴谋更令人吃惊的事也会在我们眼皮底下发生。但是人们总是否认这些事情会发生，说什么纯属谣言之类的话。这些戏剧般的事实总是表演得那么自然，涂上了一层品味高雅的油彩。我甚至都得擦亮我那用来看歌剧的望远镜的镜片才看得清事实的真相。但是我再对你说一遍，当这个人是我的朋友时，我们曾痛快地畅饮香槟，曾一同在维纳斯·康茂德的祭台下跪请愿，曾手挽着手一起祈祷，如今这个朋友遭陷害了，就算要毁掉几十个家庭，我也要为他讨回公道。 Many persons, when they hear of these tragi-comedies of life, refuse to believe them.They take the side of human nature and fine sentiments; they declare that these things do not exist.But Talleyrand said a fine thing, my dear fellow: “All things happen.”Truly, things happen under our very noses which are more amazing than this domestic plot of yours; but society has an interest in denying them, and in declaring itself calumniated.Often these dramas are played so naturally and with such a varnish of good taste that even I have to rub the lens of my opera-glass to see to the bottom of them.But, I repeat to you, when a man is a friend of mine, when we have received together the baptism of champagne and have knelt together before the altar of the Venus Commodus, when the crooked fingers of play have given us their benediction, if that man finds himself in a false position I’d ruin a score of families to do him justice.
从这一切中，你应该看得出我是爱你的。我以前写过这么长的信给你吗？没有。所以我下面要告诉你的话，你一定要认真听好啦。哎！保尔，我得练好我的字，因为我要从政啦。我要进入公众视野了。我打算在五年之内，当上内阁大臣或某个使馆的大使。男人到了某个年龄段，他唯一的情妇就是他的国家。我已经加入一个圈子，这个圈内的人计划推翻现内阁，甚至要推翻政府现在的所有制度。总之，我跟随着一位瘸了一条腿的亲王——我认为他是一位天赋极高的政治家，他的名字将永留史册；一位无所不能的亲王就像一个艺术家在自己的领域无所不能一样。 You must be aware from all this that I love you.Have I ever in my life written a letter as long as this?No.Therefore, read with attention what I still have to say.Alas! Paul, I shall be forced to take to writing, for I am taking to politics.I am going into public life.I intend to have, within five years, the portfolio of a ministry or some embassy.There comes an age when the only mistress a man can serve is his country.I enter the ranks of those who intend to upset not only the ministry, but the whole present system of government.In short, I swim in the waters of a certain prince who is lame of the foot only,—a man whom I regard as a statesman of genius whose name will go down to posterity; a prince as complete in his way as a great artist may be in his.
我们这一伙人中几个人：龙克罗尔、蒙特里沃、葛朗利厄家、拉罗什—于贡、赛里奇、费罗和格朗维尔，我们结盟反抗“立宪党”，因为这个所谓的立宪党是以《宪法报》为阵营的。我们要推翻纳瓦兰、朗热家族、旺德奈斯家族和大主教。为了取得胜利，我们甚至与拉法伊特家族、奥尔良人和左翼分子联合起来——当然这些人在胜利的前夕就得干掉。因为按他们的原则，在这个世界上就不可能有政府。为了我们的国家——和我们自己，我们什么事情都能做到。 Several of us, Ronquerolles, Montriveau, the Grandlieus, La Roche–Hugon, Serisy, Feraud, and Granville, have allied ourselves against the “parti-pretre,” as the party-ninny represented by the “Constitutionnel” has ingeniously said.We intend to overturn the Navarreins, Lenoncourts, Vandenesses, and the Grand Almonry.In order to succeed we shall even ally ourselves with Lafayette, the Orleanists, and the Left,—people whom we can throttle on the morrow of victory, for no government in the world is possible with their principles.We are capable of anything for the good of the country—and our own.
关于国王的私人问题，如今已经成了感情方面的蠢事，必须把他们清除掉。从这方面来看，英国的总督制比我们的制度更先进。政治与此事不相关，我的兄弟。政治在于通过创造一个寡头集团来给国家以推动力。这个集团要掌握政府的思想，领导公众走上一条光明的大路，而不是把这个国家弄得四分五裂。在过去的四十年里，我们美丽的法兰西就在经历这种分裂，这明智而又幼稚的法兰西，这疯狂而又温柔的法兰西，它的确需要一套体制，而不是仅仅是一些领导人。在这个重大的问题上，人又有什么用呢？如果目的是伟大的，如果法兰西人能幸福的生活，免遭灾难，我们赚点钱，积累点财产，享有些特权，享受些快乐，民众又怎么会介意呢？ Personal questions as to the King’s person are mere sentimental folly in these days; they must be cleared away.From that point of view, the English with their sort of Doge, are more advanced than we are.Politics have nothing to do with that, my dear fellow.Politics consist in giving the nation an impetus by creating an oligarchy embodying a fixed theory of government, and able to direct public affairs along a straight path, instead of allowing the country to be pulled in a thousand different directions, which is what has been happening for the last forty years in our beautiful France—at once so intelligent and so sottish, so wise and so foolish; it needs a system, indeed, much more than men.What are individuals in this great question?If the end is a great one, if the country may live happy and free from trouble, what do the masses care for the profits of our stewardship, our fortune, privileges, and pleasures?
我非常坚定我的立场。目前我有十五万法郎的百分之三的公债，还存有二十万法郎的积蓄以备不时之需。这点钱放在口袋里，对于一个开始攀爬权力阶梯的人来说算不了很多。 I am now standing firm on my feet.I have at the present moment a hundred and fifty thousand francs a year in the Three per Cents, and a reserve of two hundred thousand francs to repair damages.Even this does not seem to me very much ballast in the pocket of a man starting left foot foremost to scale the heights of power.
其实，从政对我来说只是一种机遇，以前我并不是很中意这一职业，你知道我一直向往东方的生活方式。我那位可敬的母亲在沉睡了三十五年后，一觉醒来发觉她原来还有个儿子能光耀门楣。一根葡萄被连根拔起，几年以后一些根又常常会出现在地面上，这种事经常发生。我亲爱的小伙子，我母亲也早已把我从她心里连根拔掉，如今我又在她脑海中生根发芽了。她已经五十八了，她认为生活中没有什么男人能比她自己的儿子更重要。在这个节骨眼上，她在泡温泉的时候遇上了一位快乐的老处女——英国人，每年有二十四万法郎的收入。作为一位好母亲，她出于狂妄的野心鼓励这个女子做我的妻子。一个三十有六的女人，我的天啊！从小生长在严厉的清教徒环境中，就像一个长期蹲守窝中的老母鸡，她还坚持认为不忠于丈夫的妻子应该被当众烧死。“那我们到哪儿去找足够的木头来烧呢？”我问她。我真想叫她走远点儿，区区每年二十四万法郎根本抵不上我的自由，我身心的代价，也抵不上我的未来前程。但她是一个患了痛风症的老头的唯一继承人，这个老头是个酿酒商，已到弥留之际，将留给她一笔财产，数目至少和这个甜心已经拥有的财富相当。除了这些优点以外，她有这红色的鼻子，死山羊一样的眼睛。她的腰使人觉得要是她不慎摔一跤会不会碎成三段。他看上去就像一个上色糟糕的洋娃娃。不过她为人勤俭，知道疼爱丈夫，丈夫叫干什么就会去干什么。她还有英国人的才干，会打理好我的房子，我的马厩，我的仆人，我的土地，肯定比任何管家干得都要好。她有妇道的尊严，腰身挺直，就像法兰西剧院那舞台上的主角一样。我总觉得她好像那受过尖桩酷刑的人，而且尖桩折断了，留在了她的身体里。不过，斯特旺小姐长得还算白净，如果我非得娶她为妻，也不会太叫人难过。但是——真正令人难受的是——她有一双双品行端正的女子的手，像神圣无暇的、装着圣经的柜子一样。那双手长得如此之红，我还想不到怎样不花太多的钱去把它们漂白。我也不知道怎样把她那跟香肠一般粗的手指变细。是的，她显然通过她那双手与酿酒商连在一起，通过金钱与贵族连子了一起。和那些富裕的英国女人一样，她想让别人把她误看成贵族妇女，于是过分做作，却露出了蛛丝马迹。 A fortunate accident settled the question of my setting out on this career, which did not particularly smile on me, for you know my predilection for the life of the East.After thirty-five years of slumber, my highly-respected mother woke up to the recollection that she had a son who might do her honor.Often when a vine-stock is eradicated, some years after shoots come up to the surface of the ground; well, my dear boy, my mother had almost torn me up by the roots from her heart, and I sprouted again in her head.At the age of fifty-eight, she thinks herself old enough to think no more of any men but her son.At this juncture she has met in some hot-water cauldron, at I know not what baths, a delightful old maid—English, with two hundred and forty thousand francs a year; and, like a good mother, she has inspired her with an audacious ambition to become my wife.A maid of six-and-thirty, my word!Brought up in the strictest puritanical principles, a steady sitting hen, who maintains that unfaithful wives should be publicly burnt.‘Where will you find wood enough?’ I asked her.I could have sent her to the devil, for two hundred and forty thousand francs a year are no equivalent for liberty, nor a fair price for my physical and moral worth and my prospects.But she is the sole heiress of a gouty old fellow, some London brewer, who within a calculable time will leave her a fortune equal at least to what the sweet creature has already.Added to these advantages, she has a red nose, the eyes of a dead goat, a waist that makes one fear lest she should break into three pieces if she falls down, and the coloring of a badly painted doll.But—she is delightfully economical; but—she will adore her husband, do what he will; but—she has the English gift; she will manage my house, my stables, my servants, my estates better than any steward.She has all the dignity of virtue; she holds herself as erect as a confidante on the stage of the Francais; nothing will persuade me that she has not been impaled and the shaft broken off in her body.Miss Stevens is, however, fair enough to be not too unpleasing if I must positively marry her.But—and this to me is truly pathetic—she has the hands of a woman as immaculate as the sacred ark; they are so red that I have not yet hit on any way to whiten them that will not be too costly, and I have no idea how to fine down her fingers, which are like sausages.Yes; she evidently belongs to the brew-house by her hands, and to the aristocracy by her money; but she is apt to affect the great lady a little too much, as rich English women do who want to be mistaken for them, and she displays her lobster’s claws too freely.
不过她不够聪明，这点倒符合我对女人的希望。如果还有女人比她还笨，我马上就会去找出来的。这个女子的名字叫蒂娜，她永远不会批评我，不会反驳我。我就是她的上议院、她的贵族院和她的下议院。总之，保尔，她就是英国天才无法否认的证据，她是英国工业巅峰所造出来的产品。无疑，她是在曼彻斯特的佩里制笔间和蒸汽机车工作间生产出来的。这个产品会吃会走，也许会生小孩，还会照顾小孩，将孩子们抚养成人。它像极了女人，可以达到以假乱真的地步。 She has, however, as little intelligence as I could wish in a woman.If there were a stupider one to be found, I would set out to seek her.This girl, whose name is Dinah, will never criticise me; she will never contradict me; I shall be her Upper Chamber, her Lords and Commons.In short, Paul, she is indefeasible evidence of the English genius; she is a product of English mechanics brought to their highest pitch of perfection; she was undoubtedly made at Manchester, between the manufactory of Perry’s pens and the workshops for steam-engines.It eats, it drinks, it walks, it may have children, take good care of them, and bring them up admirably, and it apes a woman so well that you would believe it real.
当我母亲介绍我们认识时，她已经巧妙滴调试好了机器，认真地将铆钉都钉好位了，给齿轮彻底上好了机油，那样运转起来才没有障碍。然后她看到我并无太多不悦的神情，就把弹簧就位，这个女人就开始说话了。最后，我母亲说出了决定性的话来：“蒂娜·斯特旺小姐每年开销不超三万，过去七年东奔西跑就是为了节省开支。”因此她肯定还有一笔钱，而且是银币。 When my mother introduced us, she had set up the machine so cleverly, had so carefully fitted the pegs, and oiled the wheels so thoroughly, that nothing jarred; then, when she saw I did not make a very wry face, she set the springs in motion, and the woman spoke.Finally, my mother uttered the decisive words, “Miss Dinah Stevens spends no more than thirty thousand francs a year, and has been traveling for seven years in order to economize.”—So there is another image, and that one is silver.
事情进展得太快，现在公告都贴出来了。我们现在互相都用“亲爱的心上人”来称呼对方了。这位小姐对我大抛媚眼，搬运工看到了都会被吓倒。一切都已谈妥。无需我的财产，斯特旺小姐用她的一部分财产创建了一份地产的限嗣继承，有二十四万法郎的收入，还购置了一处房产，也纳入限嗣继承财产。她还赠予我一百万法郎。对此，她没什么好抱怨。她叔叔留给她的钱，我分文未动。 Matters are so far advanced that the banns are to be published.We have got as far as “My dear love.”Miss makes eyes at me that might floor a porter.The settlements are prepared.My fortune is not inquired into; Miss Stevens devotes a portion of hers to creating an entail in landed estate, bearing an income of two hundred and forty thousand francs, and to the purchase of a house, likewise entailed.The settlement credited to me is of a million francs.She has nothing to complain of.I leave her uncle’s money untouched.
这位好心的酿酒商，对我的限嗣继承财产也出了一份力，听说他的侄女就要是侯爵夫人了，高兴得不得了。他为我的长子是能做一些贡献的。 The worthy brewer, who has helped to found the entail, was near bursting with joy when he heard that his niece was to be a marquise.He would be capable of doing something handsome for my eldest boy.
一旦资金达到八十万，我就要把钱都投到土地上去。那样，两年之内，我的不动产就有望带来六十万法郎的收入。保尔，你看到了，我给朋友出的主意，我都是身体力行的。 I shall sell out of the funds as soon as they are up to eighty, and invest in land.Thus, in two years I may look to get six hundred thousand francs a year out of real estate.So, you see, Paul, I do not give my friends advice that I am not ready to act upon.
如果你早听我的，你就应该娶一个英国妻子，内伯波的某个女儿，她会给你单身汉的自由。如果你还没结婚的话，我真会把我的未婚妻让给你。不过那也无济于事，我也不是那种叫你沉迷于过去的人。 If you had but listened to me, you would have an English wife, some Nabob’s daughter, who would leave you the freedom of a bachelor.I would concede my future wife to you if you were not married already.But that cannot be helped, and I am not the man to bid you chew the cud of the past.
跟你说这么多是想向你解释我未来的处境，我得小心翼翼地玩这场伟大的掷钱游戏。没有你是不行的，我的朋友。那么我亲爱的保尔，与其扬帆去印度，不如同我一道去塞纳河划船，这样要明智多了。相信我，巴黎仍然是能赚大钱的地方。波托西就在维维安纳街，在和平路，在旺多姆广场，在里沃利街。在其他任何地方或国家，要赚钱就得生产实物，为人跑腿，不断前进或是后退，还得为此汗流浃背。但是在巴黎，你只要有思想就足够了。在这里，所有的人，甚至是资质平平的人，都能在穿上拖鞋时、饭后剔牙时、晚上睡觉或早上起床时发现一座金矿。想到一个馊主意也能赚到钱，还能被大家所理解，在全世界范围内，再找一个这样的地方给我看看。 All this preamble was needful to explain to you that for the future my position in life will be such as a man needs if he wants to play the great game of pitch-and-toss.I cannot do without you, my friend.Now, then, my dear Paul, instead of setting sail for India you would do a much wiser thing to navigate with me the waters of the Seine.Believe me, Paris is still the place where fortune, abundant fortune, can be won.Potosi is in the rue Vivienne, the rue de la Paix, the Place Vendome, the rue de Rivoli.In all other places and countries material works and labors, marches and counter-marches, and sweatings of the brow are necessary to the building up of fortune; but in Paris thought suffices.Here, every man even mentally mediocre, can see a mine of wealth as he puts on his slippers, or picks his teeth after dinner, in his down-sitting and his up-rising.Find me another place on the globe where a good round stupid idea brings in more money, or is sooner understood than it is here.
如果我能爬到梯子的顶端，我会是那种不肯拉你一把，不肯帮你说句话，不肯替你签字担保的人吗？我们这些贪图享受的年轻人需要一个可以信赖的、忠诚的朋友，叫他当替罪羔羊，或者像舍命救帅的士兵一样叫他去死。没有一个有荣誉感的、可以无所不谈的心腹，我们是从不了政的。 If I reach the top of the ladder, as I shall, am I the man to refuse you a helping hand, an influence, a signature?We shall want, we young roues, a faithful friend on whom to count, if only to compromise him and make him a scape-goat, or send him to die like a common soldier to save his general.Government is impossible without a man of honor at one’s side, in whom to confide and with whom we can do and say everything.
我在此向你建议：别登上“艾米丽美人号”，迅速地赶回这里。我将安排你和旺德奈斯决斗，决斗中你先开枪，像射击一只鸽子一样把他放倒。在法国，丈夫如果打死妻子的情妇，马上就会得到人们的尊重。没有人会瞧不起他。我亲爱的兄弟，恐惧是一种可贵的社会因素。对于那种习惯了在别人面前低三下四的人，恐惧是成功的手段。我向来不是很在乎生死，也从没有过恐惧感，但是我注意到这种情感对我们的当代风俗产生了一些奇怪的效果。一些人沉迷于享乐，生怕失去这种享乐，而有些人则极度害怕失去一个女人。以前那种像丢掉一件衣服似的孤注一掷的冒险精神，如今已经不复存在了。现在许多人的勇敢只不过是针对对手的恐惧进行的一些巧妙算计。整个欧洲，只有波兰人为了取乐而打仗，他们培养艺术精神纯粹是为了艺术，而不是为了投机。 Here is what I propose.Let the “Belle–Amelie” sail without you; come back here like a thunderbolt; I’ll arrange a duel for you with Vandenesse in which you shall have the first shot, and you can wing him like a pigeon.In France the husband who shoots his rival becomes at once respectable and respected.No one ever cavils at him again.Fear, my dear fellow, is a valuable social element, a means of success for those who lower their eyes before the gaze of no man living.I who care as little to live as to drink a glass of milk, and who have never felt the emotion of fear, I have remarked the strange effects produced by that sentiment upon our modern manners.Some men tremble to lose the enjoyments to which they are attached, others dread to leave a woman.The old adventurous habits of other days when life was flung away like a garment exist no longer.The bravery of a great many men is nothing more than a clever calculation on the fear of their adversary.The Poles are the only men in Europe who fight for the pleasure of fighting; they cultivate the art for the art’s sake, and not for speculation.
现在听我说：杀了旺德奈斯，你的妻子将为此而颤抖，你的岳母将为此而颤抖，大家都将为此而颤抖，你也就恢复了你的身份地位，证明了你对妻子那伟大的激情。你就征服了大众，征服了你的妻子，你将成为一个英雄。这就是法国。你经济上的窘境，我已经用十万法郎打点好了。你可以先还清你的主要债务，把你的土地典当成现钱，因为你马上将取得一个职位，让你能偿还债主的钱。那么，对于你的妻子，只要你摸透了她的性格，你就能制服她。你爱她的时候，你无法管制她。一旦你不再爱她，你将拥有不可征服的力量。我的任务就是要让你的岳母变得像手套那样顺手。这两个女人从你那里弄走了每年十五万法郎的收入，你得重新夺回来。 Now hear me: kill Vandenesse, and your wife trembles, your mother-inlaw trembles, the public trembles, and you recover your position, you prove your grand passion for your wife, you subdue society, you subdue your wife, you become a hero.Such is France.As for your embarrassments, I hold a hundred thousand francs for you; you can pay your principal debts, and sell what property you have left with a power of redemption, for you will soon obtain an office which will enable you by degrees to pay off your creditors.Then, as for your wife, once enlightened as to her character you can rule her.When you loved her you had no power to manage her; not loving her, you will have an unconquerable force.I will undertake, myself, to make your mother-inlaw as supple as a glove; for you must recover the use of the hundred and fifty thousand francs a year those two women have squeezed out of you.
所以，我说，放弃你那自我放逐的计划，这个计划以我来看无异于用枪顶着自己的脑门。这样一走了之，就更加印证了那些流言蜚语。赌徒离开赌桌去凑钱，即使凑齐了回来也是要血本无归的。我们的金子必须揣在自己的口袋里。你跟着我，我们到政治的大舞台上去赌一把，我们之间的账务是清清楚楚的。所以，坐上驿站的马匹赶快回来，重新玩过这场游戏吧。有亨利·德马尔赛作你的搭档，你一定会赢的，因为亨利·德马尔赛知道怎样出谋划策，怎样一击制胜。 Therefore, I say, renounce this expatriation which seems to me no better than a pistol to your head.To go away is to justify all calumnies.The gambler who leaves the table to get his money loses it when he returns; we must have our gold in our pockets.Let us now, you and I, be two gamblers on the green baize of politics; between us loans are in order.Therefore take post-horses, come back instantly, and renew the game.You’ll win it with Henri de Marsay for your partner, for Henri de Marsay knows how to will, and how to strike.
你要搞清楚我们的政治立场。我的父亲在英国内阁任职；通过埃旺热利斯塔家，我们将和西班牙结成亲密关系，因为你岳母一旦和我交手一番后会发现，和魔鬼作对是没有好处的。蒙特里沃已是少将军衔；不久以后，他肯定会当上国防部长，他雄辩的口才也会帮助他自己在议会更上一层楼。龙克洛尔将成为国务大臣和智囊团成员；马歇尔·德拉罗什·于贡已经是驻德大使和法兰西贵族院议员；赛里奇掌管着行政院，他也是行政院中不可或缺的角色；格朗维尔掌管司法部，他的两个儿子也供职司法部门；葛朗利厄在宫廷中也是位高权重；费罗是贡德维尔派系的领军人物——这些工于心计的阴谋家一直大权在握，我也不知道原因何在。有这些人的支持，我们还有什么好怕的？只要这个巨大的财富的车轮为我们而转动，钱财根本算不上什么问题。你又不是什么背着书包的学生——女人算得上什么？我亲爱的兄弟，如果你让一个女人成为你生活的全部，那么生活会成为什么样子？没有舵的船，你是操控不了的，但是一艘没有罗盘的船，将随风漂流。哼！我亲爱的保尔，社会炼金术的秘诀在于充分利用我们经过的每一个年龄段，抓住春天的花蕾、夏天的花朵和秋天的果实。我和另外几个好心的家伙，这十多年来我们像三个火枪手一样——红队、黑队和灰队——尽情享乐。我们真是为所欲为，有时甚至干点儿打家劫舍之类的勾当。如今，时间和阅历已经催熟了李子，我们所要做的就是用力摇下这些成熟了的李子。跟我们一伙吧，你也可以从我们锅里分一杯羹。 See how we stand politically.My father is in the British ministry; we shall have close relations with Spain through the Evangelistas, for, as soon as your mother-inlaw and I have measured claws she will find there is nothing to gain by fighting the devil.Montriveau is our lieutenant-general; he will certainly be minister of war before long, and his eloquence will give him great ascendancy in the Chamber.Ronquerolles will be minister of State and privy-councillor; Martial de la Roche–Hugon is minister to Germany and peer of France; Serisy leads the Council of State, to which he is indispensable; Granville holds the magistracy, to which his sons belong; the Grandlieus stand well at court; Ferraud is the soul of the Gondreville coterie,—low intriguers who are always on the surface of things, I’m sure I don’t know why.Thus supported, what have we to fear?The money question is a mere nothing when this great wheel of fortune rolls for us.What is a woman?—you are not a schoolboy.What is life, my dear fellow, if you let a woman be the whole of it?A boat you can’t command, without a rudder, but not without a magnet, and tossed by every wind that blows.Pah!The great secret of social alchemy, my dear Paul, is to get the most we can out of each age of life through which we pass; to have and to hold the buds of our spring, the flowers of our summer, the fruits of our autumn.We amused ourselves once, a few good fellows and I, for a dozen or more years, like mousquetaires, black, red, and gray; we denied ourselves nothing, not even an occasional filibustering here and there.Now we are going to shake down the plums which age and experience have ripened.Be one of us; you shall have your share in the pudding we are going to cook.
来吧，亨利·德马尔赛将成为你真正的朋友。 Come; you will find a friend all yours in the skin of H. de Marsay.
保尔·德马内维尔看完这一封信后，心中的希望大厦、幻想大厦和爱情大厦瞬间都就被击垮了。这时，他乘坐的这条从法国出发的船已经驶过了亚速尔群岛。一股冰冷又无力的愤怒袭向了他，他被这种愤怒吞没了。 As Paul de Manerville ended the reading of this letter, which fell like the blows of a pickaxe on the edifice of his hopes, his illusions, and his love, the vessel which bore him from France was beyond the Azores.In the midst of this utter devastation a cold and impotent anger laid hold of him.
“我对他们到底做了什么？”他自问道。 “What had I done to them?” he said to himself.
那是傻瓜、无能之辈才会提的一个问题。他什么都看不到，也预测不到任何事态的发展。然后，他向自己忠心的朋友大喊道：“亨利！亨利！” That is the question of fools, of feeble beings, who, seeing nothing, can nothing foresee.Then he cried aloud: “Henri! Henri!” to his loyal friend.
许多人遇到这种事都会疯掉的，保尔却倒头就睡，那种大灾大难之后的熟睡——拿破仑在兵败滑铁卢之后也是这样倒头就睡的。 Many a man would have gone mad; Paul went to bed and slept that heavy sleep which follows immense disasters,—the sleep that seized Napoleon after Waterloo.
